O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l'emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.
Oh you, very dear son, I have completed this book for you, which is the last of the science of medicine together with its fulfillment, and I have made the end through its expositions and its declarations.
Et m'est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l'uevre de mains, c'est a savoir «cyrurgie».
And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l'uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n'est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.
And because the work of hands is withdrawn in our region and is entirely strange, the science has perished and been cut up, and nothing remains of it except the small descriptions in books of the ancients that hands have changed.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.
And from this has come error and vanity, and the intentions are closed and the science is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l'ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d'exposition et de declaration et de l'abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l'uevre avec l'ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.
Now it seems to me that I want to revive it together with the organization of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come together with the forms of cautery irons, and other instruments of the work with the addition of the declaration and preparation of it, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n'est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.
And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is distant.
Et covient celui qui s'en entremet sormonter en la science d'anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu'il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d'aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d'ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.
And it is fitting for one who undertakes it to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so much that he knows the judgment of the limbs, and their forms and connections and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and arms and their number, and the movement and of the moving and resting veins, and of the place of their exit.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l'uevre est poc; et meismement en l'art de main.
And for this Hippocrates says that the name with the name is much, and with the work is little; and especially in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l'introite de cest livre que qui n'est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu'il ne chiece en error et qu'il n'ocie les homes; ensi que j'ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s'entremettent de ceste science et si s'abandonent sen science et sens experiment.
We tell you in the introduction of this book that who is not knowing of the things said before, let him beware that he does not fall into error and that he does not kill men; thus I have seen many times several of those who undertake this science and abandon themselves without science and without experiment.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d'une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.
For I saw a foolish doctor who cut an abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries of the neck; for which so much blood came out that the woman fell dead between his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d'un home d'eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.
And I saw another doctor who extracted a stone from an aged man, and the stone was large; so it carried with it a piece of the bladder, and the man was dead within 3 days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s'on lou tailloit il en morroit.
And I had already been called to extract it, and saw the disposition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well if one cut it he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d'ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu'il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.
And I saw another doctor who took into care a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break had a wound; and the doctor full of ignorance tightened the break over the wound with splints by strong binding, and did not leave any breathing room for the wound, and left it thus for a term; and commanded him not to unbind it; and it remained thus that the leg was all swollen and the foot and came to perdition.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l'oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.
I was called to come to him, and I hastened to come unbind the leg; and when I had unbound it so it was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d'aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.
But all the way the corruption was already confirmed in the limb, and I could not heal it; and the corruption did not cease to go through the limb until the limb was entirely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.
And I saw another doctor who broke open a cancerous abscess, and then inflamed it through the malice of his lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d'umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu'on il touche de fer s'il n'est en teil leu c'on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.
For cancer, when it is pure of melancholic humor, it is not fitting that one touches it with iron if it is not in such a place that one can remove all that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c'est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.
And for this, very dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into 2 divisions: that is to say, work where there is peril in several dispositions; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and peril.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos
For which it is necessary that you guard yourself, so that the foolish doctors cannot speak ill of you

Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l'autre de gloire.
So take your weapons in care, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and are praised; and leave the frightening diseases of grievous health; and remove your weapons from that which makes you doubt, and have faith in you so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.

Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»
Galen says in some of his admonitions: "Do not take into care bad disease, lest you be called a foolish doctor."

J'ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.
I have divided this treatise according to 3 chapters.

Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l'ueuvre.
The first chapter is about fire cauteries and sharp medicine cauteries, and the chapter is ordered from the head to the feet; and about the forms of instruments, and cautery irons, and all that is necessary in the work.

Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.
The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and about cupping glasses and wounds, and about extracting arrows, and similar things; and the chapter is ordered and the forms of instruments.

Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc'as piez, et des formes des estrumens.
The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and is ordered from the head to the feet, and about the forms of instruments.

Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l'uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l'aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.
Before we remember the work, it is necessary that I speak of the quality of the aid and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l'aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s'acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.
I say that the quality of the aid, and of the harm, is the longest discourse and subtle science and hidden secrets; and many of the wise spoke of this, and agreed on this; and their words suffice me little, for I fear the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c'est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.
I say that cautery helps universally for all complexions where there is matter, except for two complexions: namely hot complexion without matter, and dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.
In hot and dry complexion with matter, some devised and said that cautery is a great aid; and others said the opposite: that cautery is not worth it for illness that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.
For the nature of fire is hot, and hot illness should not be cured by heat, nor by dryness; and he who says the opposite says that cautery greatly aids hot and dry illness that comes in men's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l'ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.
For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m'acorde a ceste parole.
And I agree with this statement.
Car je l'ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.
For I have found it sometimes through experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s'en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l'a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l'espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n'avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.
And anyway, let no one meddle with it except those who have tested it, and who know through long use the chapter on cauteries, and the diversity of men's complexions, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the occurrences and the space of time; we have no fear of other complexions, especially in cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s'asemblerent et s'acorderent au cautere.
And all the physicians assembled and agreed on cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.
And know, son, that cautery with fire is one of the secrets of cures, and of greater goodness than cautery of burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.
For fire is simple, and does not come out except to the member that is cooked, and does not harm other members if little named.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide
Burning medicines go from member to member in extending, and bring to the member illnesses of grievous healing; and by chance kill the sick.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s'il n'i a superfluiteit.
The fire, for its height and for the goodness of its substance, does not do this, if there is no superfluity.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l'estude que j'ai mis en l'art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m'escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l'uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.
And this I have found for you through experiment and through the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and was on the truth of things; and for this I excuse myself for the length of the speech, for it does not please me that I remove from you the secret that is hidden in fire, and the quality of the work, how it repels the illnesses of bodies, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s'acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.
And know, son, that they agreed on what time cauteries should be made, and chose spring.


dou cautere olivaire
Of the olive-shaped cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c'on fait par la cause d'une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.
This cautery is valuable for moisture and cold on the brain, and there are two that one does for the cause of a disease called "soda", and for the cause of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, and to the ears, and for multitude of dreams and tooth pain and throat pain, and especially for all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis and deafness and apoplexy and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.
The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged by purgative medicine cleansing the head for 3 or 4 nights, according to what the strength and age and habit of the patient can suffer; and then have the patient's head shaved.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d'enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:
And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and put his hands on his chest; after put the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and there where your middle finger comes, mark with ink then heat the cautery which is called "olivare", of which here is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d'encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l'os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l'os si com je lou t'ai dit;
And put it on the place marked with ink, and do descending and tightening your hand little by little while turning; then lift your hand quickly, and look at the place if you see the bone a single little bit; and if you don't see it, then restart the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you;
aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l'oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu'il soit sanez.
after take a little salt, and put in water and wet cotton inside, and put on the place, and leave it 3 days; after put on cotton moistened in butter; and leave on until the burn is removed; after treat the wound with the ointment which is called "tetrapharmacon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s'espurge; et por ce si aide mues.  Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l'os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l'os, et soit curez.
And the ancients said, that the longer the wound remains open, the more it purges; and for this it helps better.  And some of these said that one should leave the cautery so long that part of the bone is burned, and then shave what is burned of the bone, and be cured.
Et dient li autre c'on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c'on abaite de l'os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.
And others say that one should leave the cautery on so long, and push so hard that one lowers the bone as wide as a whorl that women put on their spindles so that the humors come out better; and one should leave the wound open for a long time; after one should treat and solder it.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu'en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.
And these two manners of cauteries do not seem to me to be good at all, except in some men where there is a way of fear; and it seems better to me that I should leave it; for the head is weakened by the continued solutions of nature, as we witness in other members; and even when the patient's head is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is safer and better for me, and I use that work then together with safety.

2
de l'anciainne dolor dou chief
Of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d'espurgement de chief et d'oiles et d'emplastres; et s'on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.
When chronic pain comes to the whole head, and lasts a long time, the patient should use iris and pills that are called "cochie", and purging of the head and oils and plasters; and if one does the cautery that we have mentioned before, and it is not effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu'il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.
Take care if the patient's head is of strong nature, and that it is not too cold; then cauterize below that cautery a little that we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc'a l'os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc'a l'os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;
After, make a cautery on each corner of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and make a cautery in the place that is called "vessels"; and it is a place where one puts cupping glasses; and lighten your hand so that you do not go up to the bone: the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in the others, and I will speak of it elsewhere;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c'est li forme:
and it is necessary that the cauteries of the corners be more subtle than those with which one cauterizes the middle of the head, and this is the form:


dou cautere dou chief
On cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc'a l'oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j'ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c'est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.
When sudden pain comes to a part of the head, and the illness extends to the eye, and the head is purged by cleansing medicines, and one has done the other cures that I have mentioned in the division of illnesses, and all this does not help: then make cauterizations in two ways, that is to say with sharp medicine and with iron.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d'alz, et oste l'escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d'alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l'estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d'ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.
The cautery of sharp medicine is that you take a clove of garlic, and remove the skin and cut off a bit at both ends, and then split the temple where the pain is in such a way that you can hide the clove of garlic under the skin; and when it is hidden, tie it and tighten it well and leave it thus for 12 hours; and then untie it and pull out the clove of garlic, and leave the wound thus for 2 or 3 days; then put cotton soaked in butter on it until pus comes out.
Aprés le cure d'oignement tant qu'il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d'aucunes medicines comburans que j'ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.
Afterwards, treat it with ointment until it is healed; and if you want, do this with some burning medicines that I have written about in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:
The iron cautery is done in this manner. Heat the cautery of which this is the form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d'un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l'espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n'arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.
And it is called "nail" because the head is made in the form of a nail where there is a bit of curvature, and in the middle there is a small protrusion; and put it on the painful place, and hold your hand and turn the iron a little lightly, until half the thickness of the skin is burned; and lift your hand so that the artery, which is outside, does not burn, and an abundance of blood flows.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d'oignement tant qu'il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l'artere en ceste emigraine qui n'est mie anciaine.
Afterwards, put cotton in salt water, and put it on the place for 3 days; then put cotton soaked in butter, and then treat the place with ointment until it is healed; and if you want, cauterize this migraine with the cautery that is called "knife-like", with all the point, and be careful not to cut the artery in this migraine which is not old.

de emigraine
On migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu'il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l'estrain que tu ne coper l'artere et que ne viegnes jusc'a l'os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n'ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l'artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s'i conoit, et qui n'est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l'uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.
When you treat migraine as we have said before in the division of illnesses, and it does not help, and you see that the aforementioned cauteries of medicine and iron are not sufficient, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery that is called "knife-like" until it is white; and first mark on the painful place a line half a finger long, and remove your hand once, and tighten it so that you do not cut the artery and that you do not come to the bone; and be careful of the jaw that moves when one eats, and the nerve that moves it and that spasm does not come to the patient, and be careful of the flow of blood from the artery when it will be cut, or cutting has great fear especially for one who does not know it, and who is not studied and experienced; and leave the work in the middle of the way; but I will tell you how to stop blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you the place where it belongs in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu'elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l'estraction de l'artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.
And if you see that this cautery is not sufficient for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize the middle of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you want, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.

de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor
On ear pain due to cold
Quant en l'oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:
When pain from cold comes to the ear, and one has worked with dissolving medicines and other cures that we have mentioned in the division, and the pain does not move, then heat this cautery which is called "points", of which this is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l'oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t'esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l'oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d'enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu'il soit sanez.
Afterwards, make points all around the sick ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and move away a little from the root of the ear after you have marked the place with ink; and have 10 points around each ear; afterwards treat the place until it is healed.

de la torture de la bouche
On the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.
Torture that must be cured by cautery is only for those that come from phlegm, as we have said in the division of illnesses; and do not make any cautery on the appearances that come from dryness and spasm of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d'ydres et d'espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .ij. cauteres: l'une en la racine de l'oreille, et l'autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l'ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l'oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c'est li forme dou cautere:
When you treat this appearance of torture that comes from phlegm of dropsy and purging of the head and gargling, and this is not effective, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient with 3 cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and the other a little outside the temple, and the third at the joining of the two lips; and put the cautery on the part that appears healthy, and make a cautery right at the head of the ear above a little below the corner of the head, and another on the temple as long as a thumb; and leave the cautery on until half of the skin is burned; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j'ai devant dit, tant qu'il soit sanez.
And it is the appearance of the knife-like cautery that we have put before, but it is a little more subtle and it is necessary that the blade be a little thicker; afterwards treat the place as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n'ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l'estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.
When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and it does not help, and the patient does not have a fever, then make 4 cauteries: 2 on the two corners of the head, and 1 in the middle of the head, and 1 on the place that is called "vessels" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and let it be treated as we have said before.

de litargie
On lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l'occipite l'emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c'est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j'ai dit.
For this illness, it is necessary to give the patient large hierae and pills cleansing the brain; afterwards shave the patient's head completely, and put on the occiput the mustard plaster that is written in the treatise on plasters; and this is the manner of the cautery: do it as I have said.
S'il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s'il ne l'est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc'a col, et ait d'espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu'il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j'ai devant dit.
If he is healed thus, it is good; and if he is not, then make 3 cauteries from the middle of the head descending to the neck, and have a space of one finger's width between each cautery; and treat it like the others, and if you want to add, and the patient is suffering, make 1 cautery in the middle; and if necessary, 2 others on the two corners, and treat it until it is healed; and let the cautery be the one called "olive-shaped", as I have said before.

de la froidor dou chief
On the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l'espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l'espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu'il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.
It is necessary that the head be cleansed with hierae and with what we have said before; afterwards shave the patient's head, then make a cautery in the middle of the head and on each corner, and 1 behind and 3 on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the illness is strong, then make 4 cauteries on the spine of the back; and leave it until most of the skin is burned, and lift your hand; afterwards treat it until it is healed, and let the cautery be the one called "olive-shaped" that we have mentioned before.

de l'epilempsie
On epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d'autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.
The epileptic should not use cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to first cleanse the brain with herbs and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is grown and able to take medicine.
Et se c'est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j'ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l'espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j'ai dit.
And if it's a child who cannot bear it, make them gargle and chew to cleanse the brain often with good foods; then shave the middle of the head, and make a cautery as we have said before, and a cautery on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the patient is strong and able to bear it, make cauterizations as I have said for those who have paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cautery be olive-shaped as I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:
If the patient is a child, make a subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.
When due to melancholy there are superfluities or corrupted moistures and thick phlegm, then cauterize with such cauteries as we have said for those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu'il est devant en la division.
And if due to melancholy the superfluities are declining to melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then give them something to drink by which the brain may be cleansed, according to what is said before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s'on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu'il soit sanez.
Then shave the patient's head; then make a well-made linen wreath, like a circle, and put it in the middle of the head; and the patient sits cross-legged, and is held well on all sides; then present the liniment, and it's better with old sheep's butter; and heat it moderately over fire, so that the finger can bear it when pressed; then empty the circle from within the middle of the head, and let it cool; and do this to the patient once a week along with other good treatments, until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.
Or if you wish, cauterize by making several points with the entire cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.
This manner of cautery moistens the brain evenly; and then put cotton moistened in butter and chicken fat on top.

de l'awe des eulz
On water in the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j'ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.
When water first comes to the eyes by the signs I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient something to drink that cleanses the head, and keep them from all moisture, and make them sweat in the bath several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l'awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.
Then command them to shave their head, and make a cautery in the middle of the head, and make two cauteries on the two temples if the descent of water is in both eyes together, or in one if the descent is in one; and cut with the entire cautery all the veins and arteries that are under the skin, and let the cauteries be long according to the width of the temple; and beware of blood flow, and if you see too much blood coming out, stop it with whatever power you have.
Et je t'enseignerai en l'estraction des arteres et a l'incision la cautele coment tu l'estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.
And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision the caution of how you will stop it; and sometimes a cautery is made on the nape below the two rear bones.

dou cors des larmes
On the flow of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l'aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c'est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j'ai dit en l'encomencement de l'awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s'il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.
When the tears of the eyes are old and habitual and are on the veins, or beside the arteries that are in the appearance of the head outside; and one sees that it is from cold phlegmatic superfluities, then make the cautery that I have mentioned at the beginning of the water descending to the eyes: one cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries on the nape below the two bones; and if there is more need, cauterize wisely above the eyebrow with a small cautery.

dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz
On the flow of tears inside the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l'artere que tu ne la coper.
When you treat it according to what we have said in the division, and it does not profit at all, then give the patient something to drink for three nights in a row; then shave the head, and make a cautery in the middle with the olive-shaped cautery; and make two cauteries with the cautery called "clavilis" on the two eyebrows, a little below the hair; and beware of cutting the artery.
Et c'est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:
And this is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l'oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:
When the eyelid is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery called "olivare". Of which here is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n'i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j'ai dit.
And if you wish, make two cauteries on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are; and do not leave the hand except so much that the third part of the eyelid is burned, according to the manner I have said.

dou poil qui point l'oil
On the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l'oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c'est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.
Sometimes it happens that the eyelashes are turned inward, and prick the eye, and cauteries are made according to two manners: namely by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu'il laisse les poilz tant qu'il soient lons et igals; et s'il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu'il ne se muevent tant qu'il naissent.
For the fire cautery, command the patient to let the hairs grow until they are long and even; and if they prick at their birth, constrain the eyes so that they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d'uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l'oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:
When they grow and are even, then put the patient in your care; then mark on the eyelid a figure that is like the leaf of a myrtle, and let the beginning of the mark be beside the hairs; then put cotton moistened in egg white and parsley mucilage on the eye, then heat the cautery of which here is the form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l'uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l'oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d'oignement tant qu'il soit sanez.
Then cauterize on the figure that you have marked little by little many times, so that the skin is burned there; and the sign of the health of the work is that you see the eyelid retracted, and the hairs raised at the edge of the eye; then lift your hand, and leave it thus for three days, then put cotton moistened in butter until the burn is removed; then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l'oil.
And if after this the hairs come, and the eyelid is softened then restart the cautery on that same place, as you did at first; and if the hairs are outside, cauterize until the eyelid is raised to its natural place, and is even, and the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu'il laisse les poilz tant qu'il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu'il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l'oil coton moilliet en abin d'uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.
The cautery of burning medicine is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow until they are large and even, then make from parchment the shape of a myrtle leaf; then take French soap and quicklime, one ounce of each, and grind them well together; and do it quickly, so that it doesn't cool, then spread it on the shape that you have made like the myrtle leaf, and put it on the eyelid; and if the disease is in one eye only, one should work on one, and if in both also; and put under the eye cotton moistened in egg white; and let the patient's head be in your care and put your pointing finger on the medicine, and press a little and move it every time the patient feels a biting sensation from the medicine, for they feel a biting sensation as if from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.
When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine with your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d'awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s'ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s'il est ensi, si est bien.
And when the biting sensation has passed, wash the place with water, and look if you see the eyelid raised as if it were raised by the constraint of fire or by incision; and if it is so, it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n'ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l'oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d'autre, tant qu'il soit sanez.
If not, put more of the medicine on the place where the medicine has not worked, until your work is even, and your eyes are put right; then put cotton moistened in butter until the burned skin has fallen off, then treat the place with the ointment called "diaphenix" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t'est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu'il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.
And if it is necessary for you to be very careful in your work with great care that no medicine falls into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l'oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu'il soit sanez; et c'est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:
And if the eyelid becomes soft afterwards, and the hair pricks the eye, then restart the medicine on the place that is softened on the eyelid itself, just as you did before; then treat it until it is healed; and this is the shape of the myrtle leaf:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.
And know that men's eyes are diverse in size, both large and small, and according to this should be your constraints; and let not the right way be hidden from him who studies this art.

de la cure de fistule par cautere
On the cure of fistula by cautery

Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.
When you treat fistula as we have said in the sections on diseases, and your treatments do not work, then it is necessary that you cauterize it in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu'il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu'il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;
Order the patient to put his head in your lap; and have the assistant hold his head between your hands in such a way that he does not move or shake his head;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d'uef ou en jus de persillion sus l'oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d'une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;
then put cotton soaked in egg white or parsley juice on the eye; then heat the cautery which is like this: and is headed at the end like the shape of a vulture's feather, together with which is the cautery;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l'un chief dusc'a l'autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.
if you wish, let it be pointed from one end to the other, and if you wish, let it be like a tent; but in any case, the one that is headed is better for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s'ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s'ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;
Then press the fistula if it is open, and draw out the pus, and dry it; and if it is closed, open it, and draw out the matter;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l'oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l'oil, et la corromp.
then put the very hot cautery on it, and hold your hand on the cautery on the part of the nerve away from the eye, so that your hand does not make a mistake; and put the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc'a l'os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors;
If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, it would be good. If not, then start the cautery again once more, and another if you need to, and leave it for 3 days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l'oignement desiccatif tant qu'il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu'il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.
then put cotton soaked in butter on it, and treat it with drying ointment until it is healed, and if 40 days pass without it being healed, then put on sharp corrosive medicine until the bone is uncovered; and scrape it according to what will come in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:
And there is a manner of cautery for fistula that some of the ancients spoke of. Attend to the fistula, and split the place; then put in the split a subtle cameo of which here is the shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d'une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;
and they make it to the quantity of a drachm of lead; and hold your hand on the cameo firmly, and let not the patient move at all, so that the melted lead does not run into his eye;
et covient c'on mette sus l'oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d'uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.
and it is necessary to put on the patient's eye cotton soaked in egg white or water: the lead thus burns the place of the fistula, and heals it with marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c'est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu'il covient en som propre leu.
And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have spoken of, that is good. If not, then it is necessary to administer holes to the nerve, and bring back the fistula to the body of the nerve according to what is appropriate in its proper place.

des crevaices en levres

On cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.
Many times cracks occur in lips that are called "hair", and especially in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:
When you treat these cracks with what we have said in the sections, and the treatment does not work, then heat a small knife-like cautery according to this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu'il viegne jusc'a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu'il soit sanez.
And put it quickly in those cracks until it comes to the bottom; then treat the place with wax until it is healed.

de l'aposteme de la goule
On abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l'uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;
When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the uvula, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, afterwards it makes pus and breaks and becomes old and becomes a fistula;
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;
and you treat it as we have said in the sections, and it does not work: then it is necessary that you have a cautery according to the size of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu'il soit sanez;
then push it into the hole of the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron comes to its bottom, and to the last place; and do this once or twice, then treat it with what we have said in treatments, until it is healed;
et s'il est curez ensi, c'est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l'os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.
and if it is cured thus, that is good; and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.

dou movement des dens
On the movement of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;
When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines and this does not work, then put the head of the patient in your lap;
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;
then heat the cautery whose shape will come hereafter in such a manner that you put a reed on the tooth; and put inside the hot cautery quickly, and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d'awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.
then lift your hand and restart the cautery according to your will; then let the patient fill his mouth with salt water, and hold it for an hour and spit it out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.
And in this manner the tooth that was moving is thus confirmed, and the softened gum tightened, and the corrupted moisture dried.

de la dolor des dens
About toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.
When toothache comes from cold, or there is cold or inflammation, and medical treatments don't work, then cauterization is needed in two ways: cauterization with butter and cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d'arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d'une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu'il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.
Butter cauterization is done as follows: take cow's butter and boil it in an iron or brass spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a probe, dip it in the boiled butter, and quickly place it on the aching tooth and hold it until it cools; do this often until its effect reaches the root of the tooth, and if you wish, soak wool and cotton in cold butter, place it on the aching tooth, and put a hot iron on it until the heat reaches the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d'arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l'endemain.
Fire cauterization is done as follows: take an iron or brass tube, thick enough so that the fire doesn't reach the patient's mouth; then heat the cautery, whose form will be shown later, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools; do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l'empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c'est li forme dou cautere:
And the patient should fill their mouth with good butter during the application of this cautery, and then spit it out; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c'est li forme de la caine:
And make the cautery from whichever end you want, according to your ability; and this is the form of the tube:

des scrophules
About scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l'autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l'apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu'il viegne au font de l'apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l'apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d'oignemens et de tentes tant qu'il soit sanez. Li forme de la cainne:
When scrofula is caused by phlegm and cold moisture, and does not respond to digestion by medicines, then heat the hollow cautery whose form is shown below, and it should have two openings for the smoke to escape from the other side of the cautery; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or twice if necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it for three days; and place cotton soaked in butter on it until the burn is removed; then treat the area with ointments and dressings until it is healed. The form of the tube:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc'a la gorge, et n'ardre dou keur mais c'un poc.
When moisture overwhelms the channels of the lungs, especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient should first be emptied by purgative medicines; then make a cautery at the root of the throat, and be careful not to reach the throat, and burn only a little of the flesh.
Aprés li fai .i. autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l'espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu'il soit sanez.
Then make another cautery at the joint of the neck at the top of the spine, and let it be the cautery called "clavile" whose form we have shown before; and treat the area as we have said before until it is healed.

de la toust
About cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.
When cough and lung disease are from cold moisture, and the patient has neither fever nor dryness, and the disease is old, make two cauteries on the breastbone in empty places; and another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two breasts; and let the cautery be the one called "clavile" according to the form previously described.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc'a .xxx., ou enqui entor.
And if you wish, make a cautery by pricking with the cautery called "points" whose form is shown above in the section on ear diseases; and let the points be up to 30, or thereabouts.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a .iij. rains selonc ceste forme:
Then treat the area as described before, and let the cautery have three prongs according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.
And for this reason, the cauteries are easier, because you make three at once.

de la dislocation de l'ajutoire
About dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l'ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n'i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.
When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is put back in place, but cannot stay and keeps coming out and dislocating with small movements, as we have experienced, then it is necessary that you first reduce the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:
Then let the patient lie on their back and on their side; then lift the flesh that is inside the armpit with the fingers of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inward, heat the cautery that has two prongs, of which here is the form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu'il le perce jusc'a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d'une tente et c'est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:
and cauterize the flesh until it pierces to the side, and the figure of the cautery will come together as four cauteries; and for this reason, a cautery is made with the cautery that has three prongs, so that the figure of cauterization is six cauteries; and the prongs are according to the thinness of a probe and this is the form of the cautery that has three prongs:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres. Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu'il soit bien confortez.
And sometimes a prong is added to this so that there are eight cauteries. Then put crushed leeks with salt on the cautery; then let the patient rest, and the limb should not be moved for a long time until it is well strengthened.
Et s'il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l'epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant. Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.
And if it is dislocated above, which happens rarely, then make a cautery on the thickness of the clavicle cautery, or many pricking cauteries. For the joint is closed, the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l'estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu'il l'estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.
When coldness and much moisture come to the stomach so that they draw it to its complexion, and catarrhs are multiplied in it, and the usual methods of treatment do not help, then it is necessary that the patient lie on their back, and extend their legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai .iij. cauteres .i. desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d'un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et .ij. cauteres defuers les .ij. costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a .iij. angles, et ait teil espaice entre l'une et l'autre qu'elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu'il porpreignent les .ij. pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:
After this, make three cauteries: one below the breastbone by the width of a finger, with the clavicle cautery, and two cauteries outside the two sides so that the figure of the cauteries is in three angles, and have such space between one and the other that they are not joined together when they discharge pus; and let the cauteries be so deep that they take up two-thirds of the flesh, and let the figure of the cauteries be according to this form without addition:
Et se tu vues cauterize d'un grant cautere enmi l'estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l'estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d'enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».
And if you wish, cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form; and for one who is afraid of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and mark on the stomach a point according to the quantity of ink you want; then cauterize it with the cautery called "points".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu'il soit sanez.
Then treat it with the treatment we had before, until it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu'il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d'enche .iij. cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l'ome vient; et ait d'espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d'un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s'il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c'est li forme:
When pain comes to the liver from cold and moisture and thick windiness, so much that it is put out of its natural complexion by excesses; and the patient is treated with what we have said in divisions, and it does not help him, then it is necessary that the patient lie on his back; and mark with ink three cauteries according to this form and this figure and this quantity on the liver, outside the hypochondria, where the man's elbow comes; and have a space between each cautery the thickness of a finger; and let the cauteries be along the length of the body, and do not press your hand too much with the cautery; and let only half of the flesh be burned, and let the patient be upright on his feet; and if he cannot, let him lie down, and extend his legs, and raise his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l'art, et te warde que tu n'ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu'il ne viegne jusc'a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.
And if it is your will, cauterize these cauteries with the knife-like cautery, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and be careful not to burn all the flesh, for you would dry out the whole body; and that it does not come to the bowel, for the flesh is very thin there, and know this for sure.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s'il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s'il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s'il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.
When there is an abscess in the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain that is not too strong; and if it is in the membrane, he feels mad pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d'enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:
And when this treatment was described by physicians, it is necessary that the patient be laid on his back with his head up; and then mark with ink the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a ray, of which here is the shape:
Et cauterize .i. cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc'a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu'il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l'art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois. Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.
And cauterize with a cautery until the skin is burned, and it reaches the syphac (abdominal wall), so that all the pus comes out; afterwards treat according to the treatment of abscesses until it is healed; and it is not appropriate for anyone to use this cautery except those who have studied the art of medicine for a long time, and through whose hands these diseases have sometimes run. Then he can operate boldly, and yet it seems to me that it is better to leave it.

dou cautere de pleuresin
On the cautery for pleurisy

Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d'aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d'aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l'emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l'estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.
The ancients said that for pleurisy one should make cauteries from roots of aristolochia, and in this manner: take a root of long aristolochia, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and be as thick and as long as your finger; and moisten it in oil, and set it on fire, and cauterize one cautery between the collarbone and the neck, and two small cauteries a little lower in the part that is below the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth and sixth ribs, declining a little towards the back; and one cautery in the middle of the chest, and another on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two on the two sides of the chest outside the cautery that is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but do it openly as if smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a .i. raseur, et l'eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu'il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l'aposteme dou foie. Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.
And some ancients said that some men use an iron cautery resembling a razor, and heat it and put it between the ribs, until it comes to that abscess; and the pain jumps out, as we have said in the abscess of the liver. But in this work there is fear that the patient dies immediately, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.

de la mice
On the spleen

Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin. Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices .iij. cauteres, ou .iiij., en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n'apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners, si com nos l'avons mostreit en la dislocation de l'espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.  Aprés i boute les .ij. ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l'autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra .iiij. Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a .iij. ners. Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.
When you treat the disease of the spleen with what we have said in the divisions of treatments, and it does not profit at all, then there are three methods of cautery that are all good. Of which one method is that you make 3 or 4 cauteries, in a line according to the length of the spleen, according to the figure of the cautery of the liver that we have said before; and do not press your hand with all the cautery, and let the patient be on his back; and another manner of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has two prongs, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the skin that is over the spleen, where the patient's elbow comes towards the left, and let the elevation from which you lift the skin be according to the skin, according to the length of the body, and let the cauteries be according to the width of the body.  Then push the two inflamed prongs until the skin is pierced on the other side, and then pull out the cautery, and thus there will be 4. And if you want, cauterize with all the cautery with 3 prongs. Afterwards treat it when it has discharged pus for a long time, and this is worth more than the other treatments mentioned before.

de ydropisie
On dropsy

Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c'a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes». Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres entor la boude, et .i. sus l'estomac, et un sus le foie, et .i. sus la mice, et .ij. derrier le dos sus l'espinee, et .i. endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l'espés dou keur. Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l'aide de Deu. Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu'il est ci devant mis.
Cautery is not useful for dropsy, except for the manner which is called "ascites". When you treat it according to the manners we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not profit at all, then it is necessary that you make 4 cauteries around the navel, and 1 on the stomach, and one on the liver, and 1 on the spleen, and 2 behind the back on the spine, and 1 on the chest; and let the cauteries be very close to the thickness of the skin. Afterwards leave the cautery open to discharge pus for a long time, and do not abandon the treatment of the patient after the cautery; and healing will hasten, and the two intentions will be together with the help of God. The shape of the cautery for the belly should be the nail that we have shown before; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what is put here before.

de l'enfleure des piez
On the swelling of the feet

Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d'awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l'auriculaire et l'anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner. Et n'entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:
When the feet are swollen in one who is dropsical, and are full of citrine water, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little toe and the ring toe; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning. And do not enter too deeply, thus the citrine water will come out, and let the cautery be according to this shape:
