Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l'un desoz le genoil devant et l'autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.
Afterwards make on the two legs two cauteries on each leg at the point of the knife; and let the cauteries be lengthwise, one below the knee in front and the other outside, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries open for a long time without treating, so that the water comes out; afterwards treat with the other treatments that we have said.

de la menoison
On diarrhea

Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l'intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l'estomac selonc ceu qu'il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l'estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches. Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l'estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.
When looseness of the bowels comes from cold and moisture, so much that the retentive and digestive virtue which is in the stomach and in the intestine is weakened, and cannot be cured by manners of treatments; and you see the patient suffering well and of strong virtue, then make a large cautery on the stomach according to what has been spoken of before in the cautery of the stomach, with the circular cautery; and 4 subtle cauteries around the navel with all a subtle nail cautery, and 2 cauteries on the hips. And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, then make a cautery on the wrist, and a cautery on each flank, and 2 small cauteries on the stomach beside the large one, for the treatment is profitable when there is good help.

de la cure des emorroydes
On the treatment of hemorrhoids

Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l'espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu'il soit sanez.
When hemorrhoids are in the anus, either one or several, and are old and are from thick cold and moist corrupted humors, and are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not help, then make cauterizations:
Three on the spine of the back, the one that is all outside below the sacrum little by little in a triangle, and one cauterization below the navel, two fingers; and if you think that his stomach is cooled, and the food does not digest, and one sees the face swelling, then make a large cauterization on the stomach, as it is said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with the nail cautery; and leave the cauterization open for a long time. Afterwards, treat the place until it is healed.

de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»
On the fleshiness that is called "thelul"

Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit;
When you cut the thelul, heat the cautery that looks like a razor, and then put it all heated on this cut thelul;
et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort;
and leave your hand there until the cautery comes to the origin of the vein, from which the blood flows;
fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s'il i a mout d'althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit;
do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of thelul, cauterize each one as we have said;
aprés les cure d'oignemens profitans tant qu'il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d'un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.
afterwards treat them with beneficial ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the sacrum, it will have greater help.

de plaie mal curee
On poorly healed wounds

Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.
When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will discuss in its place, such a disease comes that cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.
When someone gets a fistula, and it is old and discharges pus and corrupted moisture, you should probe it with a thin probe, and make sure you know with the probe how deep it is.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing;
Afterwards, heat the cautery that looks like a razor, and push it into the fistula according to the depth that the probe entered, and repeat the cautery until those rotten and corrupted bodies are burned, once, or twice or thrice, according to the quantity of its need;
et te warde d'ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.
and be careful not to burn the nerves that are there, and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l'intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu'ele n'est mie persans;
if the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and to the intestine, be careful of these places, and do not do this except in fleshy places, and think that it is not piercing;
aprés cure le leu tant qu'il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement;
afterwards treat the place until it is healed, and if the place is sealed, and the materials are removed for a long time, then know that the place is completely healed;
et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.
and if the materials are not removed, know that the place is perforated, and the bone at the bottom is corrupted; and so as one of these that we will discuss in its place.

de la maladie des reins
On kidney disease

Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d'une part et d'autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit;
When pain from cold comes to the kidneys, and from thick windiness, and one does not take desire for women, then it is necessary that you make cautery on the kidneys on one side and the other with the nail cautery that we have mentioned before;
et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.
and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, and they will provide greater help.

de la vessie
On the bladder


Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l'urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d'un poce;
When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make cautery on the outside part over the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, and one on the right and one on the left, and let each cautery be as long as the knuckle of a thumb;
et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.
and make one cautery on the outside of the back, or two if you need it; and let the cautery be nail-shaped according to the form mentioned before.

de la marris
On the womb

Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor:
When the womb is cold and moist, and does not stop conceiving because of this, and the menses are corrupted and their periods are late; and when they come, one feels great pain:
adonques covient il c'on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.
then it is necessary to make three cauteries around the navel, as we have said for the cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries on the outside of the back; and let the cautery be nail-shaped, as we have said.

de la hainche
On the hip

Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble;
When viscous moistures descend to the socket of the hip, and because of this it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when one measures them together;
et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle;
and the place of departure is found empty, so it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the socket of the hip with a cautery resembling a circle, and mark before the place around the socket as it turns, so that the socket is inside the circle;
et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac. Et se cist cauteres ne t'est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l'olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs;
and let the cautery be such as that with which one has cauterized the stomach. And if this cautery is not available to you, make three large olive-shaped cauteries, and let the cautery be as deep as all the leather;
et le cure tant qu'il soit sanez.
and treat it until it is healed.

de la dolor de la hainche
Of the pain in the hip

Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c'est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.
When pain comes to the hip joint, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we have said in the division and the cure is not effective, and the illness is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of thick humors with fetid pills, or other similar good pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c'est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.
Afterwards, cauterize him; and the manner of cauterization is according to two methods: namely together with burning medicines, and cauterization by fire.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d'espaice la groissece d'un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:
Cauterization by fire is done in many ways, of which one is as follows: that you cauterize on the hip joint three triangular cauterizations in this shape, and make them good and deep, and have between each cauterization a space the width of a finger, and let the cautery be olive-shaped; sometimes a cauterization is made in the middle on top of the hip, for which there are four in this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.
And if you wish, cauterize it with the circular cautery that we mentioned before for dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circle encompasses the whole hip, and all the thickness of the skin is burned.
Et c'est li maniere c'on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc'a la cuisse ne jusc'a la jambe.
And this is the method used for sciatica, when the pain is in the hip, and does not reach to the thigh or to the leg.
Et s'ele vient jusc'a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur;
And if it comes to the thigh and leg, make two cauterizations where the patient says the pain is, and one cauterization above the ankle four fingers, a little to the left side; and let the cautery be knife-shaped, and let the thickness of the skin be burned;
et se li malaides sent que li dolor s'estende jusc'a dois dou piet ou pres d'enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iii. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».
and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the toes or near there, cauterize where he feels the pain with three or four points using the cautery called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n'i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.
And if needed, make more; and if he knows that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, make a cauterization with the knife-shaped or circular cautery, and be very careful with all your cauterizations that you do not leave the cautery so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause greater harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.
And I myself have seen several who have made a cauterization on the ankle, and left it so long that the leg became completely swollen, and the foot as well, and the whole foot was pierced and corrupted. After this, a bowel movement from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l'une et en l'autre, selonc ceste maniere.  Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l'un entrechetres jusc'a l'autre d'espaice la quantiteit d'un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c'est li forme:
And if the pain is in two parts together, make a cauterization in one and the other, according to this method.  And the wise said for the cauterization of the hip, of which this is the method, make such an iron and let it be at the head as thick as a date pit, or a little less, and let it be by sections and let there be from one section to the other a space the size of a thumb knuckle; and let the sections be open on two sides, and be like knots, and have a well-made iron handle; and this is the shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu'il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iii. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d'oignement tant qu'il soit sanez.
And let it be heated until it is all red and throws sparks, and then put it on the sick hip joint, and let it be turned on the healthy side; and cauterize it once with a round cautery and leave it for three days; and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; afterwards treat with ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s'afiert.
Albucasim says that we use this cautery little because of the fear of its appearance, and we see few who use it; and yet it is one of the good cauteries, for those who can bear it, and where it is appropriate.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices .i. estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d'arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait .ij. nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d'un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:
The cautery of burning medicine is that you make an instrument with sections into which the edge of the opening descends, and let it be of brass or iron with a long wall, and in the height have two knots, and have between each the quantity of the thickness of a finger; and let them be open outside and above, and join together according to this shape:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les .ij. cercles de l'awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu .i. poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l'arsure de li.
Then put it on the hip joint of the patient lying on his healthy side, and press your hand hard on the hip joint; then pour between the two circles some hot water that has been heated a little by fire, and leave it for an hour, and let the patient endure the heat and burning of it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l'estrument et leve la hainche d'awe douce, et laisse ensi .iii. jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l'eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse .iii. jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d'oignemens tant qu'il soit sanez.
For he finds a biting sensation as if from fire; and when the biting has passed, lift your hand with the instrument and wash the hip with fresh water, and leave it thus for three days, and put butter on it until what is black from the scalding is removed; and leave it for three days so that pus comes out; and this will be the last aid after the treatment with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li dolor s'est estendue jusc'a la cuisse ou jusc'a la jambe, se li fai .i. estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c'est li maniere de l'awe chaude, et je l'ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.
And if the pain has extended to the thigh or to the leg, make an instrument that holds water according to what you have done in the hip equally; and this is the method of hot water, and I have written about it in the treatise on the rectification of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l'une com de l'autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en .i. nuef pot. ou il ait .i. petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d'un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot .i. autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu'il en i ait .i. doi desus les poudres cant tu l'avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu'il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.
Take alkali and quicklime, as much of one as the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot with a small hole outside so that the point of a razor can enter; and put over that pot another well-leaded pot, and put on top alkali and lime and fresh water, so much that there is a finger above the powders when you have pressed it well with your hand; and leave it thus until sharp water descends and falls into the leaded pot, then take all that water, and pour it over lime and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d'ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d'autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.
And then it will be very sharp and is administered in many medical operations and in cauterizations of other limbs For it does the same work as fire, and there are other medicines with which one cauterizes the hip well such as tesisie and anacardium honey and lime with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n'i fist autre cure, et qu'il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l'enseigne ci aprés.
And Galen tells us of a cure by which a man was cured of hip pain and sciatic vein, and praises it greatly, and says that no other cure was done, and that he was healed in a single time when this cure was done, and he had bathed as he teaches hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec .i. poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse .iii. houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l'arsure.
And he says in such a manner that you take fresh and dry green litharge, and grind it well with a little fat, and put it on the hip and on the thigh and on the leg where the pain is, and bind it; and leave it for three hours and in such quantity that the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s'en ira toute et sera sanez.
And then make him enter the bath until his body is a little wet, and make him enter the bed, and all the pain will go away and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n'est aprés l'evacuation de cors.
And know that no one should use cauterization with such medicines, unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere. Prenez lainne et la beurez d'oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l'autre qui est apelez foscile.
And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat dung, it helps greatly; and the cauterization should be done in this manner. Take wool and soak it in old oil, and put it on the small hollow that is between the big toe and the other that is called the fibula.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l'empren a feu tant qu'il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu'il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu'il viegne jusc'a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».
Then take dry goat dung, and set it on fire until it becomes charcoal, and put it on the wool, and leave it until it is extinguished; and do this again, and do not cease doing so until you think by sense that it has come to the hip, and that the pain has ceased; and this manner of cauterization is called "goat cautery".

de la dolor dou dos
Of back pain

Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.
When pain comes to the back, either by falling or by a blow or by too great evacuation, or by appearances of cold matter spread, cauterization is not effective for any of these appearances, except for that which comes from infusion of cold matter.

Il covient c'aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d'autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d'enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:
It is necessary that after the patient is purged with fetid pills or other similar ones, that one makes on his back, where the pain is, three lines marked with ink, and on each line 5 cauterizations or more according to the strength and quantity that the patient can bear; and let the cauterization be done according to the cautery called "points"; and if you wish, make 3 or 4 cauterizations with the medium nail-shaped cautery according to this form:

Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l'encomencement si est qu'il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l'apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.
Many times this illness comes to small children, and the signs of the beginning are that they have labored breathing when they rise, and fear; and you find in the last spine of the back and in us the appearance that comes on the other spines.

Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.
When you see this and you want to cure it, cauterize it with the circle cautery according to this form.

Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l'espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l'espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l'uns de l'autre.
So that the cautery encompasses each part of the spine equally. And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with the pointed cautery 2 or 3 lines, and let the points be close to each other.

Aprés cure le leu tant qu'il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n'amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.
Afterwards, treat the place until it is healed according to what we have said, and be careful not to administer cautery to a hump that is in spasm of the nerve.

de la dolor des jointes
Of joint pain

Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:
When joint pains are from moistures that are spread to each member of the body, and when pain comes to the feet, which doctors properly call "gout", and when it is from a cold cause and cures of medicines cannot cure it, it is cured by cauterizations in this manner: make many cauterizations around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:

Et s'il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c'on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc'a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n'i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.
And if there is need that you prick on the surface of the foot, make a cauterization with all the cautery that one calls "point". And if the pains come to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, make on each knee 3 or 4 cauterizations on each part, with the olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, make more, but do not hold your hand there except until the thickness of the skin is burned.

Et se les dolors dessendent jusc'a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s'il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc'as coutes ou jusc'as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l'aide de Deu.
And if the pains descend to the knee and to the back, administer the cautery that we have said in its chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the forearm 2 lines; and if any pain remains in the fingers, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the elbows or to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good care to the patient and give medicines. For if you give him good care and you purge phlegm, he will be healed with God's help.

de la routure dou syfac
Of rupture of the peritoneum

Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c'est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu'il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu'il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu'il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d'enche desoz la routure sus l'os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d'un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:
When rupture comes to the groin, and the bowels descend to the testicles and it is recent, it is necessary that when you want to cure it, he does not eat that day; and that he uses things that loosen the belly, so that the feces descend from his belly; afterwards make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath until the bowels are returned, and bring them back with your fingers, and mark with ink below the rupture on the pubic bone, and with a sign that is similar to half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery of which this is the form:

tant qu'il soit blans et qu'il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu'il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l'os, et se tu ne l'ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc'a l'os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.
until it is white and throws sparks. Then bring the bowels back to their place; and the assistant should hold his hand over them so they do not return back; and open well the thighs of the patient, and put under him a cushion and an assistant on the thighs, and another on the chest who holds his hands; then put the cautery on the mark with all your hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again another time until you come to the bone; and be very careful that the bowels do not come out when you make the cautery; that you do not burn them; and that by this the patient does not die, or other harm.

Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc'a l'os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d'ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d'autres oignemens tant qu'il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d'aler en chambres.
And know that when you do not come to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. And it is necessary that the cautery for children be subtle according to their measure, and for adults also large according to their measure; after 3 days treat the place of the cautery with butter until the scald is removed; afterwards treat it with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie 40 days on his back until the wound is well closed; and it is necessary that his nourishment be laxative for a long time, so that the bowels do not come out when he will go to the privy.

Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu'il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.
And after 40 days, when he will want to get up, administer to him a well-made bandage, and let him wear it for 40 other days; and let him have good rest, that he work little and guard against too great repletion of drinking and eating, and of shouting too loud; and when he does this instruction he is entirely healed. And I will say hereafter the cure of cutting in its chapter.


de la routure dou ventre
Of rupture of the belly

Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu'elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c'on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme: mais signe premier le leu d'enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.

When ruptures come in other bellies and are known, and you want them not to grow more, make a cauterization with the round cautery according to its quantity, and let a third of the skin be burned; afterwards treat it according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that one should cauterize it with the three-angled cautery according to this form: but first mark the place with ink and make a line across the width above the rupture, and another outside, and place your hand in the middle with all the nail-shaped cautery. But the first cautery is lighter and better.



de dolor anciene en aucun membre
Of old pain in any limb

Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n'i vaut, adonc covient qu'il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s'il est sanez dou premier cautere, c'est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu'il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.

When pain comes to any limb, either from falling or being struck, and this pain lasts a long time, and medical treatment is not effective, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery that is called "points", and let the cautery be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and its weakness and its strength and its location of twists and its pain. If it is healed from the first cautery, that is good; if not, begin another cautery on it, for such is the custom that it should change to the limb that is near it, which is why it is necessary that you make the cauterizations until the patient is healed.

40
de meselerie

Of leprosy

Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s'ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l'autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc'a l'os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s'en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu'il est devant.

Lepers are sometimes aided greatly by cauterization, and especially the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. When you want to cauterize it, take care if the disease is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not descend nor remain, and you fear that the corruption may overtake the whole patient, then make 5 cauterizations on the head: one in the middle of the head at the crown, and another towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and 2 on the two horns, and one behind on the nape; and leave your hand there until the cautery comes to the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can come out; and cauterize it on the fontanel according to what is in front.

Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l'espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l'espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l'os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l'os de l'estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.

And if the leprosy is spread everywhere; and it is manifestly apparent, it is necessary that you cauterize it with these cauterizations that we have said on the head, and one cauterization on the top of the nose, and 2 cauterizations on the spine of the neck, and 6 cauterizations on the spine of the back, and a large one on the rump and another beside it, and 2 on the two shoulders; and 2 on the elbows, and 2 on the cartilages of the chest, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are on the back of the heel, that you do not burn them; and sometimes one makes a cauterization on the pubic bone, and another on the breastbone, and another on the liver.

Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d'aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu'il soit saneis.

And know that the more cauterizations you make, the more you help him, and the more it benefits him; and know that the patient does not feel any pain from the cauterization as healthy people feel it, because the body is already completely corrupted. And it is necessary that the cauterizations be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the manners of irons. Afterwards treat the place with vetch flour with honey and other treatments until it is healed.

Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n'est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l'espés dou keur; puis le cure d'oignemens tant qu'il soit sanez.

When swelling comes to any limb and is treated by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then make cauterizations on the limb according to the largeness and smallness of the limb; and let the cautery enter a little into the thickness of the skin; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.

Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l'issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s'en entremette nuls s'il n'est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.

And sometimes one makes a cauterization on the hand and on the foot and on the back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus the swelling is removed; and yet let no one undertake this if he is not knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the nerves moving the body.

41
de albaras

Of vitiligo

Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n'i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d'un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l'espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d'alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d'un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu'il soit sanez.

When the disease that is called "albaras" is old, and the skills of medicine are of no value, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deep, according to the quantity of the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed, and its color is changed; then treat it with vetch flour and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and pigeon blood and swallow blood, one part of each; and let it all be mixed together, and be bound with a cloth, and be attached to the place until it is healed.

42
li cure de chancre par cautere

The cure of cancer by cautery

Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre. Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l'ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu'il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.

When cancer comes at the beginning, and you want to stop it, cauterize it with the cautery that resembles a circle, all around the cancer. And yet the wise say that one should also make a cauterization in the middle of the cancer; and yet this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen sometimes; and it is more right that it be cauterized around, with the cautery that is called "circle", as we have said in many cauterizations.

43
de l'enfleure qui ne puet meurer

Of the swelling that cannot ripen

Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu'ele fait ou por l'eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c'est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.

When someone has a disease that is called "adubelati", and it is slow to ripen either because of the excess it makes or because of the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say very old) and he has little blood, or because of the time; and you want to hasten its ripening: then cauterize around it with many small pointed cauterizations; afterwards leave it thus. For it will hasten to ripen.

Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu'il soit sanez parfaitement.

And if you want to pierce it with the cautery, heat the cautery of which this is the form:
And put your hand in the middle of this disease that is called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the skin, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it outside in such a way that the flow of the corruption is eased. Afterwards treat it until it is perfectly healed.

44
li cure dou feu par fer

The cure of fire by iron

Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n'est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu'il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.

There is another manner of disease that is called "corrodens", and is nothing other than an itching of a limb, for it eats the limbs just as fire does dry wood. If you see this disease in a place that can suffer cauterization together with fire, then heat the nail-shaped cauteries very small and large, according to what is suitable for the place where the disease is; afterwards cauterize it on all sides until you remove all the corruption, and nothing remains of it, so that all that is corrupted is removed.

Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d'oignemens engendrans char. Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c'est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.

And then leave it for 3 days, and put on the cauterized places ground sulfur with oil until the scalds from the fire are removed, and all the corruption. Afterwards treat it with ointments generating flesh. And if you see after 3 days that healthy flesh is not growing, that is good; and if not, then begin again the cauterization on what remains of the corrupted places.

Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j'ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.

And this itching has sometimes been cured by sharp medicine in place of cauterization by fire; but nevertheless cauterization by fire is of greater help, and I have already said the cure of sharp medicine in the division: take it when you have need of it.

45
des porrelz qui vienent as piez
About the warts that come on the feet

Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.
It often happens that on the feet, externally, a disease called "clos" (nail) according to our understanding grows, and it is a large, felt-like thing that hurts the foot.

Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres.
And the cauterization of this disease is done in two ways.

C'est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d'aigue chaude.
That is to say, cauterization by fire and cauterization by hot water.

Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu'il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu'il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu'il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu'il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l'emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.
Cauterization by fire is when you heat a cautery iron shaped like a vulture's feather, made of good iron to the measure that it can encompass the nail from all sides, and that it has thin edges; then put it hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it reaches the bottom of the nail; and leave it thus for three days until it begins to discharge pus; then make a plaster of wild mallows crushed with salt, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nail will fall off and be uprooted from its roots.

Puis cure le leu d'oignement enjanrant char tant qu'il soit sanez.
Then treat the place with an ointment that generates flesh until it is healed.

Et s'il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d'aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d'arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l'althelul, c'est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu'ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d'awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l'aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc'a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l'aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.
And if they are converted externally on the body, and it often happens on hands and feet, it is necessary that you administer hot water cauterization; and it is done in this manner: take a tube of brass or iron, or a vulture's feather, and put it on the nail and the althelul, that is to say warts; and put the tube on so that it encompasses all around, then put a little hot water in it, and hold your hand steady, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the tube comes to the root of the nail, and the hot water can find a deep path to the root; and let the patient endure the burning of the hot water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will uproot itself with all its roots.

Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.
Do this one after another, until you uproot all those that are on the body, then treat them with ointments that generate flesh.

46
li cure dou trembler
The cure for trembling

Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d'autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l'espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l'estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.
When someone trembles from cold nerves, or from quartan fever or another, it is necessary that you make four or five cauterizations on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each vertebra; and one cauterization on the chest, and one on the stomach with an olive-shaped cautery; thus the trembling will cease, and the health of the cold disease will be hastened.

47
des pustules puans
About stinking pustules

Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.
Sometimes baths appear externally on the body, or stinking pustules, which come from large corrupted matters.

si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.
So it is necessary at first when they appear that one make a cauterization on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of myrtle wood, of which the point is set on fire, or of long birthwort root, or with a lenticular cautery.

Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l'evacuation de sanc.
And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow from then on, but the superfluity from which they come is broken up, and they are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.

48
quant li artere est copee
When the artery is cut

Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l'artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l'incision de l'aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d'estenchier.
Often great flows of blood occur from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes externally, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cauterization of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very difficult thing to stanch.

Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l'estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n'en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu'il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.
And yet when this happens to someone, hasten to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press it hard until the blood is calmed under your finger, and no drop comes out anymore; then put several small and large olive-shaped cauteries in the fire until they are all red; then take one, either large or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is broken, and put the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery there until the blood is stanched.

Et s'il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.
And if it jumps out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery goes out, quickly take another of the cauteries that are in the fire.

Et ne cesser de faire ceu l'un aprés l'autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n'ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l'artere, c'on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n'est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n'est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.
And do not cease to do this one after another until the blood is stanched; and be careful not to burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from the artery, one cannot stanch it well, especially when the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not drawn out, or by strong binding with thread, or by medicines put on that have the power to stanch blood; and let it be bound and tightened suitably.

Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n'i profite se poc non.
Whoever will administer stanching by tightly binding with cloths or by putting burning things on, or other similar things, it will not profit much if at all.

Et se ce avient a aucun et il n'ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu'il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d'awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.
And if this happens to someone and there is no physician or medicine present, they should put their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press well until it is stanched above the wound and above the vein; and do not move the finger, but wet it with cold water often so that it is very cold until the blood is congealed and thickened and stanched; and from then on do what is necessary with cauteries and medicines.

Ci encomencent li chapistre dou livre
Here begin the chapters of the book

De la cauterization de l'aige qui est engenree as chief.
On the cauterization of water that is generated in the head.

De l'incision des arteres que sont aprés les oreilles.
On the incision of arteries that are behind the ears.

De l'estraction des arteres que sunt en temples a tout l'espatule ague de .ij. pars.
On the extraction of arteries that are in the temples with the sharp spatula on both sides.

De l'estraction des arteres que sont en temples a tout le cautere qui est apelez «almagderi».
On the extraction of arteries that are in the temples with the cautery that is called "almagderi".

Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille
Here begins the second book of surgical treatments

Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc'a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c'on trueve plus legierement ceu c'on voura.
We have told you in the first chapter about every disease for which cautery by fire or burning medicine is necessary, and the occasions and causes and instruments and forms of cauteries; and I have put that chapter from head to toe, and I will go in this chapter by the same way so that one can find more easily what one wants.

Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.
And before I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first one about cauteries, and for this reason greater caution is needed.

Car en l'ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l'ovrir la voinne, et a l'incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l'estraction des saiettes, et a l'incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.
For in the work of this chapter, there often occurs evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and in the incision on abscesses, and in the cures of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in the incision on stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and death comes to many.

Et je vos amoneste que vos n'entreprenez folie.
And I warn you not to undertake foolishness.

Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s'aïrent si avec lor maladie qu'il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu'il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.
For many kinds of people come for treatments. There come some who are so angry with their disease that they die easily because of the madness they find from their disease, and from the greatness of its malice; and of these one should be afraid.

Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.
And of these there are some who give you their sense, and say: "wait, I am cured"; and the disease is despicable.

Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu'en vostre covoitise, et n'ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.
It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put greater care in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not work foolishly but wisely on that of which you are certain, and from which you can have taken and praise; and use prognosis and indication in cures of your patients to which health may be converted; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, and glory, and memory of praise.

Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.
Very dear son, May Our Lord give you good understanding and righteousness, and may He wish to inspire you with the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.

Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu'il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc'a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.
Now I have ordered this chapter by dividing it into chapters, according to what is before in the chapter on cauteries, which I have devised for you from head to toe, so that you may more easily find what you will need.

dou chief plein d'aigue
On the head full of water

Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l'enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l'enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.
Know that this disease comes very often to children at birth, and when the midwife squeezes the child's head too strongly; and sometimes this comes from a hidden cause that one does not know.

Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu'en enfans, et a toz ces que j'ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu'il me vaut mues lassier l'ovraige en teilz cures.
And I never saw this disease except in children, and in all those that I have seen death hastened; and for this reason it seems to me that it is better to leave the work in such cures.

Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d'aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu'il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu'il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l'os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l'os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l'os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:
And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and the head swelled each day so much that it could not sustain it; and the moisture grew so much that he died, and this moisture is gathered under the bone on the membrane, between the skin and the bone; and the work is such that if the moisture is between the skin and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you make in the middle of the head a wide incision; and let it be as long as two knuckles, so that the moisture runs; and here is the form of the spatula:

Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d'une croix, selonc ceste forme:
If the moisture has grown more, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the manner of a cross, according to this form:

Et se li moistor est desoz l'os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t'est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:
And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs that you see are the sutures of the head open on each part, and the water jumps out when you press it with your hand on the inside, and this is not hidden from you: so it is necessary that you make three incisions in the middle of the head according to this manner:

Et aprés l'incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc'a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.
And after the incision, extract all the moisture out. After, tighten the incisions with cloths and powders, and put wine and oil there, and leave it thus until the fifth day; then untie it, and treat the wound with tents and ointments, and let the head tighten equally, and give the patient dry food with little moisture until the member is comforted and healed.

Et une autre maniere d'incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l'aposteme, et li assemblé de l'aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre. Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l'emplissement de l'aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l'artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l'evacuation de moistor.
And another manner of incision is that you look where the size of the abscess appears, and the gathering of the water; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left. Cut therefore where the abscess appears, and the filling of water, and split it according to what you have the power to do; and be careful not to cut the artery; and let blood flow, so that the patient does not die from the running of blood and the evacuation of moisture.

de reume
On rheum

Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c'on li copera les .ij. arteres.
When someone gets a disease that is called "catarrh" in the eyes or chest, and the disease is old, and the cure of medicine does not profit, then the last cure is the cautery along with cutting the two arteries.

Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d'un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l'une et de l'autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d'enche, puis cope l'une et l'autre d'un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc'a l'os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.
It is necessary therefore, when you want to cut them, that the patient have his head shaved; after rub the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then let the patient tighten his neck with a cloth; then look where the vein beats, and the places of one and the other are behind the ears, and little are hidden; then mark the places with ink, then cut one and the other with a spatula sharp on two sides. until the cut comes to the bone, and this should be across the width of the head.

Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l'artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.
And if you want, push the spatula under the artery and cut it above, cutting as if two fingers across.

Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.
And when the vein is cut, the blood jumps up continuously outward.

Et se li artere n'apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l'espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d'enche et fent jusc'a l'os; et ceu qu'il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l'artere; puis regarde la plaie: s'il remaint sus l'os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n'i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d'oignement tant qu'ele soit sanee.
And if the artery does not appear to the touch, it is necessary that you measure the quantity of the space of three fingers, then mark with ink and split to the bone; and what is necessary of the blood to put out is six ounces, and by chance a little more or less. according to what the patient can suffer, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if any of the membrane remains on the bone, cut it so that no hot abscess comes there, then tighten the wound and bind it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.

de emigrainne
On migraine

Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.
When old migraine comes, and acute catarrh, because of the moistures of tears and the heats in temples and old mad soda and similar things, and it is medicated by manners of medical cures and all this does not profit him, we extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have told.

Et li maniere de l'estraction d'elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l'artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s'elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d'aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d'aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d'aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:
And the manner of their extraction is that the patient have the hairs of his temples shaved, and attend to the artery that appears in the temple, for it appears well by its beating, and is little hidden except in some men who are too cold; and if it is hidden, let the patient tighten his neck with some cloths, then rub the place with some rough cloth, and water the place with hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula of which here is the form:

puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l'artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l'uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés.
then lightly skin the leather until you come to the artery, then draw it up with tweezers, and separate it well from the membranes that are under it on each part; and if the artery is subtle, turn it to the point of the hook, then cut it from that part according to the quantity of the two ends.

Car s'elle n'est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.
For if it is not cut, the blood does not jump out at all.

Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc'a .iij.; 
And draw blood from the six hundred, up to three hundred;

et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d'un fil double fort de soie, 
and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a strong double silk thread,

que porriture n'i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; 
so that infection does not come before the wound heals, and to prevent blood flow;

puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, 
then cut the excess between the two ties at that same hour,

et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc'a l'os tant que li chiés soient copez; 
and then, if you wish, cauterize it with a knife-shaped cautery down to the bone until the ends are cut;

et c'est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n'a fievre et il est de chaude complexion. 
and this is the best procedure, if the patient does not have a fever and is of a hot complexion.

Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors. 
For the cautery helps to finish off the moisture: for this reason it is of greater help for moistures.

Ou il covient por l'estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; 
Or it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fill the place with old cotton and put well-made tents on top;

et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu'il soit sanez; 
and when they are untied, let it be treated with dry medicines that make flesh grow, and with tents, until it is healed;

et se sans cort de l'artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, 
and if blood flows from the artery while you are working, hasten to cut it with a cautery,

ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l'estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; 
or fill the place with vitriol and strain it with your hand so that the blood is stanched;

et se tu n'as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, 
and if you don't have this at hand, put your finger on the place until the blood is congealed,

et arose le leu d'aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; 
and sprinkle the place with cold water until the blood stops, and let it be strained as is necessary;

et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l'estraction de l'artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, 
and what is better and easier in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein with this cutting cautery from two sides,

mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor. 
but let the cutting edges be very thick to keep their heat longer.

Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor. 
For when the instrument is too thin, it retains less of its heat.

Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d'espaice, 
And there should be a finger's width of space between the two blades,

et puis quant tu as signiet d'enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu'il viegne jusc'a l'os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; 
and then when you have marked the two places with ink, and you put the hot iron on until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places;

et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n'est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; 
and let them be separated between the two ends because it is not completely sealed by this cautery;

et c'est li forme dou cautere:
and this is the shape of the cautery:

des larmes
On tears

Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, 
When tears from the eyes are descending from the veins that are on the outer skull of the head,

et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c'on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, 
and medical treatment that one applies does not help, and you see the patient's face redden,

et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, 
and feels a movement on the forehead as if from ants; and their eyes are thin and moist so that the eyelashes have fallen out,

et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l'ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure. 
and the eyelids are heated, and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this cure is needed.

Et l'apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu'il ait ou front, 
And the ancients called it "contused cure", and it is that you have the patient who has this illness shave the hair that they have on their forehead,

puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; 
then make three cuts on the forehead equally along the length of the forehead;

et soit l'une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc'a neif, 
and let one of the cuts be like two fingers right in the middle of the forehead going down to the nose,

et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, 
and the other two on the two sides above the eyelids,

et te garde de l'incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; 
and be careful of cutting the arteries that are on the two sides above the eyelids;

et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, 
and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jawbones,

et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins; 
and let each wound be the width of three fingers joined across;

et aies apparillie une piece d'esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, 
and have ready a piece of sponge and many dry cloths to wipe the blood,

puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:
then push the sharp spatula with two sides, of which this is the shape:

des l'incision qui est dever la temple jusc'a la seconde incision; 
from the incision that is towards the temple to the second incision;

et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l'os, 
and scrape all the skin that is between the two cuts with all the membrane that is on the bone,

puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc'a l'autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile. 
then do the same from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove this spatula.

si boute en la premiere fendure l'estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», 
Then push into the first cut the instrument that is called "knife-like",

et est tresbien trenchans d'une part, et d'autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c'est li forme:
and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is smooth, not sharp, and this is its shape:

Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l'os, 
And put the sharp side towards the flesh attached to the skin, and the smooth side towards the bone,

et lou boute tant qu'il veigne a la moiene fendure. 
and push it until it comes to the middle cut.

Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l'incision soit continue jusc'a ceu qui apert dou keur, 
And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous up to what appears of the skin,

et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc'a l'autre defuer; 
and then do the same in the middle cut up to the other outer one;

et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; 
and then extract blood equally, and press the place for the blood taken;

puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, 
then put in each cut a tent of old cotton,

et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n'i veigne; 
and put on top cloths soaked in wine and oil and vinegar, and watch that hot abscesses do not form;

et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d'aigue tede,
