and on the third day untie the binding, and administer a large amount of lukewarm water,

puis lou cure d'oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d'autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu'il soit sanez.
then treat it with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and with other treatments used to cure wounds, until it is healed.

dou reume des eulz
On rheum of the eyes

Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; 
When acute catarrh comes to someone habitually, and you see the eyes thin and small, and the vision weakening, and the eyelids burned;

et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; 
and the hair falls out, and in the head there is deep acute pain, and the patient sneezes;

adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, 
then know by these symptoms that these matters and this catarrh come only from many veins,

et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste. Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, 
and the best cure for it is this. And it is that you command the patient to shave their forehead,

puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. 
then make a large cut in the middle of the forehead, and another one of the width of a thumb.

Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc'a l'os; 
And begin from the cut of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be down to the bone;

et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; 
and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating;

et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, 
and when the bone is uncovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge,

et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; 
and then separate between the two lips of the cut and put old cotton there, and linen tents;

puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d'aposteme chaut; 
then tie on top cloths soaked in wine and oil, and guard against hot abscesses;

quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l'os tant que chars i comence a naistre, 
when it is removed, it is necessary that you rub the bone until flesh begins to grow there,

puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char. 
then treat it with drying things, which make flesh generate.

En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; 
In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour, and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster of it;

et l'aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.
and administer it on these wounds to generate flesh everywhere.

de l'estoupement des oreilles
On the blockage of the ears

Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.
Everything that falls into the ears is one of four things: either grains, or an animal, or a stone from a mine or similar thing like iron; or seeds, such as jet, beans, peas; or flowing things such as water and vinegar and similar things.

Quant il chiet en l'oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s'ajoste mie a l'oreille, ne ne croist en l'oreille, si met l'oreille au solel.
When a stone or other kind of thing that doesn't stick to the ear or grow in the ear falls into the ear, put the ear in the sun.

Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d'oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l'oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l'oreille au desus.
If you see the stone, then drip a little violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and make him sneeze with condisi, and block his nostrils when the sneeze comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and stretch the ear upwards.

Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s'elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:
Many times it comes out by this treatment; and if it doesn't come out, administer extraction with fine tweezers, of which this is the form:

S'elle saut fuer as pinceures, c'est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l'oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s'elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d'arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l'oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n'i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s'elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.
If it jumps out with the tweezers, that's good; if not, then administer extraction with a fine hook of small curvature; and if it doesn't come out by this, make a brass tube and push the head of the tube into the ear hole firmly, and block what is around the tube with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the tube; then pull it out strongly, for many times it comes out as we have said; and if it doesn't come out in this way, take glue with which birds are caught, and put it on the end of some instrument that is suitable for this purpose, and put a little cotton around it; then press the glue on the stone or whatever it is, and pull it out.

Et s'elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l'oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l'oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l'oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l'oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu'il soit sanez.
And if it doesn't come out from all these things we have said, then hasten to split the ear before a hot abscess comes there, and spasm; and the manner of the splitting is that you first bleed the patient from the cephalic vein, and draw blood according to the measure of his strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn his ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear at the fat in the dependent place; and let the incision be like a crescent, until you come to the stone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck it quickly with your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.

Et se c'est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si'il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:
And if it is grains that are in there and they swell, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer a thin, fine spatula according to this form:

et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l'oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l'estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.
and administer incision of that grain. But do not do this when you think that the grain is moist from the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with fine tweezers and by sucking, as we have said, so that the extraction is facilitated.

En l'aigue donques que chiet en l'oreille covient que li malaides use d'esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l'oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s'elle saut fuer per ceu, c'est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertuis de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d'autre part, et fiere d'une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l'oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l'un des chiés en l'oreille, et l'autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d'autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.
For water that falls into the ear, it is necessary that the patient first use sneezing with condisi, and fill the ear with old cotton. And let him lie on that same ear where the water is. If it comes out by this, that's good. If not, then take many stones according to the length of your finger, thin and light, and heat them a little in the fire; and let the patient put one in the hole of his ear, and jump on one of his feet on the other side, and strike another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not cease to do this from stone to stone until all the water comes out, and thus it all comes out; and if you want, take a reed, and put one of the ends in the ear, and set the other end on fire until most of the reed is burned; then do the same with other reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said for the stone.

En l'estraction de la beste, s'elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s'elle est de grant cors c'on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c'est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l'oreille.
For the extraction of an animal, if it is small-bodied, like a flea or similar thing, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large-bodied that one can feel it, then administer extraction with tweezers; and this is the easiest thing to remove that is in the ear.

En l'estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l'oreille au soleil: s'il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s'il n'aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:
For the extraction of worms generated in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and in the treatise on distillations, and the treatment does not profit, it is necessary that you look at the ear in the sun: if any worms appear, then pull them out with fine tweezers, and if they do not appear, then take the tube of which this is the form:

Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l'oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s'il n'obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j'ai dit en la piere; et s'il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l'ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l'oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:
And let it be narrow below and wide above. And push the finest end into the ear according to the amount of suffering of the patient, then suck strongly with the whole tube; do this often until all the worms come out. And if they do not obey to come out, then block around the tube with cotton as I have said for the stone; and if they do not jump out as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have tested in killing worms, and you will find them in the treatise on distillations; and distill your oils and your medicines into the ear with this instrument, of which this is the form as you see:

Et soit d'argent ou d'arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d'arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l'oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l'oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c'on la distille en l'oreille; et garde qu'elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.
And let it be of silver or brass, narrow below with a small hole, and open above for distilling; and to press the distillation inside use a brass instrument well made for this, and if you want take a razor and wrap cotton suitably around the point; then pour your oil or your juice, and what you want of your medicines into the tube, and let the tube be in the ear; then push the razor with all the cotton inside, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled into the depth of the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillation be a little heated in the fire before it is distilled into the ear; and make sure it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.

de l'estoupement des oreilles
On the blockage of the ears

Aucun enfant naissent qui n'ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l'oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l'oreille, si c'on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.
Some children are born who have no hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to men through blockage of a wound, or from flesh grown inside the ear, and this blockage sometimes comes deep in the ear, so that one cannot see it; and sometimes it happens a little outside the hole, and one can see it well.

Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c'on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c'on voit covient que tu mettes l'oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l'opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:
That which comes deep, so that one cannot see it, is of difficult healing in many dispositions, and in that which one can see, it is necessary that you put the patient's ear in the sun; and look inside: if you see the apparent blockage, open it with this spatula of which this is the form:

Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu'il ne blece l'oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l'oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.
And let it be sharp and cutting in front and behind all flat, so that it does not wound the ear; if the blockage is from flesh grown in the body of the ear, hold it with fine tweezers, and cut it lightly, until all that flesh is removed.

Et se li opilations est em parfont en l'oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l'eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l'oreille. Se tu sens l'opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l'oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l'oreille; puis met en l'oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l'oignement egyptien.
And if the blockage is deep in the ear, take a fine light razor and heat it a little in the fire, then put it in the body of the ear. If you feel the blockage from which the patient feels difficulty in hearing, pierce lightly, and be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear; then put a tent in the ear according to the width of the hole, and moisten it in Egyptian ointment.

Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l'oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d'oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu'il soit sanez.
Do this for some days until the wound is healed, or take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder it with ground vitriol; and if you see the ear swollen, it is necessary that you remove the tent and replace it with another tent moistened in a cerote made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then treat it until it is healed.

Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l'oreille, et use d'autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.
And if bleeding occurs, plunge a sponge and cloths in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding which are in the treatise on distillations.

de la char des papieres
On the flesh of the eyelids

Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d'un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.
These althelul that come on the eyelids of the eyes when they are moist and are dry, it is necessary that you stretch them with tongs and tweezers, and cut them from their roots with a spatula; then put ground vitriol on the place.

Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l'incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.
And if blood flows from it, cauterize it with a fine lenticular cautery, and cauterizing after the incision is better; and many times they return, when something remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not come back.

de la gresle
On hail

Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d'une part et d'autre, et c'est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l'escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.
Many times come on the eyelids of the eyes things that resemble hail in their form and in their hardness, and for this this disease is called "grandine", and it is a gathering of thick moisture in the eyelid above and below; the procedure is this: observe if the grandine moves from one side to the other, and this is an easy thing to know; then split it widely, then scrape each part lightly, then take it with tweezers, and cut it.

se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l'assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu'ele soit sanee; et s'elle est petite, si n'i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.
If you cannot cut it without piercing the eyelid a little, it does not harm the patient; and if the split is large, bring it together with a suture, and treat it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not force it, for the ointment restores it immediately and generates flesh.

Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l'oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d'une part et d'autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l'incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l'oil d'aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.
And if the grandine is descending to the inside of the ear towards the upper part, invert the eyelid, and stretch the grandine with tweezers, and cut it and press it on one side and the other; and if the eyelid is separated by the incision, this does not matter; and when the grandine is cut, wash the eye with salt water, and treat the place with that which generates flesh until the patient is healed.

de la graisse des eulz
On the fat of the eyes

Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c'a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l'exinach qui apert en l'oil.
Exinach is a fat that is generated in the membranes of the upper eyelids, and this happens more to children than to any people, and greatly harms their eyes, and catarrh comes to them in the mornings, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes; and for this they lie on their faces always, and sleep on them, and their eyelids under their eyebrows are moist which the swelling and the appearance have covered with the exinach which appears in the eye.

Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l'exirnach entr'ous.
And when you press the place with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.

Et li maniere de l'ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d'un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d'une part et d'autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c'on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l'exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d'une piece de graisse blainche.
And the manner of the procedure is that the patient put his head in your lap; and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains exinach on each side, then put it on him; and press with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the exinach is gathered in the middle of the circle; then split in the middle of the moisture with a cutting spatula a wide split, and let it not be larger than the wound that one makes for bleeding a vein; and split the skin deeply until you come to the exinach; and in many dispositions exinach comes from the split, in the form of a piece of white fat.

Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu'il soit espars; et garde que tu n'ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc'a l'oil, que tu ne le bleces.
Extract it then with a piece of lint cloth between your fingers to the outside, and turn your hand to the right and to the left until it is spread; and be careful not to add to the split, that you do not come with the spatula all the way to the eye, that you do not wound it.

Et se li exirnach n'apert en l'encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu'il apere; puis l'estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz. Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu'il soit sanez. Et s'il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d'emplaustres assouajant tant qu'il soit sanez.
And if the exinach does not appear at the beginning of the split, increase the split a little lightly until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then moisten cloths in vinegar and water, and put on the place, and tighten with bandages. And there are such men who grind salt and put it on to corrupt that moisture which has remained. Then treat it until it is healed. And if a hot abscess comes to the place, treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed.

des poilz des papieres
On the hairs of the eyelids

Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c'est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu'il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.
When hairs grow on eyelids other than the natural ones, and are old, they harm the eyes, and cause kinds of diseases such as habitual tears and softening of the eyelids and albugo, so much that it is a cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the treatment is according to four ways: either by cautery with fire, or by sharp medicine according to what is before in the chapter on cautery, and is done either by incision and suture or by tubes, according to what I will say.

Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l'oil a ta main senestre; s'elle est convertie, c'est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc'au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d'enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.
It is necessary that you put the patient's head in your lap, then turn the eyelid of the eye to your left hand; if it is turned, that is good; if not, then push a needle with a thread above; and let this be beside the margin of the eyelid where the hairs grow beside these hairs, and draw a thread above with all the eyelid, and turn it to the razor; then split in the part below the eyelid, below the added hairs, with all the cutting spatula, from the large tear duct to the small; then extract a thread, and put under the eyelid a small tent of cotton and cloth, then mark on the eyelid a figure of ink, like the leaf of myrtle, and however it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you want to raise the eyelid which is divided to all.

Et si a teil qui a mestier c'on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;
And there are some who need a large quantity of the eyelid to be cut according to how softened the eyelid is;

puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc'a petit;
then split with the spatula along the two lines you have marked, and begin from the large tear duct to the small one;

et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d'un raiz,
and let one of the incisions be near the natural eyelashes with the thickness of a ray,

puis boute l'oncine en l'un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l'escorche toute;
then push the hook into one of the two corners of the skin, then peel it all off;

puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d'une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc,
then join the two edges with a suture using a needle with a fine wool thread, and wipe away the blood,

et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n'en aies cure,
and make the excess threads stick to the two eyebrows with some sticky substances, if you want to do this; and if not, don't worry about it,

puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc'a .iij. jors ou .iiij.;
then leave the suture and threads for 3 or 4 days;

puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans,
then treat the wound without suture using drying and astringent substances,

car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l'assemblement de li,
because the eyelid rises up during the healing of the wound and its joining,

mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c'est ovraiges sens paor;
but the suture is better (as the ancients said), and this is a work without fear;

et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d'une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:
and there is another method: which is that you mark the eyelid with a figure that is like a myrtle leaf, as we have described, with 3 separate hooks according to the shape that is here:

puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:
then cut what protrudes with small scissors evenly according to the shape that is here:

Et se tu n'as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n'est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure;
And if you don't have the power to hold the forceps, and the thing is not even, then take a needle with a thread, and push it into the middle of the figure;

et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;
and push another thread next to the large tear duct, and the second thread next to the small one, and gather the threads evenly between your fingers;

puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit,
then raise your hand evenly, and lift all the skin on which you have marked, as we have described,

puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu'il soit sanez;
then join the two edges of the wound by suture, and treat it until it is healed;

et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l'apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;
and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with wax and similar soothing ointments;

et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l'incision;
and sometimes it happens that the eyelashes are inverted: so it is necessary that you use what we have said about the incision;

mais li costure en l'une et en l'autre est plus artificialz.
but the suture in both cases is more artificial.

Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j'ai dit,
The treatment of the cysts is according to this form: and it is that you invert the eyelid and split it inside according to what I have said,

et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;
and then make 2 canes by art, and 2 fine bands as long as the eyelid and the width of the spatula is;

et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz;
and cut at the two ends of the two parts where you hold the threads;

puis assemble l'un et l'autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l'oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment;
then join one and the other subtly on what protrudes from the eyelid of the eye, and tighten the two canes of the two parts strongly;

et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu'il cherra par lui.
and leave it like this for some days, and the skin that was tightened will die and blacken and rot, until it falls off by itself.

S'il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu'il soit sanez;
If it delays, cut it with scissors, then treat it until it is healed;

et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;
and when the wound is healed, and the eyelid is raised, and the eyelashes will no longer prick;

et c'est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:
and this is the form of the two canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:

li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil;
the work is such that you take a fine needle, and push a soft and fine silk thread into it;

puis assemble les chiés et noe l'un et l'autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;
then join the ends and knot one and the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm long;

puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;
then arrange in the chase another fine silk thread briefly, and knot the ends of the thread;

puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c'est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus,
then let the patient put his head in your lap; and let it be beside the sun so that the work is illuminated, for it is a subtle and delicate work,

puis boute l'aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;
then push the needle with the chase into the root of the added hair, and make it pierce the eyelid quickly until you pull it above the natural hair;

puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s'il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors;
then pull the hair up to the chase, and push that hair into the chase, if there are one or two or three or more;

puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.
then pull your hand until the hair comes out with the chase in the eyelid with the natural hair.

Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit,
And if the chase is pulled and the hair does not come out with it, you will pull the chase below with all the thread that you have arranged,

tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l'oil;
until the chase comes out of the hole above and you see it through the vision of the eye;

adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l'oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s'aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;
then you will pull the chase and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for 2 or 3 days, until the hair adheres in its place and the flesh grows over it;

et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu'il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.
and if the hair is small, accompany it with a long hair from the natural hair, and let it be raised with that one or leave it, until it is lengthened and then lift it.

de la porriture de l'oil
On the rotting of the eye

Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l'oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l'une natureil, et l'autre innatureil.
When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or rotting comes to the eye, there are two types: one natural, and the other unnatural.

Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.
And it happens by healing of a wound, or by cutting or cauterizing, and by similar things.

Et li maniere de l'ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu'elle soit sanee;
And the manner of working on it is that you split that healed area, and separate its edges, and put linen tents inside, and bind it until it is healed;

et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.
and it is not necessary that you use in its treatment things that dry and constrict.

Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;
For if you do this, the disease returns worse than the first;

mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l'arose d'aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites,
but work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and water or marshmallow and linseed should be cooked,

et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.
and diachylon ointment melted in some of the oils, and wrap a tent in it, and treat it with this.

Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu'ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu'elle fut devant;
And the treasure of your treatment is that you take care that it does not heal according to the form it was before;

et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu'elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu'elle fut devant.
and this work that we have spoken of is nothing but a correction of this disease, so that it does not return according to the form it was before.

de la char qui vient en l'oil
On the flesh that comes in the eye

Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.
This disease which is below which is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.

Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;
The accidental comes from wounds and splits and cauterization and similar things;

et li voie de l'ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char,
and the way of working on it is that you take a needle, in which there is a double thread, and stick it into the flesh,

et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c'a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char;
and make it pierce from the left tear duct to the right, so that the thread comes in two ends of the flesh;

puis estent la char au desus a tout l'aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.
then stretch the flesh above with the needle, and cut it with a wide spatula.

Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu'il covient, c'est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure,
And if the shape of the eyelid returns as it should, that's good; if not, take a razor and put it in the split,

et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;
and turn the eyelid, and split two splits on the inside side of the eyelid;

et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l'incision que tu as copeit,
and let the ends of the two splits be from the two angles of the incision that you have cut,

et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d'une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»;
and let an angle be made so that when they are assembled, the figure is like the figure of a letter which is called "Greek j";

puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere,
then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its sides are sharp below, from what follows the eyelid,

puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d'un fil de lainne;
then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a wool thread;

puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu'il soit sanez.
then treat it with what we have said about softening medicines, and with tents, until it is healed.

Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres,
And if the disease comes from a split or a suture or cauterization, it is necessary that you split a full split under the eyelashes,

et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d'une tente, si com j'ai dit;
and according to what is before; then separate between the two edges with a tent, as I have said;

et doit on faire l'ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme,
and one should do the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form,

et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;
and the wise master prepares skill with all his power how to make the figure return to its natural form;

et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu'il i covient d'ovraige et d'estrumens em plusors dispositions.
and the patient himself, according to what is needed in terms of work and instruments in various conditions.

dou soudement de la papiere
On the welding of the eyelid

Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l'oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez,
When this welding happens to many men in such a way that the upper eyelid is welded to the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions,

si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d'un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;
it is then necessary that you push the point of a razor under the eyelid, and lift it up;

et l'estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans,
and stretch it with tweezers, until you cut what is attached with a fine spatula, which should not be too sharp or too cutting,

si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l'oil;
so that the patient cannot suffer that the too sharp spatula does not injure the eye;

et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;
and let your incision, with which you peel off that joining, be light, so that the eyelid returns to its natural form;

et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l'oil aigue salee, et le leve d'aigue douce, et de coliere;
and all that joining is healed, and sometimes they put salt water in the eye, and wash it with fresh water, and with eye lotion;

puis met entre la papiere et l'oil une tente de lin, et met sus l'oil laine moillie en abun d'uef;
then put a linen tent between the eyelid and the eye, and put wool moistened in egg white on the eye;

et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu'il soit sanez.
and after the third day use eye lotion and welding substances until it is healed.

de l'ungle de l'oil
On the unguis of the eye

Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n'est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee,
Know that the unguis is of two types: it is sinewy and similar to a hard membrane, and another which is not sinewy, but is similar to congealed white moisture,

que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;
that when one touches it with iron and thinks to take it with tweezers, one cannot;

et l'une et l'autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu'ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l'oil.
and both types begin near the large tear duct, and grow little by little until they cover all the sight and all the light and the movement of the eye.

Et li maniere de l'incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;
And the manner of incision is that the patient puts his head in your lap, then you open his eyes;

et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l'ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l'estent au desus;
and lift the eyelid with your hand, then gather the unguis with tweezers of small doubling, and stretch it above;

puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort;
then take a needle, and put in it a horse hair, or cow hair, or ox hair, and a strong thread;

et double la pointe de l'aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l'ungle, et la perce a tout l'aguille,
and double the point of the needle a little and stick it in the middle of the unguis, and pierce it with the needle,

et lie l'ungle d'un fil et l'estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l'ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc'au chief,
and tie the unguis with a thread and stretch it above, and peel with the hair the side of the unguis that follows the pupil and its hair to the end,

puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces,
then cut the remainder at the root of the tear duct with the fine spatula and with small scissors,

et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l'incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;
and leave the natural flesh in the tear duct, so that through the incision the flow of tears does not come habitually;

et aucune fois s'estent li ungle a l'oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;
and sometimes the unguis extends to the hook only, and to the thread, as we have said;

puis l'escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:
then one peels it with the gentle spatula of which here is the form:

Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;
And take care that the spatula does not touch the fleshy membrane and break it, and that the pupil is not pierced;

et aprés l'incision giete en l'oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc'a l'autre jor;
and after the incision throw in the eye a little ground salt, and eye lotion made of litharge, and leave it until the next day;

puis le cure de ceu qu'il i covient tant qu'il soit sanez.
then treat it with what is necessary until it is healed.

Et se li ungle n'est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l'aguille, et li uncines n'i puet entrer,
And if the unguis is not sinewy, and you cannot push the needle, and the hooks cannot enter,

maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d'ungle de medicines;
many times this type of unguis is cured with medicines;

et naissent sicom j'ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l'oil dou malaide,
and they grow as I have told in the division, and if you want to cut it, open the patient's eye,

et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:
and take the light spatula a little sharp according to this form:

Et reis l'ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu'elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse,
And shave the unguis above subtly, and if you see that it diminishes at all and the shaving presses on it,

si distille de ta bouche en l'oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet,
then drip from your mouth into the eye eye lotion made of litharge and red eye lotion and ground salt,

et estoupe l'oil jusc'a l'autre jor; puis rencomence l'autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu'elle soit toute ostee.
and stop up the eye until the next day; then restart the other work according to this same procedure, until it is all removed.

Se aucune chose ne t'est contraire en l'oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait,
If nothing is contrary to you in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then leave it,

et cure premier l'aposteme chaut tant qu'il soit sanez, puis rencomence l'ovraige si com devant, tant qu'il soit sanez.
and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then restart the work as before, until it is healed.

Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l'oil par grant nuisement,
And if the appearance of the flesh of the tear duct harms the eye greatly,

si la sospent a l'oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n'i viegne;
then suspend it with the hook, and cut a part of it and not all, so that the flow of tears does not come;

puis distille en l'oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.
then drip into the eye red eye lotion which is made of litharge.

de la char qui naist sus la prunelle
On the flesh that grows on the pupil

Es eulz d'aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer,
In the eyes of some men sometimes red flesh grows, and covers the pupil and tightens on the eyelids and turns them outward,

et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz,
and looks like a pomegranate flower; and the procedure is that the patient puts his head in your lap, then you open his eyes,

et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;
and gather all that flesh with hooks suitable for this, and support it with force;

puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc'a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l'oil a l'ovraige;
then cut the first flesh, and go cutting everything with the razor to the end, and be careful not to injure the eye in the procedure;

et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l'incision de l'ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel,
and let the incision of the spatula be as we have said in the incision of the unguis and with small scissors with which one removes the pannus,

si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char,
as the form after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is completed and all the flesh removed,

si emple l'oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives,
then fill the eye with ground salt or drip into it red eye lotion and similar corrosive medicines,

et met sus l'oil defuer coton avec abin d'uef, si qu'il soit asseurez d'aposteme chaut;
and put on the outside of the eye cotton with egg white, so that it is protected from hot abscess;

et s'il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut,
and if anything remains, and hot blood overcomes you, and you fear hot abscess,

si laisse l'oil et cure l'aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;
then leave the eye and treat the abscess with things that soothe hot abscess;

puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu'il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l'oil par ceste semblance.
then return to your work until it is healed, and do this when flesh is added to the eye in this manner.

Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;
But always it is necessary that you lighten the treatment of each weak eye by the natural way;

et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.
and by the accidental way, in work of iron; and do not push your hand in any of these procedures until you see that this member can suffer that procedure.

des voines des eulz
On the veins of the eyes

Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l'oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l'oil toz jors.
Pannus are red veins that are covered on the eye, and take away from the sight its function and weaken the eye always.

Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n'i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;
It is necessary then first that you look if the eye, in which pannus is, is strong, and there is no other disease except the pannus;

adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu'il mette son chief en ton sain,
then gather it in this manner: command the patient to put his head in your lap,

puis sospent celles voines a tout l'oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:
then suspend those veins with the hook according to his wisdom, and let the hooks be fine double according to this form:

Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:
And let there be two hooks by degrees in one body according to this form:

puis c'on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre,
then one gathers with scissors those veins subtly, and wipes the blood hour after hour,

tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l'oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l'oil as pointes des spatumiles,
until you see removing those veins out of the eye; and take care that you do not injure the eye with the points of the spatulas,

et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;
and do this work at the hour of noon before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you cut only those veins;

et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l'oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.
and when you have done this, then drip into the eye green and red eye lotion to corrupt what remains of the pannus.

Et se tu n'as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l'oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz,
And if you do not have the power to gather all this in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye of things soothing the pain of the eyes,

et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d'aposteme chaut,
and leave it some days until the pain is soothed and it is protected from hot abscess,

puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu'il soit sanez; et c'est li forme des forces:
then restart according to this manner which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of the scissors:

de la fistule de l'oil
On the fistula of the eye

Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j'ai devant dit,
The doctors call "arissati" fistula: when you treat it by cautery and by sharp burning medicine according to what I have said before,

et elle n'est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l'aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer,
and it is not healed, then it is a trick in it that you split on the abscess, there where it should mature,

et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.
and draw out all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.

Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l'estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:
And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, scrape it with the instrument of which here is the form; and it is called "rough head", and should be made of Indian iron with a round head, and should be pointed like a file as it is in the present form:

Et met sus lou leu de l'os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;
And put it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that this corruption is scraped;

et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.
and do this sometimes, then restore the place with drying medicines.

se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n'est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n'i vient, saiches qu'il est sanez;
If the place is healed, and flesh grows there, and the body of the pus is healed, and remains so for 40 days, and it does not renew and is not swollen, and no bad accidents come, know that it is healed;

se ceu non, si n'i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l'os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues,
if not, there is no other trick than to bring back the fistula to the hole of the nerve according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time by iron, and by sharp medicines,

et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc'a chief si com tu vois ci:
and when it will be uncovered then take a drill according to this form, and let the head be of iron with 3 angles, and the shaft be thinned to the end as you see here:

puis le met sus l'os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l'oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu'il perce l'os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s'il tient sa main sus son neif;
then put it on the bone next to the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then turn with all the drill until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it by the wind that comes out if he holds his hand on his nerve;

et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t'ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.
and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and the place hardens, so goes the matter to the nerve; so it is an easier thing for the patient.

de l'issue de l'oil
On the protrusion of the eye

Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement,
When the eye appears completely outside, and there comes no disturbance to the nerve, nor diminishment,

si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier,
it is necessary that you bind the patient; then bleed him, then put cupping glasses on the nape of the neck without striking to suck,

puis met sus l'oil .i. liien fait d'acaice et de aloe et d'encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l'oil, et l'emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;
then put on the eye a bandage made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolla, and then tighten the eye, and plaster it with bands and cloths;

et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l'un sus l'autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;
and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths soft enough, and double each in 4, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye needs;

puis l'estrain par desus d'un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;
then tighten it above with a hard band strongly, and restart the cupping glasses to suck without striking;

puis oste les ventouses et laisse l'oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l'estraignes mout;
then remove the cupping glasses and leave the eye tightened day and night, and if the bandage softens, it is necessary that you tighten it much;

puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l'oil repairier, c'est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l'emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu'il soit sanez.
then remove the bandage after the day and night, and if you see the eye returning, that's good; if not; then restart the plaster and the cloths and the bandage and the cupping glasses until it is healed.

dou derrompement de toile uvee
On the tearing of the uveal membrane

Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;
When tearing comes in the uveal membrane, then appears, and comes out of the eyelids like a grape, and is frightful to see;

adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc'a celi desus,
then if you want to cut it, the procedure is such that you push a needle into the root from the lower part to the upper part,

puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;
then push another needle where there is a double thread from the part of the tear duct; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the disposition;

puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l'uve entor, et l'estraint bien, puis estrai l'aguille et met sus l'oil lainne moillie en abun d'uef;
then cut the place of the double thread and tie a part of the uvea around, and tighten it well, then pull out the needle and put on the eye wool moistened in egg white;

et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l'uve, puis cure l'oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;
and leave it until the thread falls with the uvea, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed;

et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l'uve chescune part d'un cercle de drap, tant qu'elle soit sanee.
and sometimes the wound is restrained by the uvea each part with a circle of cloth, until it is healed.

Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l'oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;
And if the eye gives great appearance, then pierce it with the fine spatula that comes deep into the eye, and let the albuminous moisture run and the eye descend, and enter in immediately;

puis l'estrai tant qu'il soit sanez.
then pull it out until it is healed.

de la bowe de l'oil
On the pus of the eye

Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l'oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n'est mie aigue;
This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but pus which is gathered in the eye, similar to descending water, and this is not water;

et li maniere de l'apparance de l'ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit,
and the manner of the appearance of the procedure is that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat,

puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;
then take the head between your hands from 2 sides, and move it until you see the pus come to the top to your eyes;

puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;
then let it be fixed in, and not descend and let the light be cleared, and let the patient see things as he used to;

et s'elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c'est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n'est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.
and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the pus is not prepared as we have said.

si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone,
then make the patient sit between your hands, then take the fine spatula and split on the corneal membrane a little by the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corneal membrane and the corona,

tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l'oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel,
until the pus comes out; and when it has come out, then drip into the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water where fenugreek is boiled and honey,

puis soit curee d'autre cure tant qu'elle soit sanee.
then let it be treated with other treatment until it is healed.

des aigues de l'oil
On the waters of the eye

Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu'il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.
We already have the appearances of the waters in the division, and what is necessary for piercing; so work on it according to health.

Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil,
It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, out of the light because of the sun,

et li lie l'oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l'oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;
and bind the healthy eye and tighten very strongly; then put the eyelid of the eye to your left hand if the eye is left, or to your right hand if the eye is right;

puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l'estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;
then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument which is called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is right;

puis met la pointe de l'estrument delez la corone par la groissece d'un rait en celle blenchor de l'oil a la partie dou menor larmier,
then put the point of the instrument next to the corona by the thickness of a ray in that whiteness of the eye at the part of the smaller tear duct,

puis boute l'estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu'il perce en la blenchor de l'oil,
then push the instrument which is called "almagda" powerfully, and turn your hand until it pierces in the whiteness of the eye,

et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l'espaice qui est des la prunele jusc'a la fin de la noirour;
and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the path of almagda be at the depth of the measure from the space which is from the pupil to the end of the blackness;

et c'est li corone de l'oil; si verras l'os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee,
and this is the corona of the eye; so you will see the bone in that eyelid because of the clarity of the corneal membrane,

et pues met l'estrument jusc'a leu ou li aigue est, puis l'espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.
and then put the instrument to the place where the water is, then press it below one way after another.

se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l'estrument en son oil.
if the water descends now, so the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.

Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l'estrument,
Afterwards rest a little, and if the water rises again the second time, put it out with the instrument,

et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;
and when it is fixed in and it does not rise, then pull out almagda lightly by turning your hand little by little;

et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l'oil dedens.
and then put back in water a little rock salt, and wash the eye inside with this.

Puis met par defuer l'oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d'uef, et lie avec l'oil sain.
Then put outside the eye tow or wool moistened in rose oil and in egg white, and bind with the healthy eye.

Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d'uef.
We, and those who are of our time, put on ground cumin with egg white.

Et se almagda n'i puet entrer en l'oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz,
And if almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are such men who have too hard eyes,

si covient que tu preignes l'estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:
it is necessary that you take the instrument which is called "alberit", of which here is the form:

Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n'aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;
And then pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make a subtle place, then push in almagda, as we have said;

et au complissement de l'uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous;
and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a suitable dormitory, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place;


et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc'a tier jor;
And let him be restricted from all movements, and take light foods, and not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and be bound according to his condition until the third day;

puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc'a septime jor;
then unbind him in that same dark house, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day;

et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l'oure de la cure ou aprés l'incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.
and it is not necessary that you do this at the time of the treatment or immediately after the incision, but it is necessary that you relieve this, because the water rises quickly.

se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l'oil devant le septime jor, et l'adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;
If a hot swelling comes, that you unbind the eye before the seventh day, and treat it with that which soothes swelling;

et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.
and when it is calmed, unbind the sight and put a pillow on his face to cover for some days, and let him remain in that dark house.

Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.
And then let him leave the house little by little, and return to his affairs; and know that no disciple should interfere in this case.

 Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l'aigue, mais toutevoie je n'en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c'est une novele chose.
 And one came to us who was from Iraq, who told us that in his country they made pierced almagda, with which one sucks the water, but nevertheless I never saw any in our land, nor did I ever read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.

Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d'arain proprement:
And these are the appearances of the forms of almagda, so that those who do not know them may see them; and let them be made of brass properly:

Et soient li chief d'aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.
And let their heads be of this same subtlety, and the last in three sharp angles.

de la char sor le neis
Of the flesh on the nose

Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.
Sometimes various added fleshes grow on the nose, of which there are some that resemble scorpions with many feet; and there are some where there is cancerous flesh of dark color, and there is soft flesh of good color.

En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l'oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;
Therefore, for that of these fleshes which is soft, and not cancerous, it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open his nostrils, and throw the hook at those fleshes, and pull them out;

pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d'une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.
then cut what you can support with the subtle spatula sharp on one side, until you know that all that flesh is removed.

Et s'il en remaint aucune chose c'on ne puisse coper, si l'ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu'il n'i demoure rien;
And if there remains anything that cannot be cut, then open it with all of the subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains;

et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c'est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.
and if blood overwhelms you, or hot swelling, then help it as is necessary; and if it is a malignant swelling, then hasten and cauterize it until the blood is stanched and all the fleshes are removed, then throw vinegar and water or wine into the nose.

Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc'a palais, saiches qu'il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu'il i a char nee en l'os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:
If the nose opens, and moisture comes to the palate, know that it is healed; and if moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is flesh born on the bone above, which the instrument does not come to cut:

adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d'espaice .i. doit ou moins;
then it is necessary that you push in a somewhat thick linen thread, and let it be knotted with fewer knots, and have between each knot a space of one finger or less;

et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu'il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;
and let the patient put the end of the thread in his nose to the best of his ability, and pull while smelling until it comes through the nose into the mouth;

et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c'est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;
and many times children do this in schools, and it is an easy thing for one who wants to do it;

puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l'autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l'autre main, et saiche l'un aprés l'autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.
then hold the end that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and pull one after the other while sawing at the knots that are on the thread.

Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;
Do this until you know that the knots have corrupted that flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe the blood, and wet the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nose as before;

fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu'il soit sanez, et s'il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;
do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of flesh; and then put a lead tube in the nose for some days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, then use them;

et c'est li forme de l'estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:
and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, with which one distills oils and medicines in the nose:

Et soit d'argent ou d'arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;
And let it be of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and the conduit also; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be full for purging the head;

et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l'oile ou aucune liquor.
and have a handle at the end to hold it when one heats the oil or any liquid.

de la char sor le neis
Of the flesh on the nose

Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu'il est vis chose au regarder;
Many times a disease called "telul" is born at the tip of the nose, and it grows and becomes large continuously, so much that it is a living thing to look at;

et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l'oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;
and for this reason it is necessary that you cut it at the beginning, and remove it all out, then put on the place the cautery or the burning medicine;

et s'on le tarde a coper tant qu'il soit grans, si pren warde s'il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c'est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;
and if one delays cutting it until it is large, then take care if it is hard, of dark color, of poor sense: do not touch it with iron because it is a cancerous swelling, for when one cuts it sometimes, great harm comes to the patient;

et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c'on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.
and if the swelling is of soft touch, not of dark color, and you see that one can cut it all, then empty the patient and cut it without fear, and treat the place with drying and astringent things.

quant li neis est copez et cosus
When the nose is cut and sewn

Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.
Know that when solutions of continuity come in one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men.

Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu'il soit sanez;
It is necessary therefore when this happens to someone, to look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips with a suture, then treat it until it is healed;

et se les levres sont ja desevrees d'une part et d'autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu'elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l'estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;
and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape all the parts of their skin until they bleed, then assemble the two lips with a suture, and tighten it, and powder over it powder of dragon's blood, and ground incense;

et met sus les poudres une piece d'emplaustre de fort ou d'autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu'il chiece par lui, puis le cure d'oignement tant qu'il soit sanez.
and put on the powders a piece of strong plaster or other soldering plaster, and leave it until it falls by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.

Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t'ai fait savoir.
The manner of the suture is that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the suture of the belly; or by thread, as I have made you know.

des apostemes des levres
Of the swellings of the lips

A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;
To many men there comes inside the lips a hard swelling, resembling grains of vetches, and smaller and larger;

adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;
then it is necessary that you turn the lips, and split over each knot, and take it with tweezers and cut it in each part;

puis emple lou leu aprés l'incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d'aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu'il soit sanez.
