then fill the place after the incision with ground vitriol, until the blood is stanched; and then wash it with vinegar, and treat the place with dry things until it is healed.

de la char des gencives
Of the flesh of the gums

Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;
Many times added flesh grows on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus";

si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;
so it is necessary that you support it with tongs, and cut it at its root, and let the pus or blood run;

puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l'incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;
then put ground vitriol on the place, or other astringent and desiccative powders; and if that flesh comes back after the incision, and many times it happens, then cut it the second time, and cauterize it: so it does not come back after the cautery;

et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.
and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.

des sordens
Of the tartar

Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;
Sometimes there are gathered at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scales that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and citrus-colored and green, so much that the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth are stinking;

si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu'il n'i demore rien;
so it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his head be in your lap, and scrape the teeth where the scales appear, until nothing remains;

et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu'elles soient mondees;
and do the same for the blackness and the greenness, and the yellowness and other stains, until they are cleaned;

et s'on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c'est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;
and if one removes what is there at the first scraping, that's good; if not, then start scraping again the second day and the third, until you have scraped everything;

et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d'estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;
and know that the teeth need various forms of instruments for scraping, according to what the work demonstrates, because the scrapers with which one scrapes outside the teeth have other forms than those with which one scrapes between the teeth;

et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.
and these forms and others should be prepared with you.

Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;
It is necessary when you treat the tooth for its pain that you delay pulling it as long as you can, for one should not do this;

car c'est une substance mout haute jusc'a donc c'on n'ait point d'excusation dou raier.
because it is a very high substance until one has no excuse for scraping.

Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.
Then when the patient is constrained to pull, it is necessary that you be certain of the aching tooth.

Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu'elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;
Many times the pain deceives the patient, and he thinks it is in the healthy tooth, and has the good tooth pulled;

et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l'avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;
and yet the pain does not depart because of this, until the bad one is extracted, for we have already seen this done to these lords;

et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;
and when you are very certain of the aching tooth, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth with a strong spatula to protect the gum on all sides;

puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu'il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;
then move it with your fingers or with subtle pliers at first little by little, until it is well loosened, then firmly affix the pliers;

et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu'il ne se mueve.
and let the head of the patient be in your lap between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.

Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s'il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.
After extract the tooth straight without breaking, and if it does not come out, then take one of these instruments and push it inside on each side lightly, and move it as you did at first.

Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l'emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;
And if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, it is necessary that you fill it with cloths, there where the holes are;

et si l'estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l'estraindre;
and so tighten it subtly with pliers, that it does not break when tightening;

et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.
and it is necessary to work very wisely around the gum to loosen the tooth.

Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.
And take good care that you do not break it, and a part remains, and greater pains than the first come back to the patient through the malice of the root.

Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n'i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;
And take care that you do not do as the ignorant healers do, who by their haste and by their boldness sometimes break the jaw, and do not administer what we have told;

mais font venir aucune fois par l'oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu'il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;
but sometimes bring about by the occasion of this great illness because of the roots that remain, or because of the jaw that they break, as we have often seen;

et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d'aisil et de seil;
and when the tooth is pulled, wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt;

et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;
and if bleeding comes, which often happens, then fill the place with ground vitriol;

et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.
and if that is not enough, then cauterize it.

Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu'il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:
The forms of the instruments, with which one moves the teeth first, should be with long points and thick handles, that they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:

Et soient de gros membres si qu'il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.
And let them be of thick parts so that they do not bend when pulling, and let them be of well-made Indian iron, and let them be toothed for better holding.

de la racine des dens
Of the root of the teeth

Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis,
When the root remains after pulling, it is necessary that you put on the place cotton moistened in butter for one or two days, until the place is softened,

pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c'est li forme:
then push in the pliers which are called "algefri", of which the head resembles a swan's beak; and let them be made inside like a file and this is the form:

Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l'estrument qui est apelez «althali», c'est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:
And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and put there the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say lever, of which here is the form:

Et soit fors et gros si qu'il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c'est boin; se ceu non, si t'aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:
And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root comes out by this, that's good; if not, then help yourself with all the instruments, of which the forms come hereafter:

Et si s'aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:
And one helps oneself with this instrument which has two prongs, of which here is the form:

et d'autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:
and of other iron tools which are in front in the scraping of the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pliers, of which here is the form:

Et soit cist estrumens fors qu'il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d'estrumens de dens sont;
And let this instrument be strong so that it cannot break, and know that there are many dental instruments;

et ausi d'autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre,
and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise subtle master finds by himself his instrument, according to what his work and the disease demonstrate to him,

car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n'enseignerent point d'estrument por la diversiteit d'au;s et s'om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu'il i covient, que je t'ai dit, et t'aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:
for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach any instrument because of their diversity; and if one breaks any of the jaw or other bones, or it rots, then search with the instruments that are necessary, which I have told you, and help yourself with the forceps, of which here is the form:

Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l'os, qu'il n'eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;
And let them be thick and well-holding to hold the bone, that it does not escape, but can hold and remove it;

et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s'il ait en l'os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:
and then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is rot in the bone, and it is small, then scrape it with all this instrument:

Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n'est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie;
When the teeth appear not according to the natural body, and the form is ugly, and especially in virgin women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth is born after the tooth, and is not in the right place, and one cannot saw nor file it: then scrape it;

et s'il est aers avec lou dent, si pren cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:
and if it is attached to the tooth, then take this instrument of which here is the form, and it resembles a small beak, and let it be of Indian iron sharp at the top:

Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres,
And cut it little by little over several days because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others,

et s'il est apparans c'on le puisse limer, si lou lime d'une teil lime com ci est li forme:
and if it appears that one can file it, then file it with such a file as here is the form:

et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu'il ne se mueve tant qu'il chiece;
and it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and file the tooth little by little over several days lightly, so that it does not move until it falls;

puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l'aspreteit tant qu'il soit igalz, si qu'il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.
then smooth it at the end with any scraper, and if the tooth is too sharp and it hurts the tongue, it is necessary to file the roughness until it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue nor corrupt speech.

quant li dent lochent
When the teeth are loose

Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu'il menjue qu'il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;
When the front teeth are loose, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on what he eats without them falling, and you have treated them with astringent medicines, and this is not enough;

si les covient restraindre d'un fil d'or, car li filz d'argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;
then it is necessary to tighten them with a gold thread, for the silver thread becomes green and rots, but gold never changes;

et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l'espaice entre les dens;
and let the thread be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth;

et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s'il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc'au dent sain d'autre part;
and if you want to straighten the teeth, then take the thread and push it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the ends between the moved teeth, if there are one or more, until you come wisely to the healthy tooth on the other side;

puis rencomence la coverture jusc'a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu'il ne se mueve point;
then restart the covering up to the part where you began, and tighten your hand subtly and wisely, so that it does not move at all;

et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu'il ne puist eschaper.
and let your binding be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.

Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu'il ne blece la lengue;
Then cut the ends of the thread with pliers, and assemble them, and hide them between the healthy tooth, and put it so that it does not hurt the tongue;

et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s'il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l'estraint d'un autre fil;
and then leave it thus tight as long as it can remain, and if it unties, or the thread breaks, then tighten it with another thread;

si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c'est li forme des dens et li figure de l'adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:
It will remain and serve thus for all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the alignment of the two healthy teeth, and of the two molars, as you see:

Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s'en entremette mie qui n'est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d'un dent d'os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l'estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.
And when the tooth falls out, one puts it back in its place, fresh to fresh, as we have said; and let not one who is not wise and patient meddle with it, and sometimes one makes the form of a tooth from cow bone, and puts it in the place where there is a defect, and tightens it as we have said, and it remains and serves thus for a long time.

de coper lou liien de la lengue
On cutting the tie of the tongue

Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c'est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l'uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l'artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d'aigue rose et d'aisil, ou d'aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.
Sometimes this tie that comes under the tongue is natural, that one is born thus; or by accident of a healed wound; and the procedure is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and have his head in your lap, and lift his tongue; then cut the nervous tie widely, until the tongue is freed from its attachment, and if there is hardness or a knot, and it is from the healing of a wound, then push in the hook and cut that tie widely; and be careful that the cut is not too deep, because of the artery that is beneath; and when you have done this, wash the area with rose water and vinegar, or with cold water, then put a linen tent under the tongue; and let the patient keep it there each night, so that the area cannot heal.

Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d'autre cure tant qu'il soit sanez, et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n'i touchier point, car c'est chancre; et s'il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l'oncine, et lou fent d'un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d'une part et d'autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu'il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d'aisil et de seil, et le cure d'autres cures tant qu'il soit sanez.
And if bleeding occurs, put ground vitriol on the area; and if the blood overcomes you, cauterize it with the lenticular cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed, and if you see it is of false color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is cancer; and if it is tending to whiteness, and there is moisture, then throw in the hook, and split it with a fine spatula, and free it on one side and the other; and if the blood overcomes you in your work, put ground vitriol on it until it is stanched, then return to your work until you draw everything out; then wash the area with vinegar and salt, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.

des apostemes de la gorge
On abscesses of the throat

Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c'est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.
Sometimes lumps come inside the throat which are called "godath", and they are properly called the two tonsils, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then take note: if it is a hard abscess of little sensation and false color, do not touch it with iron.

Et s'il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu'il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s'il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l'estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.
And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron either, because of the bleeding; but leave it until it is ripe, and then you will separate it, or it will break on its own; and if it is of round white color, and the root is thin, then have the instrument ready for cutting, but first check if the hot abscess has settled and is calm.

Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l'estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d'argent ou d'arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:
Then have the patient sit before the sun, and his head should be in your lap, and open his mouth and have the assistant take it between his hands, and press the tongue down with the instrument, of which here is the form; and let it be of silver or fine brass like a knife:

Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l'aposteme, si pren l'oncine et lou fiche en l'amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l'estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l'un endroit l'autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d'andainne:
When you press the tongue with this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the hook and fix it in the tonsil, and draw it out above as much as you can; and draw some of the membranes with it, then cut it with the instrument, of which here is the form, which resembles scissors; and the ends are curved, and one opposite the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of Indian iron or steel:

Et se tu n'as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:
And if you do not have this instrument present, then cut it with pincers, of which here is the form:

Et soit trenchans d'une part, et d'autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l'une des amandres, si cope l'autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l'incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu'il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.
And let it be sharp on one side, and not on the other side; and when you have cut one of the tonsils, then cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision have the patient gargle with hot water, and water and vinegar, and if bleeding occurs, have the patient gargle water, or boiled pomegranate peels, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stanched; then treat it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses grow in the throat besides the two tonsils, so cut them then just like the two tonsils equally.

Et je medicinai une femme d'un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c'est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s'elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij.
And I treated a woman for an abscess that had grown inside her throat, that is to say an abscess of little sensation; and it had already nearly closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not exhale because the passage was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained thus for a day or two.

Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu'il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l'un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l'autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l'oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n'en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu'il refut mout gros; adonques je l'engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.
And the abscess had already risen so high that it had put out two branches through the two nostrils. I hastened then immediately, and fixed a hook in one, then drew it out, and drew out a great portion of pus; then I did the same in the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after I fixed the hook in these abscesses, and cut a part of them, and only a little blood came out; and thus the passage of the woman's throat was unblocked, and she began immediately to drink water and then wine, and I did not cease cutting this abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept regrowing, and refilling the place that I had emptied, until it was very large again; then I devised a way and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it remained without growing; and I departed from those parts, and did not know what God did with her after me.

de l'uve
On the uvula

Quant reume dessent a l'uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s'elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n'est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l'incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.
When rheum descends to the uvula, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is thick and round below, it is called "uvula". When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not profit, and you see that the hot abscess is calmed, and it is thin, then it is necessary that you cut it; and that which is round gathered and not long; and it is sanguine or of false color or black, then it is necessary that you avoid cutting it. For there is great peril for the patient.

Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j'ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l'estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l'oncine en l'uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j'ai dit en l'incision des .ij. amandres.
It is necessary then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and its length, that you make the patient sit before the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument of which we have made mention before; then fix the hook in the uvula, and draw it down, and cut it with one of the two instruments that I have mentioned in the incision of the two tonsils.

Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l'incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l'incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu'elle soit sanee.
And it is necessary that you do not cut except for the excess which is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut more, you harm the voice, and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two tonsils, and treat it until it is healed.

Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d'engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l'estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu'elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:
And if the patient is afraid of cutting, then it is necessary that you use a device for cauterizing it without fear. And the manner of cautery is with sharp water. And it is that the patient puts his head in your lap, and then you press his tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and mix with quicklime, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and fill the hollow of this instrument, of which here is the form:

Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d'une cuillier, et met l'estrument a tout la medicine sus l'uve;
And it has at the top an opening where one puts the medicine, like the hollow of a spoon, and one puts the instrument with the medicine on the uvula;

et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu'ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;
and the patient should be lying on his side, so that the saliva and mucus run from his mouth from the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat and hurt him;

puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l'uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d'une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;
then hold your hand with all the medicine and press it on the uvula, for half an hour, until you see it blacken and the stinging of the medicine is calmed;

et se tu vues, pren coton et l'envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l'estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s'aerde sus l'uve;
and if you want, take cotton and wrap it on an instrument, and wet the cotton in the medicine, and push the instrument with the cotton into the tube above, until the cotton sticks to the uvula;

et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v.
and do this often, until the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and it falls off after 4 or 5 days.

Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l'essue entor l'uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;
And if you need to restart the cauterization with the medicine, restart it, and after the cauterization wipe around the uvula with cotton soaked in butter, and clean what is around from the medicine;

et soit arosez d'aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu'il soit sanez.
and let it be sprinkled with cold water, and be treated with gargles until it is healed.

Ceste cure est plus save de l'incision, ne que li cautere; s'elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d'eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;
This treatment is safer than incision or cauterization; if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take calamint and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and southernwood and similar herbs, and put them all or some of them in a pot, and add vinegar, and boil;

et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:
and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and in the middle of the pot there should be a hollow instrument like this:

Et soit d'argent ou d'arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l'uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;
And it should be of silver or brass, and one of the ends should be put in the patient's mouth so that the vapor rises to the uvula through the tube, until the uvula is deadened;

aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l'avenement de l'aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;
afterwards repeat it often, until the uvula dries, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the occurrence of a hot swelling, because many things can happen;

et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d'aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n'est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d'uef, si que li bouche au malaide n'ait mie trop chaut;
and do not do this except at the decline of a hot swelling. And if this instrument is not available, take a tube and put an eggshell inside the end, so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot;

car li craiffe d'uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c'est bone cure ensamble salut.
because the eggshell does not let the vapor harm the mouth, and this is a good treatment together with safety.

Maintes fois s'aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l'estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;
Many times a bone or fish spine, or something else, gets stuck in the throat; so it is necessary that you remove what you can see, and press the tongue in the sunlight with the instrument, so that you can see the thing better;

et ceu que ne t'apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l'estomac;
and what does not appear to you and is hidden in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach;

par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d'esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec;
perhaps the stuck thing will come out through vomiting; or the patient should swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of turnip, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread;

et lie a l'esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s'aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;
and tie a thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will stick, and then you will pull it out;

et s'elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:
and if it does not come out from what we have said, then take a lead instrument of this shape:

Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu'il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;
And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the end raised high;

et warde que tu ne touchier l'epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l'os dedens;
and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest coughing come to him, nor push the bone inside;

et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l'estrument, por ceu qu'il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;
and it is better that the patient pushes the instrument, because he knows better where the thing is stuck;

si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l'estrument igalment, tant qu'elle soit fuer.
so push it down, or pull it out with the instrument evenly, until it is out.

de la sansue de la gorge
About the leech in the throat

Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j'ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;
Sometimes the leech is treated, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines;

et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l'estrument que je t'ai dit.
and when this does not help, then look in the patient's throat in the sunlight, after you press his tongue with the instrument that I told you about.

Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.
And if you see the leech, pull it out with a small hook, or with fine forceps that are good for this.

Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.
And if this does not work, take a hollow tube, and push it into the patient's throat, then push a hot iron into the hollow of the tube, and do this often.

Et se teigne li malaides d'aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d'aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;
And let the patient hold water all day. Then take a full glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and throw it in without swallowing, and move it with his hand often;

et si tost com li sansue sent l'aigue, si chiet.
and as soon as the leech feels the water, it falls.

Et s'elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d'asefetide, a l'estrument que j'ai dit en la fumigation de l'uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.
And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I mentioned for the fumigation of the uvula; do this many times, for it will fall without delay.

Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d'un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l'estrument;
And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot where there are live coals, and let the pot be covered with a lid pierced in the middle, and in that hole should be the end of the instrument;

puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n'en isse mie, mais viegne jusc'a la sansue;
then throw your fumigation in it, and the patient should put the end of the tube in his mouth, and close his mouth, so that the smoke does not escape, but comes up to the leech;

et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s'elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;
and the leech will fall now, and if it does not fall, repeat the fumigation many times;

et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d'aigue;
and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty things and garlic, and not drink any water;

et adonques li iert mestier qu'elle isse fuer par cest governement.
and then it will be necessary for it to come out through this treatment.

Et li forme de l'estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;
And the shape of the instrument with which one pulls out the leech, when one can see it, is similar to curved forceps to better enter the throat;

et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu'elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:
and it has a resemblance to the beak of a swan, and there is a roughness of a file, so that what it grabs, it cannot let go; and here is the shape:

li chapistres des apostemes
The chapter on abscesses

Mout de semblances d'aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d'un et d'autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;
There are many types of abscesses, according to what the memory comes afterwards of one and another in this book, and they are different in perforation and in cutting;

et c'est en .ij. manieres dont l'une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu'il tient moistor.
and this is in two ways, of which one is in its own appearance, and from what it holds moisture.

Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l'uevre.
And the second way is for the places where they are in the body. For the abscess of the head is different from that of the fundament, and the abscess of the fleshy place is different from that which comes in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.

Et si a apostemes c'on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;
And there are abscesses that one should not pierce, until the pus is ripe according to its completion;

et si a de telz qu'il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.
and there are some that must be pierced when they have grown, and do not ripen according to their completion, such as abscesses that are near joints.

Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu'il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.
For when an abscess comes near joints, and one leaves it until it is rotted around, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.

Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu'il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;
Or the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay the perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the principal member;

ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu'il soit meurs;
or it is near the fundament, so one pierces it before it is ripe;

et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu'il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;
and it is not necessary that you pierce a raw abscess without complete digestion, except for that which is near the fundament, lest it rot deeply, and be elongated inside, and fistula comes there;

et ne puisse saner en grant termine.
and cannot heal in a long term.

Et covient que tu saiches l'oure de la perforation de l'aposteme qui est meur selonc l'acomplissement, et c'est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l'amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l'aguisement dou chief de l'aposteme, et les autres signes;
And it is necessary that you know the hour of perforation of the abscess which is ripe according to completion, and that is when the pain is calmed, and the departure of the fever, and the diminution of the pain and redness, and of the throbbing and sharpness of the head of the abscess, and the other signs;

et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l'aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;
and it is necessary that you make the perforation in the most dependent place of the abscess, and where it appears best;

et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n'a point de ploieure.
and let the perforation be along the length of the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all even places where there is no bending.

En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.
For those that bend, according to that limb.

Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu'il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.
And when the abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.

Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d'ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.
For if you pierce it before that, the body of its venom will be elongated, and it is full of much filth; and perhaps its lips and depths will harden.

Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.
And there are some abscesses that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb needs.

Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l'aposteme;
And it is necessary that you administer in small abscesses, small holes; and in large abscesses, large holes, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess;

et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:
and there are such abscesses where it is necessary to hollow out the core, and cut; when it has already become like a cloth, and is deadened, it is necessary to do as one does with boils:

et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.
and there are some that are split into 3 angles, and there are some that are cut like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of the groin; and there are some where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar incisions.

Cil qui n'ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;
Those that have no head, like a soft superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce them flatly;

et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;
and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus at that hour, but draw out a part;

puis estoupe l'aposteme jusc'a l'autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;
then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more again; do this many times gradually, until all the pus comes out;

meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.
especially if the patient is of weak virtue, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or a decrepit old man.

Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l'issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t'en persois.
For the spirit sometimes jumps out with the exit of the pus, so that perhaps the patient dies, and you do not perceive it.

Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l'aposteme est petite;
Avoid then this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, wipe the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small;

et se c'est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;
and if it is a flat cut, administer tents of linen or old cotton;

et se c'est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu'ele viegne l'une contre l'autre;
and if it is a large abscess, and there are many holes, it is necessary that you push into each a tent so that they come one against the other;

et se tu as copeit en l'aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l'as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l'emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc'au tier jor;
and if you have cut in the abscess a part of the skin, and you have hollowed around it, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or shavings of linen cloth without moisture, and bind it until the third day;

puis l'oste, et le cure d'oignement tant qu'il soit sanez.
then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.

Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.
And if bleeding occurs in your work, administer cold water and vinegar, and wet a cloth, and put it on the bleeding place many times.

Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j'ai dit em mains leus en cest livre,
And if the bleeding persists, administer management and treatment, and the powders that I have mentioned in many places in this book,

et se c'est ou tens d'iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;
and if it is in winter time, and the place where the abscess is is very nervous, it is necessary that you put on tents and cloths soaked in wine and hot oil;

et se c'est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc'au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;
and if it is in summer, and the place is fleshy, it is necessary that you put on cloths soaked in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said;

et puis deslie l'aposteme et l'essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu'il soit sanez.
and then untie the abscess and wipe it and treat it, as is necessary, until it is healed.

Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.
And this must be known universally in cures of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed with the cures of abscesses, and here is the chapter.

des soros
On tumors

Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d'une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.
In the heart of the head come small abscesses, and they are types of knots that are in membranes, like the gizzard of a hen, and there are many similarities.

Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n'i a point de doutance se li artere n'i fait contraire.
There are fatty ones and some where there is moisture like pus; and there are some that are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery does not cause problems.

Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.
And the work of the cut is that you test with an instrument that is called "probe", of which the form comes hereafter, what thing it contains.

Car s'il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.
For if it contains moisture, split it from above lengthwise.

Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;
And when the moisture is emptied, skin without leaving anything the skin that contains this moisture, for it always comes back when one leaves anything;

puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s'il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc'a l'autre jor;
then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and fill the wound with it, and leave it until the next day;

et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.
and this corrupts what has remained of the nest.

Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu'il ne demoure point dou nit;
And you can restart the cotton, as before, the second day, and the third, until you know well that nothing remains of the nest;

puis cure la plaie d'oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu'il soit sanez.
then treat the wound with ointment suitable for this, until it is healed.

Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;
And if the abscess holds a fatty knot, cut it according to this form, lengthwise;

et i giete tes oncines, et l'escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;
and throw your hooks there, and skin it from all sides, and put all your care to draw out the sac where it lies;

et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t'ai dit aprés.
and if the artery causes you problems, do what I told you after.

Et ausi fai de l'aposteme s'il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t'ai dit.
And also do this with the abscess if it is stony, and for cutting and treating as I told you.

Et li taille sus l'aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.
And the cut on the stony abscess and the moist one is easier, for they are of little blood.

Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n'a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d'une vielle femme;
And there are some of these abscesses in the head where there is no moisture, and of these was an abscess that I cut in the head of an old woman;

et trovai l'aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;
and I found the abscess like a deaf stone, rough and white, and could not break;

et s'on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d'une piere.
and if one had struck someone with it, one would have made a wound as well as with a stone.

En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;
In other abscesses coming in the head, except those that come to the heads of children and to the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at the most dependent place, to better let out the pus;

et les cure si com il covient.
and treat them as is necessary.

des scrophules
On scrofulas

Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l'une avec l'autre.
Many times these abscesses occur on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groins, and sometimes come elsewhere in the body, and are many, and are engendered one with the other.

Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;
And each scrofula is properly within its sac, like the knot and the abscess of the head, as we have said;

et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.
and the appearances of these scrofulas are many.

Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.
There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not want to obey health.

en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n'est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l'artere ne au conduit, et n'est mie parfonde;
in that then that you see of good disposition to the touch, and is similar to the color of the body, and moves from each part and is not attached to the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the duct, and is not deep;

si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l'escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;
it is necessary that you cut it from above, and skin it from each part, and extend the two lips of the skin with hooks, if you need to, as we have said in abscesses of the head;

et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n'eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.
and draw it little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and let not the spatula be sharp or cutting, lest the hand slip, and do not go too far forward, that you do not cut what you should not.

Et se tu copes la voinne ou l'artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;
And if you cut the vein or the artery, and this does not let you work, put ground vitriol in the wound, or some powders that staunch blood, and tighten the wound;

et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.
And leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound is softened, and begins to decay.

Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l'acomplisses;
And when the blood has stopped, return to your work until you complete it;

puis quier a ton doit indice s'il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.
then search with your index finger if any small scrofulas remain, cut them and clean them.

Et s'il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d'un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;
And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, you should not cut this scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall off by itself, without harm;

puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.
then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then treat it.

Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu'il n'i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.
And if you cut out the entire scrofula, you should bring together the two lips of the wound, and sew them immediately, since no excess remains due to the size of the scrofula.

si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.
so you should attend to cutting its root, and pulling it out, and sew it as we have said.

Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu'elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;
Those scrofulas that hold excess, pierce there where it appears ripe; and pierce it as said before, downwards, then administer tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption;

et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d'oignement enjanrant char, tant qu'il soit sanez.
and when the wound is well cleaned, treat it with ointment generating flesh, until it is healed.

de squinance
On quinsy

Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c'est li escripture de lor parole.
The ancients spoke about cutting the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their words.

A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c'on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.
For those who have quinsy, it is necessary that the cut in the throat which is called "epiglottis" be avoided; and that one does not help by this, because all the veins and the lung of the patient are for those who have hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in the two tonsils.

Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l'epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l'estranglement.
When the disease is in the channel of the lung, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to escape the loss that comes from strangulation.

Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l'epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;
It is necessary then, when we want to split the epiglottis, that we split it below three or four circles a small transverse cut, between the two circles or by the quantity of the cut of the syfac, not in the cartilage;

et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l'epiglote qu'il n'i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d'enqui.
and this place is suitable for the section of the epiglottis as there is no flesh, and the vessels are far from there.

Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu'il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l'oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu'il viegne a la cheneil;
And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat with all the hook, then splits the skin until he comes to the channel;

et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;
and avoid the blood vessels, if you see any, and then cut the syfac, as we have said;

et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;
and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm of the channel which jumps out through the place which is broken, and by the lack of voice;

et laisse la plaie overte une piece.
and leave the wound open for a while.

Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l'estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;
And when the hour has passed of which one fears strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the skin, and sew it all alone without the cartilage;

puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu'il soit sanez.
then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it is healed.

Albucasim dist c'on ne faice ce jusc'a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.
Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be dying, and his breath fails him.

Adonques cope on l'epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;
Then one cuts the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death;

et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.
and for this reason the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four.

Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu'elle fut curee;
And then they commanded to sew the wound and treat it, until it was healed;

et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.
and I will tell you what I saw.

Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;
I saw that a young lady took a knife, and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the channels of the lung;

et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.
and I was called to treat her, and found her as if dead.

Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu'elle n'avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.
I uncovered the wound, and found the blood that had come out, and knew well that she had not cut vein nor conduit except the throat, and the wind was coming out through the wound.

Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu'elle fut sanee;
I hurried, and sewed the wound, and treated it until it was healed;

et n'avint a la damoisele fuer qu'elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;
and nothing happened to the young lady except that she was hoarse of voice, and returned afterwards to her disposition;

por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l'epiglote n'ait mie paour.
therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there should be no fear.

de la grosse gorge
On the thick throat

Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d'une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;
This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and is a large abscess in the color of a goiter, and is common in women;

et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n'a point d'engien.
and is according to two manners: natural, and accidental; in the natural there is no device.

Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l'une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d'artere;
And the accidental is according to two manners, of which one is similar to fat knots, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from knots of artery;

et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l'intromissoire:
and there is fear, and it is not necessary to work with iron except in that which is small, and test and search it with all the probe:

se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s'il en i a point;
if you find it like a fat knot, and it does not hang on any vein, cut it, as one cuts knots, and pull it with all its sheath, if there is any;

et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu'il soit sanez parfaitement.
and search well all, and treat it as is necessary, until it is perfectly healed.

des nous
On knots

Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;
There are many kinds of knots, of which I will tell all the appearances;

et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.
and now it is necessary that I tell all the difference that is between knot and issue.

Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;
I say that issue is holding heat and fever, until the boiling is passed, and the rotting is accomplished;

adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.
then the fever and the heat rest.

Avec lou nout n'a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;
With the knot there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains a syfac, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a goiter, and becomes big;

et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j'ai dit en la division.
and they are according to two appearances, either fat, or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.

Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l'enquier premierement a tout l'estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.
It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the knot, that you test and inquire first with all the instrument which is called "probe", according to what its form will come in the chapter which is after.

Et li maniere de l'inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l'aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l'aposteme;
And the manner of the inquiry of the abscesses of knots is that you take in the moistest place that you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the skin, then that it be according to the size of the abscess;

puis estrai l'entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.
then extract the probe, and take care in what jumps out.

Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j'ai dit des autres apostemes;
If running moisture runs, whatever color it has, split it as I have said of other abscesses;

et se aprés l'entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu'il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l'escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;
and if after the probe no moisture comes, know that it is fat, so split it then in a cross, and take it with tweezers, and skin it lightly from each side and keep the coat where it lies that you pull it healthy with the knot;

et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu'il n'i demoure rien.
and if you cannot pull it healthy, pull it in pieces so that nothing remains.

Car s'il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;
For if anything remains, the knot comes back many times;

et s'il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d'aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d'autres cures tant qu'il soit sanez;
and if a little remains, and the blood grieves you, fill the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, and tighten the wound, and put on things soothing hot abscess, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed;

et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.
and if the knot is large, sew the two lips of the wound, and treat it with that which generates flesh.

et se li voine batans t'est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;
and if the beating vein is contrary to you or another so hurry and fill the place with ground vitriol, and leave it bound two days or three, until the wound rots, and the boiling of the blood rests;

puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.
then return to cutting what has remained of the knot.

Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit;
Here are the forms of probe instruments, and they are of three kinds: large and medium and small;

et s'en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s'en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;
And there are three square ones which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, for examining fistula abscesses;

et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d'arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d'argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;
and they are like the needles with which one sews sorcels, and are of yellow brass, or iron, or silver, and those which are yellow are more valuable, and are more proven of black lead for examining the curves of fistula;

et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.
and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the holes.

Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis;
The forms of hooks are of many appearances, as you see here: large, medium, and small;

et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres;
and there are hooks that have two curves of three kinds also; and there are hooks that have three curves, and are also of three kinds;

et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d'une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.
and there are hooks that have two curves, and hooks of only one curve, and they are of three kinds; and all these are necessary in their place.

Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d'une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c'on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;
The heads of these with which one cuts are sharp, and there are some which cut only on one side, with which one skins the knots, so that one does not cut the vein or the nerve;

et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s'en persoivent a l'overture des apostemes;
and of these probes are the blades hidden in handles, so that the patients do not perceive them at the opening of the abscesses;

et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n'en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;
and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses them only in fleshy places, such as legs, and arms, and breasts, and in groins, and in similar places;

et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:
and sometimes one makes another small instrument, similar to pistachio shells, according to this form, with which one stanches blood:

et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:
and one sometimes puts it on the place which bleeds at cutting of veins, and on arteries, and sometimes round according to this large form:

Aucune fois enflent les mameles d'aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu'eles semblent mameles de feme;
Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so that they resemble women's breasts;

et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:
and they remain ugly and swollen, and who wants to cure them, it is necessary to cut according to this form from this line b. to g.:

puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu'ele soit sanee;
then skin the fat, and fill the wound with medicine generating flesh, then bring together the two lips of the wound with suture, and treat it until it is healed;

et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;
and if the breast hangs down, and is softened by its size as it happens to women, split it in two sides above, by two similar cuts;

de coi l'une soit tenans a l'autre a la fin de l'une et de l'autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc'a la ligne .g.;
of which one is attached to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. to line .g.;

puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu'il soit sanez;
then skin the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and administer there what we have said of suture and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed;

et s'il n'est sanez, ou li incision n'est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;
and if it is not healed, or the incision is not all done, because the patient does not want to rest, or because of the flow of blood, it is necessary that you fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment;

et le laisse tant qu'il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu'il soit saneis.
and leave it until it eats the remainder and the fat, then treat it until it is healed.

des apostemes des asselles
On abscesses of the armpits

Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s'en i a que contienent moistor.
These abscesses that come under the armpits are kinds of hard scrofulas where there are sides, and there are some that contain moisture.

Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu'il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc'a la ligne .g.:
Those therefore that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line b. to line .g.:

Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l'aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc'a l'autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d'oignement avenant a ceu tant qu'il soit sanez.
And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment suitable for this until it is healed.

Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.
And if the abscess is of appearances of scrofulas, split it as we have said in cuts of scrofulas, and if the wound yields pus, administer cautery as we have said before.

de la routure de l'artere
On the rupture of the artery

Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;
When the artery is broken, and the skin is welded which is above, abscesses often come from it, and the same happens to the swollen vein and abscess;

et si le conoist on ensi quant c'est por l'artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement;
and one knows it thus when it is for the artery, the abscess is long in depth; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel a tightening;

et quant c'est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c'est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d'autres leus, et est mout grans.
and when it is for the vein, it is round appearing outside; and it is folly to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits and in the groins and on the neck and in many other places, and is very large.

Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d'enfleure d'artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;
It is therefore necessary to avoid the treatment of iron, and that which is at the head should be avoided also, and in that which is from swelling of artery split above the skin lengthwise;

puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l'artere des toiles, tant qu'ele soit descoverte;
then open the cut with hooks, and gently separate the artery from the membranes, until it is uncovered;

puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc'a l'autre costeit, et estraint l'artere d'un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t'ai ensigniet en l'estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;
then push under it a needle, and make it pierce to the other side, and tighten the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries which are in temples;

puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d'un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;
then prick the place which is between the two ties with a probe until the blood which is there comes out, and let the abscess be untied;
