puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans et semblans choses. Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n'aert a l'os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;
and similar things. And if you find rottenness in the skin, and it doesn't adhere to the bone, cut out all the rotted part, and throw it away, then treat it;
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l'artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d'un fil;
and if there is an artery or vein in the wound from which blood flows, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, seek the artery, and if you find it unbound, tie it with a thread;
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.
and if that doesn't help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l'ait muee.
And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is easy: it is that you put in this powder which seals before the burn has changed it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l'estraint forment, tant qu'elle s'aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;
And the manner of the powder is this: take one part incense; two parts dragon's blood; three parts quicklime, and powder it finely, and fill the wound, and tighten it strongly, until it adheres well and joins with all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s'elle n'enfle; car on n'oste la madicine tant qu'ele soit sanee.
and then bind it well, and leave it without unbinding, if it doesn't swell; for one doesn't remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n'ait l'encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n'ait muee la plaie.
And sometimes one does this with lime only, when one doesn't have incense or dragon's blood, but only if the burn hasn't changed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n'i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d'orge faites d'aigue et de miel, tant qu'ele giete bowe; puis le cure d'autres cures tant qu'il soit sanez.
And if the burn has changed the wound, especially in summer, don't put this powder on it; but put on some digestive ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it discharges pus; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
 Et se li brisure d'os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l'estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.
 And if a bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, extract it with fine tweezers; and I will tell you about head fractures later.
de la plaie dou col
On the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n'a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.
If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c'est li ners, si n'i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n'i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;
If it's the nerve, there is no other trick than to leave the treatment, and put nothing constricting on it, for it harms the nerves and makes them retract;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d'aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;
and don't put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.
but let the medicine be gentle, such as lime washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cucie washed also in sweet water, and other mineral stones in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu'il soit sanez.
And if the wound is large, sew it and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;
And if the wounds are deep and it is hollowed and full of pus, pierce it at the lowest place;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;
and if the artery is cut, and blood flow comes from it, separate it, and tie it, and cauterize it if necessary;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;
and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the heart, and the conduit is preserved, through which the food goes, sew the heart over the windpipe, and don't touch the throat but put it back according to its natural figure;
et puis l'estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d'oignemens desechans tant qu'il soit sanez;
and then tighten it suitably, and leave it for some days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l'os, si la quier; et s'il i a pieces d'os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;
and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, seek it; and if there are pieces of bone, draw them all out if you can, and those that you cannot have, leave until the wound rots, and is separated and the exit is eased;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j'ai dit.
and if the wound is fresh, powder it with the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s'il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j'ai dit en son chapistre.
And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel
On the wound from a lance or knife
Se c'est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;
If it's a blow from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, look if air comes out of the wound when the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal;
et s'elle n'est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n'i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;
and if it's not deep, and it's fresh with all its blood, don't put the powder on it at first, nor bind it because of the blood that might remain deep inside, and return to the heart, and kill the patient;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor; et se tu n'as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;
but put attractive ointment on it, and bind it twice a day; and if you don't have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for 3 days, or 4, or more;
si n'i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n'estraingnemens d'alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.
so spasm won't come, nor evil trembling of the heart nor tightening of breath; and when you see good dispositions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d'autres cures, tant qu'il soit sanez; et s'elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.
Treat it then with tents and other cures, until it is healed; and if it can't heal, and opens, know then that there is a fistula; so treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d'incision d'espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s'elle est grans, de cousture; et s'elle est petite, de poudre,
And if the wound is from a cut of sword or knife, and it is simple, on the chest or back, treat it with what is mentioned before; if it's large, with suture; and if it's small, with powder,
et s'elle est empressee en l'os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s'il sont desevrez; et s'il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;
and if it's pressed into the bone, and has cut pieces, seek the wound, and draw them out if they are separated; and if they are not separated, let the wound rot, so extraction will be easier;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.
and for other wounds on other members, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre
On the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d'aus;
The rupture of the belly is large and medium and small; from the large wound sometimes comes out the intestine, or the nerves of the intestines, by which their introduction;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c'on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s'on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;
and the suture is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the large one, because one puts back the intestines with more difficulty, if one doesn't put them back while they're still warm;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu'il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c'on ramoine mues l'intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.
because the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, so they go back in with more difficulty, and for this reason the medium wound is better, because one brings back the intestine to its place better than with the other two.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres: les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;
And know that the rupture of the belly is according to 4 manners: the 2 common sutures occur in the suture of the belly, and the suture of other wounds of the body and 2 other proper sutures are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.
and yet they are more proper with the suture of the belly, and I will say each one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l'intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l'une des .ij. manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.
I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestine comes out, and it's difficult to put back, this is by one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l'intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;
And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: wet a sponge or a soft cloth in lukewarm water only, or you cook in water squinant and cypress and spike, and sprinkle the intestine until the swelling is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.
and sometimes astringent wine does this, and is better than water alone for reducing swelling.
Et quant tu vois l'enfleure departir, si amoiste l'intestine d'aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;
And when you see the swelling go away, moisten the intestine with water where marshmallow and mallow have been cooked, for by this the entry is eased with little;
et s'il n'i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l'estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n'i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n'i ait;
and if it can't enter, split the wound a little with the instrument with which one cuts hemorrhoids; and the first cure is better than the cut, for no one should cut without great necessity;
et c'est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:
and this is the instrument for splitting: it cuts inside in the curve and not outside, and here is the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.
And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine comes out, put it back according to its natural form in its proper place, if you have the power, for this is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;
When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly, it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head;

et s'elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,
And if it is in the lower part of the belly, place the head and chest higher than the lower parts,
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l'une des .ij. parties si met t'entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;
and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, focus on ensuring that the wounded part is higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.
and thus it is appropriate to administer what I say for large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t'est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;
For small wounds, put what is prepared for you, then have in your hands a compassionate assistant who holds the entire rupture in his hand, and brings the edges together;
et c'est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,
and this is the common manner of sutures, which is that you take one needle or several, according to the size of the width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d'espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;
then leave a finger's width from the head of the wound, and insert a needle with a good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,
and pierce the two ends of the skin with the two ends of the peritoneum, which is under the skin inside, until you make it pierce that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;
and bring the two ends of the peritoneum together with the four together;
puis l'estrain d'un fil double entor l'aguille de .ij. pars, puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,
then tighten it with a double thread around the needle from two sides, then bring the two ends of the wound together properly,
et puis laisse .i. doi d'espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;
and then leave a finger's width, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;
then tie it with thread as you did the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to your need for needles, until the entire wound is closed;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:
and let the needles be medium, between thin and thick, for thin needles cut all the flesh, and the too thick ones cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu'elles soient moienes;
therefore it is appropriate that they be medium;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k'elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;
and it is not appropriate to push the needles too far out of the flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound before it heals;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu'elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,
and then cut the ends of the needles, so they do not hurt the patient while sleeping, and put tents or small cloths at the ends of the needles to hold them better,
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;
and leave them until the wound is healed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.
and this manner of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, for one or two needles suffice.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;
The second suture is common, and it is that you bring together the two ends of the skin and the two ends of the peritoneum with a needle that has a strong medium thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble, si ramoinne l'aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c'on cout les dras;
and when you have pierced these four ends together, bring the needle back to the part where you started, in the manner that one sews clothes;
et met d'espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d'un menor doi;
and put a space between each suture the width of a little finger;
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c'uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d'un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d'une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.
men know this suture, and I sewed a wound that a man had in his belly, who was wounded by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm's width in size, and intestines came out well two palms' width in size, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l'intestine puis k'il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc'a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.
I returned the intestine after it had been out for 24 hours, and the wound was healed up to 15 days, and I treated it, and he was cured.
Et li mire l'avoient jugiet qu'il morroit, et ce fut miracle;
And the doctors had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d'oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n'en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;
and I did not treat it with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d'aigue de miel tant qu'il fut sanez.
and I put nothing more on the wound than old cotton twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture: pren l'aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc'a celi dedens;
Now I will tell you the two proper manners of suturing: take the needle, and push it from the outside part to the inside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l'aguille, et la fai percier d'autre part des la partie dedens jusc'a celi defuer;
when it has pierced the skin straight through, leave the end of the peritoneum on the side where you pushed the needle, and make it pierce the other part from the inside to the outside;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d'une part, et le reprent d'autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.
and the understanding of this suture is that you sew as furriers do skins, and that you leave the peritoneum once on one side, and take it again on the other, until the suture is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l'un des chief dou syfac a l'autre chief, en teil maniere:
The second manner of suturing, which Galen specifically mentions, is as some do, who bring the two parts together naturally, and apply one end of the peritoneum to the other end, in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;
insert a needle in the nearest end of the abdominal wall, and pierce that place only, and leave the two ends of the peritoneum;
puis torne l'aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc'a celi dedens, as .ij. chiés dou syfac;
then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outside part to the inside, at the two ends of the peritoneum;
puis fai percier l'un et l'autre des la partie defuers jusc'a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l'autre costeit;
then make it pierce one and the other from the outside part to the inside, in two other ends of the abdominal wall that are on the other side;
et c'est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.
and this is the best manner of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c'on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;
Galen says this word, and some testify to it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, with thread in each;
et doit on bouter l'une aguille d'une part, et l'autre d'autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;
and one should push one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew straps;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.
and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the suture is more difficult than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l'ait muee, si remet arer l'intestine, et lou cout;
The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, before the art has changed it, put back the intestine, and sew it;
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l'ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;
then put on the powder generating flesh, and if the art has changed it, put on some ointment that is present, until the wound suppurates;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;
and the threads fall out, and let the peritoneum and abdominal wall be healed;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu'il soit sanez;
then treat the wound as the others, until it is healed;
et se tu n'as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu'ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k'il soit sanez.
and if you have no medicines, put on, as soon as it begins to discharge pus, old cotton, and change it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n'as mestier d'autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;
For you have no need of other medicine in many dispositions when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;
and if you fear that the wound may communicate with the principal members, it is appropriate that you moisten light wool in oil of moderate heat, or in rose oil, and put it around the groins, and under the armpits;
et s'il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc'a l'intestine;
and if he feels pain or corruption in the bowels, and it often happens, then give him an enema of lukewarm black wine, especially if the corruption comes to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c'est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.
and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c'est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l'aprochement de sa nature des ners.
The intestine which is called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is because of the abundance of veins that are there, and because of the thinness of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l'intestine, tandis qu'il est fres;
And if the omentum comes out of the wound, put it back as with the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s'il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n'i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;
and if it is old and has become green or black, it is appropriate that you tie the place that is black, so that blood flow does not come there, for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l'estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.
then cut what is between the ligature, and put the two hanging ends from the part below the wound to the outside to ease the extraction when the omentum falls, and the wound suppurates.
de la routure dou boueil
Of the rupture of the bowel
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d'une lance;
When the intestine is round, and the wound is small, one can restore it in some men, because I saw that a man was wounded in the belly by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l'estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;
and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and it became old and turned into a fistula, and excrement and flatulence came out of it;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu'il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.
I took care of it as best I could, and did not cease to refine until it was healed, and the place closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n'eust mal en son ventre;
And when I saw it close, I feared that the patient might have pain in his belly;
et il n'i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;
and he had no pain, but remained in better condition, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l'intestine, qu'il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:
And some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres, si qu'elle estraigne sa bouche sus;
Take ants with large heads, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the ant has opened its mouth, place it on the two edges, so that it tightens its mouth on them;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu'il ne puet desliier, puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.
and then cut off its head, and it holds so that it cannot come undone, then put another ant after in the same manner as before, until the wound is entirely covered; and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s'aerdent en l'intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l'intestine d'un fil subtil qui est copez de l'intestine d'une beste, en teil maniere:
These heads adhere to the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a thin thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d'intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l'aguille, et en cout l'intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;
Take the end of this intestinal thread that is very lean, and then tie to the end of this thread a thin twisted linen thread, then push the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and bring it back into the rupture;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d'esperance;
and this manner of sewing with ants is only according to the way of trust and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l'un des grailes intestines, si n'i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.
and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the small intestines, there is no skill or health, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu'ele soit
On fistula, wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.
Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes old, is universally called a "fistula", especially when it is hollow and produces pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d'un oiseil;
And a fistula is, according to the truth, a hard and white felted nodule, where one feels no pain, and is as hollow as the quill of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;
and sometimes clear pus comes out, and other times thick; sometimes little, and other times a lot;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n'est sanee, et il n'i a char, ce n'est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:
and I have already spoken about it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and has no flesh, is only due to one of nine causes:
c'est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu'il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n'i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n'est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os:
that is to know, by the scarcity of blood in the body; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the lips, which does not allow flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the place is rotten, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good for the cure; or because the corruption is a kind of pestilence; or because the property in the region is slow digestion, and slow health, and swollen by nature; or there are veins or bones:
et j'ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.
and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.
Now it is necessary that I make known to you the cure of fistula which is done by handiwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l'intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l'espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;
Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the great veins, and to the arteries, and to the nerves, or to the peritoneum, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to some joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.
and there are such that come to the property of the principal member, and to similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n'i a fors que labour, et ignorance;
And all the fistulas that are of this manner are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc'a leu que j'ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d'arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;
and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place that I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you want to know it, then take a probe of brass or iron, if the fistula is straight, then seek it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d'une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;
and if the fistula is twisted, then search it with a subtle lead probe, for the lead bends better around the tortuosity;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l'un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d'un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;
and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot search it well with probes, then inject it through one of the openings, for the moisture runs from one opening to another, and cleanses it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s'il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu'il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;
then seek it wisely to your power, that you know if there is bone or nerve, and it is hollow in depth, and ask well of the patient about the pain that he feels at the pressing of your hand, and the place where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s'elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d'artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t'ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t'ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;
and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut it according to what I have told you, and remove the felt and the corrupt flesh that are inside;
et puis la cure tant qu'elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc'au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;
and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep in the right place, it is necessary that you cut deeply, as much as you can, then put wet probes in sharp medicine, and push them to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu'il soit sanez; et s'il n'est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.
and then put ointments generating healthy flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu'il soit sanez;
If vein or nerve does not trouble you or principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then scrape it until the corruption is all removed, then cure it with things generating flesh until it is healed;
et s'il n'est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n'es mie alez jusc'a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;
and if it is not healed, and produces pus as before, know that you have not gone to the bottom: so uncover and seek until you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s'il est ensi sanez, c'est bien. Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n'i pues avenir; si n'i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;
and if it is thus healed, it is good. If not, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot reach it; so there is no other skill than to leave it to nature;
et s'il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l'estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu, et s'il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n'en laissier nes un;
and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can draw it with tongs, then extract it with a suitable instrument for this, and if there are many bones, then draw them all, and do not leave even one;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n'i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.
and if the moisture makes you contrary, and there is no error or fear, then cut both moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;
And if you cannot remove them in one hour, then put on the wound something generating rot, and leave until the place is rotten around the bones, and then they will have the bones more easily;
et se c'est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;
and if it is a large bone, such as from the leg or thigh, then scrape only the corruption until the blackness is all removed, then restore the wound;
et s'il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc'a mole de l'os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc'a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu'il soit soudez;
and if there is a large part of the corrupted, and it comes to the marrow of the bone; so it is necessary to saw and cut all the way to the corruption, and then cure it until it is soldered;
et je te dirai d'une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.
and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d'une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d'un gros aposteme, et n'ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;
There was a young man around 30 years old, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came inside the body, so that the matters came to the leg, and it was swollen with a large abscess, and had no external cause to open;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;
but the doctors by their folly worked so much on it that the abscess opened, and much matter ran out, and it became a fistula, and many openings came that all threw out pus and moisture from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n'i ot nul saige en l'art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;
and many doctors put care into it for about 2 years, and there was no wise one in the art of hands, until I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which one cured it, and that which ran through the openings in great course;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine. Je boutai une tente en l'un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l'autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.
and the body of the young man became red, and had a citrine color. I pushed a probe into one of these openings, and then searched all the openings, and found that one came against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l'un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l'os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc'a l'os dedens;
I hastened therefore, and cut into one of the openings until I uncovered a part of the bone, and I found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption went as far as the inner bone.

je soiai ceu qui m'aparissoit de l'os corrumput, et cuidai qu'il n'i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;
I sawed what appeared to me to be corrupted bone, and thought there was no other corruption except what I removed; and I began to treat the wound with healing medicines for a long time, but it could not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l'os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l'os, et la soiai, et puis l'ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l'os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;
and then I started again, and uncovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I sawed it, and then removed it, and tried to heal the area; but I could not until I cut about a palm's width of the bone, and pulled it out with all its marrow, then treated it with medicines;
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l'ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.
and it was healed and mended quickly, and it was not necessary to restart the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l'evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l'os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n'ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l'aleir ne a venir.
For due to the evacuation he often sobbed, but he was healed entirely, and hard flesh grew in place of the bone, and he was in good condition and had no harm or ill effects at all, neither in going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren .i. liien, et l'estrain au chief de l'os qui apert, et comande aucun k'il l'estende en haut;
And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be sawed in this manner: take a ligature, and tie it at the end of the bone that appears, and command someone to extend it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l'os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;
and put another ligature of wool thicker than the first ligature, and tie it on the flesh above the bone, and extend the end, so that you pull the corrupted flesh below, and uncover the flesh above the place where you want to saw, so that the saw does not injure the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l'os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.
and put a firebrand or a board under the bone to better cut the corrupted flesh; and it is necessary to saw as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and saw again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n'apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;
And if the bone is corrupted, and does not appear, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, uncover all the flesh;
puis met .i. tison desoz, et puis soie des l'une partie a l'autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;
then put a firebrand underneath, and then saw from one part to the other the corruption, and let the sawing be along the length of the corruption a little, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l'os ou elle contient de l'autre part;
and if the corruption is in the joint, cut the corrupted joint, and saw the bone where it continues on the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n'i a autre angien que dou coper;
and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other solution but to cut;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t'apert;
and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand, or in the ankle of the foot, this thing is very difficult, but nevertheless it is necessary that you investigate this corrosion, how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;
and clean it in all the ways that you can, but so that the vein or the nerve do not hinder you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l'assise des os et l'aparance d'ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;
and know that the incisors and saws for cutting these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and their subtlety, and their size and their smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d'ovraige son estrument;
and for this reason it is necessary to prepare for each type of work its instrument;
et saiches que l'uevre te moustrera l'estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;
and know that the work will show you the instrument that you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the evidence of the types of diseases;
si porpense l'estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu'il le covient.
so consider the instrument that you need according to what is necessary.
dou feu
Of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;
The heads rot either from an internal cause, or from an external cause;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;
and when you have treated this corrosion with the cure of medicines, and they do not benefit, it is necessary to cut that limb up to the place where the corrosion comes, so that the patient escapes by this from death, or from the malice, which is greater, of the loss of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu'il semble qu'il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;
and the sign is that the limb becomes black, so that it seems that it is burned by fire, and rots after the blackness, then this corrosion goes from limb to limb, and takes over the whole body;
si te haste dou coper, et se c'est par la percussion d'aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc'a la main.
so hasten to cut, and if it is by the sting of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion and viper and similar, if the corrosion is at the tip of the finger, cut it, and do not give it space to come to the hand.
Et s'elle vient jusc'a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc'a bras;
And if it comes to the hand, cut it at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come to the arm;
et s'elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;
and if it comes to the arm, cut it at the elbow;
et s'elle passe le coute, c'est li mors, et n'i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;
and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and no treatment avails except the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s'elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l'autre jointe;
and do the same when the corrosion comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, cut it after the other joint;
et s'elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;
and if it comes to the foot, cut the whole foot;
et s'elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;
and if it rises to the leg, cut at the knee joint;
et s'elle vient desus le genoil, si n'i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;
and if it comes above the knee, there is no other solution but to let the patient die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l'un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l'autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;
and the manner of cutting or sawing the limb is that you tie it above and below, and one assistant extends one of the ligatures downward, and another assistant the other ligature upward, and you separate the flesh that is between the two ligatures with a wide spatula, until the bone is uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.
then cut or saw it, and put on each side a linen cloth, so that the saw does not touch the healthy place, and another injury and hot abscess does not come to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;
And if bleeding occurs when you operate, cauterize the place quickly, or put on some astringent powders;
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu'elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d'un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu'il soit sanez;
then return to your medicine until it is completed, then tie the wounded limb with a suitable ligature, and treat it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k'il avint a .i. home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu'elle porprist tout le piet;
and I will tell you what happened to a man in his foot: a blackness came to him that seemed like a burn from fire, and this corrosion first came to his toe, until it took over the whole foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;
and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cut off the foot, and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;
and a long time after, the corrosion returned to his finger, and he came to me, and I put repercussive things on it after cleansing the body, and the corrosion could not stop;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;
and he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, as I had hope of repelling the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu'il ne morist, car li vertus de l'ome estoit foible;
and I also feared that if I cut his hand, he might die, for the man's strength was weak;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;
and he despaired completely, and returned to his land, and hastened to cut off his hand, and was healed;
et je n'ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c'on faice autreteil, s'on en a mestier.
and I have not told this except so that one might do the same, if one has need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu'il fait grant assemblee de bowe;
Sometimes an abscess comes in a fleshy place, and remains so long that it makes a great collection of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;
and then it breaks and pierces, and the pus comes out, and the place remains empty, like a vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc'a l'os, ne jusc'au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n'est mie apelee «fistule»;
and the skin that is above is as thin as a fine cloth, and does not corrupt to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a disease is called "sain", and is not called "fistula";
mais s'elle est si alongie qu'elle viegne jusc'a l'os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;
but if it is so elongated that it comes to the bone in depth, it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;
and the cure is that you cut this skin all around, especially when it is thin, like a cloth;
et ne s'aert mie por sa corruption.
and it does not adhere because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s'aerde, et li corruption n'est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:
And if you have confidence that the skin will adhere, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, cure it with an enema thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:
see if the "sain" is large, and the pus that comes out has a foul odor, then treat it with an Egyptian medicine which is made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;
take vinegar, and oil, and litharge, equally, and put them to cook in a vessel on the fire, until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;
and then take from this according to your need, and melt it in water and honey, and use it as an enema for the breast, and tighten the opening;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l'estrai en espreignant;
and leave the medicine in for 2 hours, then extract it by squeezing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;
do this many times, until the breast is cleansed, and the stench is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d'aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n'est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;
and sometimes it is given an enema of ash water, when this medicine is not available, and it is that you take ashes of vine wood, and pour water over it, then strain it, and use it as an enema, until you know that the breast is well cleansed;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l'aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d'aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;
and if the patient cannot bear it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the ash water, then give an enema of water and honey with a little ground litharge;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;
or you give an enema of mixed honey and wine, as honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine makes the breast adhere;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;
and when you have done this, and you have confidence that the breast is well cleansed, then give an enema of that which makes flesh grow in it, and it is that you take diaphoenix plaster, and melt it with rose oil and in wine;
ou tu le clisterize d'aucunes medicines et d'oignemens, dont j'ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;
or you give an enema of some medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken of the properties in the treatise on ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n'i puet entrer, si l'eslarge d'un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l'oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k'il soit eslargiez;
and if the opening of the breast is small, and the enema tube cannot enter, then enlarge it a little with an iron, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, until it is enlarged;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.
and if the wound is too wide, then sew it and leave only one place where the enema can enter, and if the opening that discharges pus is at the top, then cut it at the lowest place that is there.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n'i laisse enjanrer char;
For when the pus is deep, it doesn't allow flesh to generate;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n'i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:
and if you cannot cut the breast below as you wish, then prepare it in such a way that the pus runs to the lowest place that is there, for when the pus is deep, it doesn't allow flesh to generate and if you cannot cut the breast below as you wish, then prepare it in this way:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n'i lassier rien de la bowe;
that the pus runs easily downward, and leave none of the pus;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;
and take consolidating medicines to put on the breast, and spread on a linen cloth that covers all the breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n'oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;
then cut with scissors right at the opening of the breast a little wider than before, then spread soft ointment on another cloth according to the size of the opening, and put it on the opening of the breast to ease the pus, and do not remove the large cloth except after many days once;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c'est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;
and the one that is on the opening of the breast, remove often to remove the pus, and know what will run from the pus, if it is venom or little or much, or digested, or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s'il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s'est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s'aert ja, et aproche li santez;
and take note if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in this way and you see the nature that leaps on the opening of the breast, know that the breast is already adhering, and health approaches;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l'oignement.
and then untie it in the morning, or the third day, and when you untie the wound, change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s'aert mie.
And if the breast discharges undigested pus after many days, know that the breast is not adhering.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.
And if thin venom runs after a long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;
For there are men whose generation of flesh in their wounds is slow, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s'aert mie;
and if undigested pus comes out of the breast after many days, know that the breast is not adhering;
et se li seins tarde d'aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c'est li derriene medicine;
and if the breast is slow to adhere, and is prolonged, then add drying medicines moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as diaphoenix ointment, for it has a large part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l'arose de viel vin igal en substance;
take diaphoenix ointment, and melt it with rose oil, and sprinkle it with old wine equal in substance;
puis le confit et en use;
then prepare it and use it;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n'est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;
and this same makes better cooked thickened, when diaphoenix ointment is not present, or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind it, and powder it on the honey when it is on the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l'estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;
and then glue a cloth with it, and spread it on the breast, and sometimes one administers long birthwort, and roots of celestial lily, which is like flour of vetches and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j'ai dit, et en use;
and use simples or compounds: grind them, and make powder, and put on the honey that I have mentioned, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n'est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l'os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;
and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this treatment, then know that the corruption is deep, and makes an impression on the bone, or on the hard members, or on the ligaments;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.
so cure it with the cure for fistula, as we have said before.
de l'aposteme de l'ungle
of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l'ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;
Paronychia is an abscess that grows under the nail of the thumb of the hand, or of the foot, or perhaps grows on other fingers;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n'i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu'elle corront la racine de l'ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;
and when it is old, and one does not take care of it, a hot abscess comes, and corrupts and discharges pus until it corrupts the root of the nail, and perhaps corrupts it all;
et vient li corrosions jusc'a l'os, tant qu'il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.
and the corrosion comes to the bone, so that there comes a stinking pain, and the head of the finger is wide, and the color is dark.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l'ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.
When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not profit, then it is necessary that you cut with an iron all the superfluity that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;
The cautery is a very great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l'encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l'ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;
and if the nail presses the flesh in, and begins to prick it, and wounds it, then it is necessary that you put the ray under the nail that pricks the flesh, and push it up, and cut that flesh subtly and lightly, and put on the remainder of the flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything;
puis le cure d'oignemens tant qu'il soit sanez.
then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l'os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;
And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it, and pull it out, for as long as the corrupted bone is there, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu'il soit sanez;
and if you see the finger corrupting, then cut it at one of the joints as it is said before, then treat it until it is healed;
et s'il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;
and if it is struck, and pushed, and it feels great pain, then it is necessary that you bleed it first;
puis cope l'ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc'a la char qui est desoz l'ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;
then cut the nail with a sharp spatula by cutting across above, and be careful that the cut does not come to the flesh that is under the nail, for the patient would feel too great pain;
et s'il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.
and if it happens, put something on it that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main
the pain of the extra finger of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d'aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d'aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.
The extra finger that grows on the hands of some men by chance is all fleshy, and by chance there is one where there are bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and some of them grow at the root of the joint, or the birth is in some knuckles of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;
The one that grows on some knuckle of the finger does not move, and the one that grows at the joint of the finger, by chance moves;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d'un large spatumile.
the cutting of the one that is fleshy is easy, in this way: cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.
The one that grows at the root of the joint is difficult to cure: so refrain from cutting.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc'a l'os, puis cope l'os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu'il soit sanez.
For the one that grows on the finger at the last knuckle, it is necessary that you first cut the flesh roundly to the bone, then cut the bone with a saw suitable for this, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.
The joining that comes to the fingers together comes by birth, or by joining of a wound, or by burning of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;
It is necessary that you cut this joining, so that the fingers return to their natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu'il ne se soudent;
then put between two tents or cloths moistened in rose oil, so that they do not join;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.
or you put between two pieces of thin lead, until the place is joined, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.
If joining comes to any of his fingers with the palm, cut this joining as it should be.
des vils
Of the veins
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.
Veins are large wrapped vessels full of melancholic superfluities, which come in several parts of the body; and occur more in the legs of those who walk on foot and who work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.
It is therefore necessary that you sometimes administer purging of bile, and then bleed from the basilic vein.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l'une est c'on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.
The iron cure is according to two methods: one is that one cuts them, and draws out the black blood; and the other method is that you lift the vein, and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d'aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc'a la partie desoz le genoil;
The cutting is done in this manner: first water the leg with very hot water, until the thick blood is thinned, then tighten the patient's leg from above the thigh to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d'une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l'un chief jusc'a l'autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;
then cut the vein in one place, or in two or three, with a wide cut, then raise and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient's strength can bear;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu'il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l'evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.
and then tie it, and command him to abstain from foods that generate black bile; and resume the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and it harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s'il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d'aigue chaude tant qu'elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;
The raising of it is done in this manner: shave the patient's leg, if there is much hair, then put it in the bath, and water the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell;
et se tu n'as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;
and if you don't have a bath, heat it by the fire, and then cut along the vein from the top of the knee, or in the part below at the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l'oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu'ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;
then open the skin with the hook, and peel the vein from each side, until it appears when one feels it; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu'ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l'oncine legier, puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois;
then push the probe underneath, until it is raised from the skin, and then hang it on the light hook, then cut it in another place three fingers away;
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu'ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;
then peel the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it with the probe, as you have done, and hang it on another hook, as you did at first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc'a la seconde taille;
then cut another incision, or several if you need to, then lift it, and cut it at the toe, then draw and lift it up to the second cut;
puis l'estrai de taille en taille, tant qu'elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d'une part et d'autre, tant qu'il en isse;
then draw it from cut to cut, until it all comes out, then cut it; and if you cannot draw and lift it, push a needle with a strong double thread, and tie it and draw it, and push a probe underneath, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it comes out;
et garde qu'elle ne cope, car s'elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;
and be careful that it doesn't cut, because if it cuts, one cannot draw or lift it, and harm comes to the patient;
et quant tu l'as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu'il soit sanez.
and when you have drawn it all out, put wool moistened in wine and rose oil on the place of the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n'est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.
And if the vein is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, it is necessary that you split it crookedly, but do not cut it; and draw it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu'il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s'il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:
The shape of the iron with which one cuts the vein is curved, and does not cut, so that it does not cut the vein; and it is of thick curvature, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is the shape:
de la voinne civile
Of the Guinea worm
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n'a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu'en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.
This worm is generated in legs, in hot parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in land where there is no moisture; and by chance it is born elsewhere than in legs, and this happens from the rottenness that comes under the skin, as serpents and worms come inside the body, generated between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l'encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu'il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d'une plante.
And the sign of the beginning of this worm is that a very great inflammation comes in the leg, then the place changes, and the worm begins to come out, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc'a .ij. З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu'il en ist point au defuer, si l'envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;
When the head appears, it is necessary that you wrap around it a piece of lead from one and a half ounces to two ounces, and tie it, and leave the lead hanging on the leg, and every time it comes out a bit, wrap it around the lead, and tie it;
et s'elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu'elle soit toute issue;
and if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and wrap the remainder, and do not cut it at its root, until it has all come out;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;
because if you cut it, it re-enters the flesh, and causes abscess and rottenness in the place, and bad disease;
por la queil chose il covient qu'elle soit traite poc et poc jusc'a chief, et n'en remaigne rien ou cors;
for which reason it is necessary that it be drawn little by little until the end, and nothing remains in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x., et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long,
and sometimes this worm, when it is drawn out, is five palms long, or ten, and a man once came to me, from whom it came out ten palms long,
et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc'a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.
and when you cut it, push a probe into the hole, and pierce it to the bottom, so that everything comes out; and let the matter that is inside be emptied, and administer to the place medicines generating rottenness for some days, then treat it as abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.
And sometimes this worm has fewer branches, especially when it appears in the joint of the foot, or in the foot, and many holes come, from which branches jump out; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char
Of the worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu'elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l'aler de membre en membre, tant qu'il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;
This disease is called in our land "cattle disease", because it often happens to cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body ascending and descending, and one can feel it well as it goes from member to member, until it breaks the skin where it goes, and jumps out;
et est enjanrez de porriture d'aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;
and it is generated from the rottenness of some humors, as come worms and serpents and roundworms and pinworms in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l'oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l'oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.
