and one fears its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance it re-enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d'un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer,
When you want to cure and extract it, one can only do so when it moves: so it is necessary that you tie the place above and below with a strong ligature very tightly, then cut above and draw it out,
et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu'il muire;
and if the worm is deep in the flesh, and you cannot find it, cauterize it with fire above, until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu'il corront l'oil, si com nos avons dit;
and the greatest harm that it does, is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l'oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;
and if you see it coming to the head near the eye, tighten strongly below it the eyebrow, then cut above, and draw it out;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.
and it is necessary to use for the patient purification of the body with purgative medicines for the bad rotten humors, and to beware of foods generating rottenness.

des saiettes
Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.
Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the parts of the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu'il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;
Their diversity is such that there are those with large points, and small ones, and hollow ones, and soldered ones; and those that have two angles, and those that have tongues, and those that have pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.
and that which falls on any member falls according to two manners: either on a principal hollow member, such as brain, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, intestine, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t'aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l'estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;
When it falls then in any place of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you hereafter, appear to you: it is fitting that you beware of extracting this arrow, for death comes after in several dispositions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t'aperent mie, et li saiette n'est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.
and when these bad signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not deep, then pull it out, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l'os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d'entendement, et vomissemens de cole;
And the signs of the brain when the arrow falls there and pierces the bone, and the membrane which is over the brain comes out, is when dizziness and sudden movements and vertigo and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;
and perhaps blood comes out of the nostrils, or the ears; and perhaps speech and voice are lost;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;
and white moisture resembling pus comes out of the wound, and also comes out like a broth of flesh;
et se cist signe t'aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s'elle n'est ens.
and if these signs appear to you, then abstain from the cure, and pull out the arrow if it is not inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu'elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s'elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;
The signs of the arrow when it falls on the heart, are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were fixed in something hard, not at all empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.
and perhaps the arrow moves like the pulse, and black blood runs from it, and coldness and cold sweat come, and syncope: know then without doubt that death descends.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d'escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.
And the signs of the arrow that wounds the lung are that blood full of foam comes out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs deeply and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.
And if the arrow falls on the covering of the chest, it is near the small ribs; and it causes great breathing difficulty and great pain and sighing; and all the members of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.
And if the arrow falls on the stomach, by chance some undigested food may come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l'intestine rout, si n'a point d'esperance en la cure, ne en l'estraction de la saiette.
And if the arrow falls in the belly, and any excrement comes out through the torn intestine, there is no hope for the cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.
And if the arrow falls in the bladder, and urine comes out and flows outside, and the patient feels strong pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.
The other members, such as the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the upper arm and the spine of the back and the breastbone and the thigh and the legs, and similar members, are safe according to several dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l'artere, et elle n'est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu'il m'avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.
When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you may do the same.
Il avint a .i. home c'une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d'autre part desoz la graisse de l'oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.
It happened to a man that an arrow fell on his tear duct at the root of the nose: I probed it, and drew it out on the other side below the fat of the ear, and he was healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l'oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n'en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d'un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.
And he drew out an arrow that had fallen into the fat of the eye beneath the lower eyelid, and the arrow was hidden, and I could only reach the point towards the shaft, and it was a large arrow from a Turkish bow, with a light iron tip without barbs; the wound healed, and no bad accidents occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.
And I extracted an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow with barbs: I sawed off the barbs, and worked so carefully that I extracted it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu'il moroit; et puis qu'il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l'engignai, et la traï fuer, et n'ot point de mavais accident.
And I extracted an arrow from a man, which had fallen into his belly, and I thought he would die; and after 30 days had passed, his condition did not change; I cut above the arrow, and worked it out, and pulled it out, and there were no bad accidents.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.
And I saw a man who had an arrow fall into his back, and the wound healed over it; and the arrow remained inside him, and it did not change his natural dispositions, nor did he find any harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d'autres semblans.
And I saw another man, who had an arrow fall into his face, and the wound healed; and it remained thus without causing great pain; and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu'elle fut cheue .iij. jors.
And I extracted an arrow from one of the king's princes, which had fallen into the middle of his nose, and was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was completely hidden. I was called to treat it three days after it had fallen.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite. Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.
I found the wound very narrow. I probed it with a thin probe, and did not feel anything; and he felt a pricking and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c'estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n'enflast; et m'aparut li leus de la saiette.
I thought it was from the point of the arrow. I put an attractive and digestive plaster on the place, so that the place would not swell; and the location of the arrow became apparent to me.
Je i mis l'emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu'il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.
I applied the plaster for several days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained thus for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his nose; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu'elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s'aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l'overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m'aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d'une part et d'autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d'engignier de manieres d'estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.
I applied a sharp corrosive medicine to the wound for several days, until it was open, and I probed it, and felt the head of the arrow which was attached to the place; then I added more of that sharp medicine to the opening of the wound, until the head of the arrow became visible to me; and about four months passed, and then I enlarged the wound so that I could insert forceps, and I moved it from one side to the other, but it could not come out; then I did not cease to refine and devise various instruments, until one day I took it with well-made forceps, according to the form that will come at the end of this chapter, until I extracted it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.
And the physicians judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I restored it then, and the wound was healed, and the patient was cured entirely.
Or t'ai dit la qualiteit de l'estraction d'aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.
Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you may apply your care to what I have not said, for the book cannot encompass everything; but the wise master compares on very little great things, and on what is present and lacking, finds new work, and new instruments, for the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n'issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d'autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c'est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.
I say that arrows do not come out of the members where they are fixed except in two ways: either through the place where they enter, or through another part; and that which comes out through where it enters, is an arrow entering fleshy places, and sometimes comes out immediately.
Et s'elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s'elle est fichie en l'os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s'elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.
And if it does not come out immediately, leave it until the flesh around it has rotted, and the exit is eased; and also if it is fixed in the bone, and cannot come out, leave it thus for some days, and move it each day; and then it comes out, and if it does not come out, pierce around it with a thin drill, until the place around is enlarged, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l'os dou chief, et vait jusc'a l'un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j'ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu'elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc'a syfac, c'est li mors.
And if the arrow is fixed in the bone of the head, and goes to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned appear in the patient: do not extract it, but leave it until it is level after some days, for if the arrow comes to the syfac, it is death.
Et se li saiette n'est fichie fuer qu'en l'os soulement, et ne vient jusc'a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l'engigne dou traire. Et s'elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t'ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu'il soit sanez.
And if the arrow is fixed only in the bone, and does not come to the syfac, and the patient remains for some days without bad accident, then devise to extract it. And if it is very fixed thus and cannot come out, administer drills around it, as I have told you; then treat the place until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c'on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l'estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n'i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s'il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.
And if the arrow is hidden in a place of the body so that it cannot be seen, seek it with the probe; and if you feel it, extract it with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound, and because of the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then split it until the wound is large; and extract the arrow if you can, and if there are barbs on the arrow by which it holds, remove the flesh that is fixed in two parts as best you can, and then break or bend the barbs of the arrow, until you can extract it; and be careful not to break the arrow, for you would extract it more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.
And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the place around has rotted, then extract it, for the extraction will be eased.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l'incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu'il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c'est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.
And if the flow of blood hinders you, administer what we have said about the cure in its chapter; and beware of cutting the nerve and the vein, and use ingenuity how you can best extract the arrow without danger, either quickly or slowly, either firmly or gently; and put the patient in the position he was when the arrow fell in, for that is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot, put him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d'autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c'on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l'estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.
The arrow that comes out from another part, where something of it appears, or the skin is swollen right there so that one can see or feel it clearly: cut then above, until the forceps can grasp it, and then extract it: it will come out immediately.
Et s'elle est retenue en l'os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu'elle entre en l'os, et eslarge l'os, puis la trai. Et s'elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l'estraction tant qu'elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l'estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l'estraction.
And if it is retained in the bone, turn your hand round, until it enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then extract it. And if it cannot come out, leave it again, and then restart the extraction until it comes out; and if the shaft of the arrow is there, push it with all the shaft; and if the shaft falls, and you want to administer pushing, administer a hollow instrument, so that the point of the arrow enters the hollow of the instrument; and then push out, and if the arrow is hollow, push in a pointed instrument, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient. Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l'estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu'elle soit sanee.
And if the arrow is poisoned, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as it should be. And if the arrow falls in the chest or in the belly or in the bladder or in the side, and it is close, and you can cut above, then cut; and beware of cutting the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew the wound, if necessary; and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d'oiseil, et vez ci la forme:
The shape of the forceps with which one extracts arrows are similar to a bird's beak, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette. Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d'un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:
And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow. The shape of the hollow pusher is also like the feather of a bird, to push at the point of the arrow, as here is the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:
the shape of the forceps for pushing and pulling is here:
des voinnes dou cors communes
Of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi., c'est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans; et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col; et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.
Of the veins from which one bleeds, there are 31, of which there are 16 in the head, namely: 2 pulsating ones which are behind the ears, which are called the two "herbech"; and the 2 arteries which are in the two visible temples; and 2 veins which are in the 2 tear ducts of the 2 eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the 2 jugulars which are in the neck; and the 2 veins that are in the upper lips of the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and 2 veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras: l'une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l'apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l'apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l'apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.
The veins from which one commonly bleeds are 5 in each arm: one is the cephalic, and is on the left side, and lay people call it the "head vein"; and the middle one is called "faste", and is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and lay people call it the "heart vein"; and the basilic is on the right side, and lay people call it the "belly vein", and it is on the forearm, and it is the one from which one bleeds, which appears clearly on the thumb.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l'auriculaire et l'anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;
The salvatella is the vein that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l'une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,
and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is below the curve of the ankle on the left side,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;
and the second saphenous vein which is at the ankle on the right side;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l'autre costei;
and the vein which is called "nesse", which is in the ankle on the other side;
et en l'autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.
and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;
The bleeding of the veins that are behind the ears helps with chronic catarrhs and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d'un drap aspre;
and the quality of bleeding, as I tell you, is that you shave the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:
then the patient tightens his neck with a screw, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places descending from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d'enche;
search for them with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, mark it with ink;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc'a l'os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;
then take the lancet, and push it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand with the vein upwards, and cut both the skin and the vein about two fingers across, and let out as much blood as you want;
puis l'estrain et lie, tant qu'ele soit sanee; et j'ai ja dit l'incision et le cautere ou premier livre.
then compress and tie it until it is healed; and I have already spoken about incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;
The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is good for chronic migraines, headaches, recurring ophthalmia, and for the flow of sharp tears in the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;
and the quality of bleeding is as I say: it is that the patient tightens his neck, until the two veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d'enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;
and feel the pulse under your finger, and then mark with ink; then lift the heart on the vein upwards with your index finger, and push the lancet underneath, and lift the vein upwards, and cut it, as you have done with the two other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu'elle soit sanee;
then untie the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it; and then tie it firmly, and leave it until it is healed;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.
and we have already spoken about their cutting and their extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;
The bleeding of the forehead vein is as effective as the bleeding of the cephalic vein for chronic facial diseases, for migraines, and for redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;
and the quality is that the patient tightens his neck by twisting, until the vein appears;
puis pren l'estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:
then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", of which here is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d'autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;
And put the point on the vein, and strike it with your hand, or with something else, and let the blood come out according to the quantity you want;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu'elle soit saneel et aucune fois l'uevre on d'un flaime large.
then untie the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and sometimes it is opened with a wide fleam.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.
However, it is not appropriate for the fleam to be too sharp; and bleed it crosswise, because the bone is close, and by chance the fleam breaks when it is thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l'oriuel en l'oil, et as maladies de la faice;
The bleeding of the two veins that are in the two tear ducts helps the eyes, and ringworm, and redness, and stye in the eye, and diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d'aucun liien, si com devant;
and the quality of their bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck by twisting with some tie, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n'i a point de char. Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;
then bleed him, and let the bleeding be crosswise, a little along the length of the somewhat wide fleam, because there is no flesh there. And if the fleam is thin, by chance it may break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.
then let the blood flow, as much as you need, and then tie cotton over it, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;
The bleeding of the nose vein is good for acute conditions, and for severe headaches, and for diseases of the face, such as migraines and redness that comes to the face, especially when it is chronic;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l'espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines, car li voinne n'apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;
and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck, then squeezes his nose with your left hand, and take the thin long fleam, and stick it in the middle of the lip in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not appear well there, and the blood will start to flow immediately;
et n'aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c'est li forme dou flaime:
and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then tie it for a night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the shape of the fleam:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l'estrecement de l'alainne, et a l'encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;
The bleeding of the two jugular veins helps with the narrowing of breath, and with the beginning of leprosy, and with many diseases, and with impetigo, and with corrosive conditions, and with herpes, and gangrene;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l'une et l'autre, si com nos avons dit;
and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck below one and the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;
and let the master stand on the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a seat, then bleed the vein lengthwise a bit widely, then draw blood moderately, or as much as is needed;
puis refai autreteil en l'autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n'estrangle;
then do the same to the other vein, then untie the tie, and compress both veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle;
et le laisse jusc'au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.
and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.

de la sainie des leivres
On the bleeding of the lips

Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.
The bleeding of the veins of the upper lips helps with inflammation in the mouth, and with corruption of the gums, and cracks of the lips, and of the nose and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j'ai dit;
And the quality of the bleeding is to make the patient sit in front of you, and tighten his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l'une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu'elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:
then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, of which one is on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are recognized by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them are small black veins:
cope donques l'une et l'autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c'est une meisme maniere.
cut therefore one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, cut the largest on each side, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner.

de la sainie desoz la lengue
Of the bloodletting under the tongue

Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c'est a l'estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l'uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l'une et l'autre, et n'aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.
The bloodletting of the veins under the tongue helps after the bloodletting of the cephalic vein, and it is for the narrowing of the throat, and for diseases of the uvula, and for diseases of the mouth; and the method of bloodletting is that the patient sits between your hands facing the sun, and you lift the tongue, and look underneath on each side for a black vein: then bleed both of them, and do not go too deep, because underneath are the arteries.

Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres: ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l'estrecement des voinnes.
The veins of the elbow from which one commonly bleeds are bled according to two methods: either by pricking with a wide myrtle-leaf lancet, or with a thin olive-leaf lancet like a sharp knife, which is called "anesil"; and they are wide or thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins.

Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:
The shape of the myrtle-leaf lancet is very well-known, and is wide as you see:

Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c'est li forme dou flaime olivaire:
And it is needed to open the hollow veins full of thick visible blood, and which contain thick and cloudy blood; and this is the shape of the olive-leaf lancet:

et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.
and it is thinner and pointed, and is for bleeding the thin veins, where there is thin yellow blood.

Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu'il saine saigement, et qu'il se warse de l'artere qui est desoz.
The bloodletting of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly; and it is necessary for the bloodletter to bleed wisely, and to be aware of the artery that is underneath.

Et s'il cope l'arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j'ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.
And if he cuts the artery, and blood flow comes, it is necessary to stanch it, as I have said; and the lancet should not be pricking, but cutting like an anesil.

Et se li basilique n'apert manifestement, si covient que tu l'estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.
And if the basilic vein does not appear clearly, it is necessary that you squeeze it, and change to another; or you seek some branch of it, or you bleed in its place the vein in the middle of the arm: it appears clearly; and cut it with the anesil lancet, as we have said.

Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d'enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l'artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c'est de l'artere: eschui la donques.
And if you want to know the place of the bloodletting, it is necessary before you squeeze the arm, that you touch the place until you recognize the pulse; then mark the place with ink, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein with the anesil lancet; and be careful not to strike the artery when you see the place swollen, because that is from the artery: avoid it then.

Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l'urine d'un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c'est sans de l'artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu'il soit sanez.
And if you see it spurting high like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from the artery: hurry then, and put your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the blood stops, which often happens; then tie the arm, and leave it thus, and let not the patient move it; and let him be in fear, and not move it until it is healed.

Et se li sans n'est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t'est presens, si cope l'artere s'elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.
And if the blood is not stanched, and it overcomes you, and medicine is not present for you, then cut the artery if it appears, because its ends will retract; and the blood will stop.

Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l'une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc'a l'autre jor; se li sans estainche, c'est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n'est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.
And take a pistachio shell, and split it, and take one of the halves and tie it on well until the next day; if the blood stops, that is good; if not, then treat it, as we have said, with powders that stop blood; and the stopping is not difficult in many cases because of the small place of the wound, and the strength of the arm binding.

Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu'elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu'elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu'il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s'il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s'il n'apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l'estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.
The bloodletting of the middle vein helps because it draws blood from the head above, and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and the cephalic, as we have said; and it is necessary for the bloodletter to be aware of the nerve that is underneath, and if he pricks too deeply, and he finds the nerve, and it swells and the health becomes difficult, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve appears many times, and if it does not appear in some men because of its fineness, it is necessary that you bleed it with the anesil instrument; and avoid the nerve to the best of your ability.

Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.
And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then split it lengthwise.

Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu'ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c'est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n'a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.
The bloodletting of the cephalic vein helps, as it draws blood from the head, and helps the eyes; and it is necessary to bleed by pricking with the olive-leaf lancet or the myrtle-leaf lancet, because it is the safest of all the veins, as there is neither nerve nor artery underneath it.

Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s'on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.
However, it is necessary to seek the easiest place, and it does no harm if one fails the first time, and one begins again; and perhaps the place swells in some men, when one fails the first time, but it does no harm.

La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.
The quality of the bloodletting is according to your thought.

Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n'est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l'une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c'est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l'encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.
The first thing you should know about bloodletting is that bloodletting is not administered except to maintain health, and to avoid future illnesses; and the bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins that are in the elbow: that is to say, cephalic, median, and basilic; and one should bleed at the beginning of spring while fasting, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of repletion appear; and one should bleed on the first day or the third, after 2 or 3 hours of the day.

Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n'a point d'oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc'a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc'a septime.
The bloodletting that is administered for illnesses has no determined hour, but when there is need day or night, at all hours and in all seasons; and it is not appropriate to bleed children up to 14 years old, nor pregnant women except from the fourth month to the seventh.

Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.
Nor should the old who have passed 60 years bleed themselves.

Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k'il mondefie les intestines d'un clistere legier, s'il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n'atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k'il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d'abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l'arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s'aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij., puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d'un poc d'oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.
And when someone wants to bleed, in whatever manner it may be, it is necessary that he cleanse the intestines with a light enema, if he has retained much feces, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines the rotten superfluities harmful to the principal members; nor should one who is too full of food bleed himself, nor one who is drunk, until he is out of it, nor those with dropsy; and one should be wary of bleeding after colic passion, and vomiting, and diarrhea, and excessive intercourse with women, and from labor, from staying awake and from fasting, and that which takes all virtue, either by thing of the soul or of the body; then thin the humors, if the blood is thick, by foods and by drinks and by medicines, if you have the power; then enter the bath, if nothing prevents it, to thin the blood, and bleed yourself from the vein of the chest around the third hour, as we have said; and guard yourself that day from work, and from pain, and from luxury, and from similar things; and be happy and joyful, and let the bloodletter be higher than the one being bled, and rub the arm 2 or 3 times, then tighten the band above moderately, for when it is too tight or loose, the blood cannot flow; and then rub the place with the hands, until the veins swell, and one feels them; then the bloodletter moistens the lancet with a little old oil, then puts his finger of his left hand on that vein below the place a little where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not flee and fail at the strike.

Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s'il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.
For there are veins that flee like cords when bleeding, and there are some that are full of windiness, so that when one puts the lancet on, it retracts the lancet, and cannot open the vein, and thus it is with these; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore it is necessary that the bloodletter be aware of these things.

Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c'est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n'est enflez.
And if the vein opens the first time, that's good; if not, then begin again a little below or above that place quickly, if the area is not swollen.

Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s'espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n'entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s'elle li plait;
And if the area is swollen, and the patient is frightened, leave it for a day or two, and do not tie the arm: by chance a hot abscess may come; do not enter the bath, then restart the bleeding if it pleases him;

et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu'il n'isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l'uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.
and if the opening is small, or the blood flows thinly and you doubt that as much blood will come out as you want, then strike that same opening with the lancet directly; and open it a little hastily, before the area becomes swollen; for this happens many times when the wound is small.

Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d'oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;
If you see the area swollen, do not restart the bleeding, and put on a little oil lees, for it eases the flow of blood, and the lees are better in this place than the oil;

et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d'eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s'espart quant il est trop gros.
and thus administer the oil lees in each bleeding when you bleed the veins, to stanch the flow of blood; and the same does treacle and egg white, when one puts it on the place; it thins the blood and spreads it when it is too thick.

Et s'il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n'est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l'estraint une houre;
And if a large abscess comes, which happens many times, especially when it is not bled except that one time when the opening of the vein is small, then hasten, and put on the place a sponge moistened in water and in salt a little hot, and press it for an hour;

et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l'issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s'il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.
and it is necessary that you do this after the exit of blood from the vein, and if there remains in the place after some days some blackness or greenness, it does not harm it; and if you want, put on something of aloe or myrrh dissolved in juice of calamint, wild mint, or similar.

Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.
And many times abscess and swelling happen at the bleeding of the basilic vein: put then your hand on it, and if you find the place soft at the compression of the hand, then that swelling is bad.

Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune thing de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l'artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d'autre cure, tant qu'il soit sanez.
Avoid then that you put on any of the things that we have said, for by chance blood from the artery may run; but make for it a dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with other treatment, until it is healed.

Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.
And draw from each blood according to the quantity of his strength, and the color of the blood.

Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu'il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu'il soit subtiliiez; et s'il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.
For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.

Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d'estraction de sanc, c'on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;
And it is necessary for one who is full and strong, and has need of blood extraction, that one make for him a larger wound, and let the lancet be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed him little and often, and one should bleed him by cutting across, not by pricking;

et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.
and this manner of bleeding is safe from running of blood and cutting of nerve, and is better than bleeding lengthwise or widthwise.

Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s'il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.
And to one whose body fails at the bleeding, it is necessary to give bread moistened in juice of pomegranates; if he is heated, then draw blood three or four times.

Et s'il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.
And if he is of cold complexion, then let him eat before the bleeding bread moistened in musk syrup, or in syrup of aromatic honey with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and very fragrant syrup.

Et s'il paume a la sainie, aprés l'issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu'il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l'evacuation de voinne.
And if he faints at the bleeding, after the exit of much blood, it is necessary that he sip broth of meat, and subtle fragrant syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of vein.

Et s'il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k'il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.
And if he wants to air his arm, and bleed another time, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleed little by little, according to the quantity of his strength continuously.

Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.
And who wants to air his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, then he bleeds seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.

Et qui se vuet sainier d'autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier. Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu'il chiece em pameson;
And who wants to bleed from another part, then he should bleed on the second day or the third. For he has much blood inside the body which is already heated, and causes fever to come; so it is necessary to draw a great quantity, and enlarge the opening until he falls into a faint;

puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;
then you observe all the conditions of bleeding, and put your hand on his pulse when he bleeds, so that death does not come instead of fainting, and this happens many times, when the bleeder is negligent;

et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s'il est corbes, qu'il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu'il saine la seconde fois;
and it is not necessary when you want to untie the arm, and make blood come out the second time, and the opening is closed, that you press strongly on it; nor if it is curved, that he extend the arm hastily, for that would be bad; but leave it until he bleeds the second time;

ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.
or you prick it with the point of the lancet, until the blood which is congealed at the opening of the vein comes out, and put on a little salt dissolved in water, and press on it lightly.

Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l'estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.
And if the vein is swollen, then leave it and do not press it, until the abscess is calmed.

Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l'autre bras.
And if there is necessity to draw blood a second time, then bleed it in that same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.

Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu'elle est composte. Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;
The vein in the middle of the arm is bled instead of the vein of the head because it is compound. And the manner of bleeding is that the patient puts his hand in hot water, until the forearm is red;

puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main,
then let it be tied moderately, so that the vein appears well, then bleed it now across, not widthwise nor lengthwise; and let the opening be wide, and let it be bled very close to the joint of the hand,

et se sans n'en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l'aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c'est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l'i met plus en yver que en esteit;
and if blood cannot come out, then put the hand back in hot water, and let the blood run in the water, until you have enough of it; and if it is in summer, do not put the hand back in hot water, for one puts it there more in winter than in summer;

et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu'il n'i a ne artere ne nerf.
and the bleeding of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve.

Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c'est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c'on la voie;
The bleeding of the salvatella of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: tighten the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein is swollen, so that one sees it;

et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n'aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n'en puet issir.
and bleed it across, and if you cut it completely, it does not harm anything; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are below all bare of flesh, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the blood is congealed in the wound, and cannot come out.

Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t'est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.
And when you have drawn as much blood as you need, then put on the vein oil and salt to heal quickly, and do this for each branch.

Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t'ai dit devers destre.
The bleeding of it in the left hand is good for disease of the spleen, and do just as I have told you for the right.

Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.
The bleeding of the saphenous vein is good for all diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the womb, and retention of menses, and disease of the kidneys, and of the thighs and old diseases of the legs, and similar diseases.

Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu'elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;
And the quality of its bleeding is that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it appears, and ties above the joint of the foot;

et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.
and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many branches; bleed it then in the largest branch, or at the ankle, which is better.

Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.
And if you bleed it on the foot, beware of the nerves underneath, and bleed it crosswise as if cutting; and let the lancet be sharp.

Et se li sans n'en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l'aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.
And if the blood cannot come out, put the foot back in the water, and let the vein empty well.

Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l'autre piet igalment.
And if the bleeder fails the first time, start again a little above, for the place is safe; do not fear the nerve, as we have said, and do the same for the saphenous vein of the other foot equally.

Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c'est por sanc chaut.
The location of the sciatic vein is at the outer ankle, and its bleeding is good for hip pain, when it's due to hot blood.

Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant, car autrement n'apert li voinne; et s'elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.
And the quality of its bleeding is that the patient enters the bath, and tightens above the ankle with four fingers by twisting, for otherwise the vein doesn't appear; and if it appears, bleed it in all the ways you can, and crosswise; and it's better that you cut it, for the place is safe, and it is very hidden in many men.

Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l'estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.
And if you don't find it, bleed any branch of it that appears on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and let as much blood flow as you want, and then untie the binding, and put cotton on it and tighten it; it is now healed.

des sainies de ventouse
On cupping bloodletting

Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d'arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.
Cups are made of horns, or brass, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.

Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes; et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n'en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu'elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.
And this cupping without striking is done in two ways: either with fire or without fire; and cupping that is done by striking and extracting blood is done in 14 places on the body, of which one is at the top of the head; and another is in the middle of the neck; and two others on the two sides of the neck; and the cup under the chin; and the cup on the two shoulders; and the cup on the loins; and the cups in the middle of the two arms; and the cups on the two legs; and the cups on the two ankles; and cupping does not draw blood, except from the small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken one, as does bleeding from a vein; and it should not be administered, neither with fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.

Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l'amenistrons chescune houre en l'encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.
And if by necessity of diseases it is appropriate to cup, or by custom, we administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in the middle and at every time; for there are those who, when they need cupping, have a heavy head; and there are those who find repletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes; and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and spit blood; and there are those who dream, and see blood and wounds and death and similar things at night.

Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c'est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.
And when we see these signs, especially when it's in the middle of the month, we command to cup after 3 hours of the day.

Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l'evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.
The bleeding of the forehead helps with the heaviness of the head ... that comes to the eyes, and it should not be after the evacuation of the whole body; and this cupping is in place of bleeding from the cephalic vein, and it is not appropriate for those who are of cold complexion to use it, or who have catarrh, for it does them great harm; and for this reason it is not appropriate for the elderly to use it, nor those who have cold diseases in the head.

Et cil qui s'en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d'obliance.
And those who bleed from it often become forgetful, and for this reason it is appropriate to put the cup a little lower for fear of forgetfulness.

Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l'estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s'elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.
Cupping in the middle of the neck is in place of bleeding from the head and the basilic vein, and for this reason it is good for tightness of the chest, and for splitting of the lung channel, and for cough, and for repletion; and it should be pushed little, for if it holds too firmly, it engenders forgetfulness in the stomach and heart.

Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l'estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu'il espresse sa main au mettre, qu'il ne cope l'artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.
Cupping on the two sides of the neck is good for headaches, and ophthalmia and migraine, and for strangulation, and for pain at the roots of the teeth, and is in place of bleeding from the basilic vein; and you should command the bleeder to press his hand when placing it, so that he does not cut the artery, and bleeding does not occur.

Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.
Cupping under the chin is good for mouth disease, and for corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and is in place of bleeding from the two lips.

Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.
Cupping of the shoulders is good for disease that comes from heat and repletion.

Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu'il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.
Cupping of the elbows is as good as from the three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; and command the bleeder not to strike too deeply, for the place is bare of flesh, and there are nerves and arteries underneath.

Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d'arain, qu'elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s'elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.
The cup that is on the rump is good for hemorrhoids of the fundament, and for diseases below, and it is appropriate that the cup be large, and be of brass, for it needs to draw well; and by chance, if it were thin, it would break; and make large wounds there.

Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.
The cups of the legs bleed openly, for they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains of the kidneys, and of the womb, and of the bladder, and bring back the menses; and are in place of the two saphenous veins, and of the two ankles, and yet they weaken the body after long use, and cause fainting in many dispositions.

Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.
The manner of putting the cup is that you put it first empty, and suck moderately, and put it hastily, and move it equally, and do not cease doing this, until you see the place red and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears; then strike, and replace the cups, and take care in the disposition of the bodies, for there are those who have tender flesh, and clear pores: so it is appropriate to strike only once, and it is appropriate to make wide wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.

Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.
And if the blood is thick, it is appropriate to strike twice: the first time to thin the path of the thick blood.

Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.
And if the blood is very thick, it is appropriate to strike a third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, one time suffices for us.

Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d'oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c'est en esteit, d'oile violet, ou d'oile d'amandres douces, ou d'oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c'est en yveir, d'oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.
And if we want a lot of blood, we start again often; and if the blood is thick, strike deeply, and the end is that the skin should be pierced suddenly, and it is appropriate for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the places of the cups with aperitive and dissolving oil: if it is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in winter, with cress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or similar.

Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d'anet, et les semblans.
And if the superfluity is thick and cold, take amaranth oil, or costmary oil, or dill oil, and similar ones.

Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n'i covient mettre point d'oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d'aigue rose, ou d'aigue froide, ou d'aigue de morelle, ou d'aigue de cucurbite, ou d'aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.
And if the one who is being bled has tender flesh and large pores, it is not appropriate to put any oil, but it is appropriate to wash after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or nightshade water, or pumpkin water, or purslane water, or similar.

Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d'aisil, ou d'aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.
And those who have a lot of moisture, wash with vinegar, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.

Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d'aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d'anet ou de camomile, ou d'autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k'il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.
And those who have gross superfluities should rise from old wine, or elderberry water, or decoction of dill or chamomile, or other similar things; and one should not be bled by cupping before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath for one or two hours; and one should not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary to be cautious when one must be cupped and when one has been cupped.

Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu'il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l'aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.
And watch if the one who bleeds is choleric, and if the blood is too sharp and inflamed; it is necessary that he take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces with vinegar, and similar things; and eat chickens, and mutton, and moist meats.

Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu'il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.
And he who has a cold complexion should take honey syrup, and medium-fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat chickens and small birds and pigeons; and on the day he is cupped, he should drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men sometimes treacle or nutmeg before cupping, or after, to comfort the principal members; and let the blood be thinned, but it is not suitable for those who are hot to drink it.

Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l'opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d'aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c'on emplisse la ventouse d'aigue chaude soule, ou d'aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu. Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:
The cups that are placed without striking are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and the navel and the kidneys and the hip, for these members do not suffer striking on them, and one does it only to draw blood from member to member, as we put on the breasts when the nose bleeds; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we put cups on the belly and on the navel to reduce the member; and it removes the pain, when there is obstruction or stone, it removes by its attractive virtue perhaps the obstruction, or detaches the stone from its place; and so it does when one puts it on the liver and on the spleen when there is retained wind, and these cups are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes full of lukewarm water, as in diseases of pleurisy, and in such a manner that one fills the cup with hot water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been cooked. The form of the cup administered with fire is this:
