Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d'arain, souef devant si qu'ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d'arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l'eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.
And it should have two fingers of width and half a palm of depth, and have on the side around the middle a small hole, as if to insert a needle, and be of brass, soft in front so that it does not hurt the patient when put on the member; and have in the middle a crossbar of brass or iron, to put a lit candle, and there should be both large and small ones according to the diseases and the age of those who take them; for the cups of children are different from those of the old, and of the thin from those of the fat.

Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu'elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier. En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n'a point de verge ne de pertus, et n'est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d'aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c'est li forme:
And one should put this cup on the member like this: light the wax candle or a wick, and put it in the middle of the cup across the rod that is in the middle of the cup, so that the light is at the bottom of the cup so that it does not burn the patient; and then put it on the member, and your finger should be on the hole that we have mentioned, so that when one wants, the vapor goes out, and one removes the cup; and one lights the wick as before, and begins again often, if you have need. In the cup then that is administered in the disease of pleurisy, with all water, there is no rod or hole, and it is administered only when it is full of water, and is put on the member only; and this is the form:

Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l'user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu'elles soient famillouses, et n'aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k'il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c'est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés. Se ceu non, si leve le leu d'aisil, et puis d'aigue, mout bien, et puis l'espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu'il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu'elles s'aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.
Leeches are administered only on members where one cannot put cups due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in places devoid of flesh, such as fingers or nose, and other similar ones; and the quality of using them is that when you find leeches that are in clean fresh waters without rot, take them; and put them for a night in fresh water, until they are hungry, and have nothing in their stomachs; and then let blood be drawn by vein and cup, then rub the member until it is red, and put on the leeches; and when they are full, and fall off, if it is a place where one can put a cup, put it, for it is very valuable afterwards. If not, then wash the place with vinegar, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it; and if the place bleeds too much after the course of the leeches, wet a linen cloth in cold water, and put it on, until the blood is stanched; and if the blood is multiplied, put on ground vitriol, or galls, and similar things, until it is stanched; or you put on the place halves of peeled beans, and leave them until they stick to the place, so it will stanch now; and if you have more need, take other leeches.

Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s'aerdent; et quant tu vues qu'elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d'aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.
And if the leeches do not want to take hold, rub the place with fresh blood, or you stick a needle in it until blood comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will stick; and when you want them to fall off, sprinkle on a little ground alum and salt, or ash, so they will fall off now.

This is the last book of fractures and dislocations

Dou restorement de la brisure de la jambe.
Of the restoration of the fracture of the leg.

Dou restourement de la brisure des os des dois dou piet.
Of the restoration of the fracture of the bones of the toes.

Dou restourement de la brisure de l'os de la nature a la femme, et de l'os dou poignil, et de la verge de l'ome.
Of the restoration of the fracture of the woman's pelvic bone, and of the wrist bone, and of the man's penis.

Dou restourement de la brisure des os quant il i a plaie.
Of the restoration of bone fractures when there is a wound.

Dou restourement de la brisure dou ventre.
Of the restoration of abdominal injuries.

De la cure dou membre qui est foibles aprés lou restorement de la brisure.
Of the treatment of a limb that is weak after the restoration of a fracture.

De la cure dou membre qui demoure tortus aprés la brisure.
Of the treatment of a limb that remains crooked after a fracture.

De la commune dislocation en membres.
Of common dislocations in limbs.

De la dislocation des mandibules.
Of the dislocation of the jaw.

De la dislocation de la forcelle.
Of the dislocation of the collarbone.

De la dislocation de l'espaule.
Of the dislocation of the shoulder.

De la dislocation dou coute.
Of the dislocation of the elbow.

De la dislocation de la main.
Of the dislocation of the hand.

De la dislocation des dois.
Of the dislocation of the fingers.

De l'espinee dou dos ou dou col quant elle est desaluee.
Of the spine of the back or neck when it is dislocated.

De la dislocation de la hainche.
Of the dislocation of the hip.

De la dislocation dou genoil.
Of the dislocation of the knee.

De la dislocation de la cheville.
Of the dislocation of the ankle.

De la dislocation des dois dou piet.
Of the dislocation of the toes.

Des manieres de dislocation ou il a plaie ou brisure, ou l'un et l'autre ensamble.
Of the types of dislocations where there is a wound or fracture, or both together.

Ci comence li livre des brisures
Here begins the book of fractures

Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l'art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.
This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is about the restoration of fractures and dislocations.

Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu'il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n'en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n'en trovai onques nul boin; et n'en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j'ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l'acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l'ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j'ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.
Know, dear son, that foolish doctors dismiss this chapter, as they have never seen any of the ancient books, nor read any letters about it; and for this reason, the science is strange in our land, for I have never found any good ones; and I know nothing about it, except through the science of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have extracted the science from them, and through experiment, and through the customs of my life; and I have already described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are administered, as I have done in these two chapters before.

Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l'aprenent a autrui.
It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the speech and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and dwells on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.

Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d'une part et d'autre, s'aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n'est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c'est a savoir froides joutes, et char d'oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s'emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n'aies doute d'aposteme chaut, ne d'espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k'il a useit.
I say that when a fracture or dislocation or sprain or bruise happens to someone, it is necessary that you hasten to bleed the patient from one side and the other, if nothing prevents you from doing so, such as weakness of body, or children, or old people; or if the weather is not very hot, or too cold; and eat cold cabbage, that is to say cold soups, and bird and goat meat, and do not drink any wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, so that you do not fear a hot abscess, nor the spreading of matter to the limb; thus the patient should return to his first regimen that he has used.

Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose. // Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.
And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that provide substantial nourishment, or that have viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and heads, and feet, and cow's stomach, and eggs, and fresh fish, and thick wine, and similar things. // For with such nourishment, the fracture heals better and more quickly.

Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n'a cure, ramoinne sus l'os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s'aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu'il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.
And know that the broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot heal well or weld according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but do not worry, bring back onto the broken bone a thick cartilage that adheres and joins the limb together, until it strengthens as it was before; and it does not take away from its function, and for this reason it is necessary to nourish it with substantial foods, as we have said.

Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres. Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure. Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d'une penne por escrire.
And know that fractures are diverse in many ways. For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the chest, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manners of fractures. For there is a fracture that goes in an arc, and another in sharpening, like the cut of a feather for writing.

Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure. Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l'os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n'i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n'i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure. Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l'estraint maintenant subtilment.
And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with just a small crack. And each manner has its own technique, and its own proper instrument for restoration, according to how the memory comes to its place; and the fracture of the bone is known by the fact that the place is twisted, and appears well from the outside, and sounds when pressed by the hand; and when there is no twisting or sound when touched, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but there may well be twisting, or cracking, or a small fracture. So it is not necessary that you move it with your hand, but put on medicines that come hereafter, and then tighten it now subtly.

Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l'estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.
And know that the fracture that goes in an arc, and the two parts are disjointed, it is necessary to set them equally now, before a hot abscess comes; and if a hot abscess comes, leave it for a few days, until the abscess is calmed; then set it equally as best you can lightly and wisely, and know that its restoration is easier than the restoration of one where there are pieces; then tighten it, as it is necessary hereafter.

Et se en l'os a piéces brisies, si l'estent de .ij. pars, se c'est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c'est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes. Et le sent bien a la main s'il te semble k'il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l'estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.
And if there are broken pieces in the bone, extend it from two sides, if it is hands or feet, or with your hand if it is a small limb, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand; and put the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, bring back by all means the additions to their places as best you can, and take care that through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient; and join well the two ends of the bones according to the best forms. And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not good: so straighten it gently, and do not tighten it too much, nor press as do those who by their work bring about hot abscess and contraction to the limb, as we have seen many times.

Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu'il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu'il ne sente nule dolor.
And when the limb is in place, admonish the patient well that he does not move it, neither while awake nor while sleeping, nor in turning, nor in any other manner; and ensure well that the limb is so secure that he feels no pain.

Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n'est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu'il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k'il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n'i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis. Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme. Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d'un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l'estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu'il n'i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l'estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l'estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu'il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s'il n'i a aposteme ou enfleure.
For when he feels any pain, it is not in place, and it is necessary to put it in such a disposition that he feels no pain; and take care that it is placed straight, so that no twisting comes when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I tell you. Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and in size and in shape. For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and the like: so it is necessary to wrap them in soft and subtle linen cloths; and those that are large, such as thigh and leg: so it is necessary to wrap them with a wide and hard bandage, for the wide bandage embraces all the large limb, and tightens it equally on all sides, so that there is no mark; then tie light tow around it, 3 or 4 turns according to the limb, and tighten your hand a little with all the bandage, then go above the fracture and tighten it less, so that the fracture can then distance the fracture a little; and soften the bandage little by little, until you take a large part of the healthy place, then take another bandage, and turn around again on the broken place; then go back to the part below the fracture, and tighten it moderately, neither too strongly nor too softly, as we have said in the first bandaging above; then put between the bandages tow of linen or cloths, until it is all equal, then tie everything above with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.

Et s'il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l'enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d'une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:
And if there is swelling or abscess, put on something that calms hot abscess, and that removes the swelling, and leave it like this for a few days; then tighten on your splints, and let them be half of a wide cane cut wisely, or of wood from which one makes splints, or of palm branches, and let them be according to this figure:

mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;
But it is necessary that the splint placed on the fracture be a bit thicker and wider than the others;

et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;
and be as long as is suitable for the size of the small or large limb;

puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure,
then tighten over the splints as you did for the first binding,

puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;
then tie a thread suitably over it, as in the first binding over the fracture;

plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;
it is tighter further away, always less;

et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;
and it is necessary that the threads be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen;

car se li fil sont gros, si com j'ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c'est grant error,
for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who make their bindings with twisted linen cords, and this is a great error,

car li lieure ne puet estre igal s'il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu'il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d'espaice.
because the binding cannot be even if it is too fine, and it is not suitable to have less than a finger's width of space between each splint.

Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l'estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu'il ne se blece.
And if the patient is wounded by the ends of the splints after tightening in healthy places, put linen padding or carded wool under them, so that he does not hurt himself.

Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.
When the wound is with the fracture, and the heart is broken, I will speak of the cure hereafter.

Et saiches qu'il ne covient mie estraindre d'esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.
And know that it is not necessary to tighten splints on all broken limbs on the first day.

Car quant li membres est grans, se n'i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d'aposteme chaut sorvenant;
For when the limb is large, it is not necessary to put splints except after 5 days or 7, or more according to your certainty of hot swelling occurring;

et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:
and here is the manner of ancient plasters to restore fracture, dislocation, and sprain:

et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d'uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use,
and it is that you take flour that clings to the walls of the mill, and mix it with egg white, and apply this concoction, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it,

et c'est li commune maniere de l'emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n'est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.
and this is the common manner of plaster restoring fracture for many conditions, and especially for women and small children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold.

Autre maniere d'emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:
Another manner of plaster restoring fracture and dislocation and sprain:

pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.;
take 10 drams each of abareis, ladanum, elecampane, asafoetida, gum arabic, and musk; 5 drams each of myrrh and aloe; 9 drams of alechil;

et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d'uef;
and make a powder, and mix them with egg white;

se li complexion de l'ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.
if the man's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is valuable for many men.

Autre maniere d'emplaustre que vaut a torsion:
Another manner of plaster that is valuable for sprain:

pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d'uef, et l'aministre.
take 10 drams each of musk and marshmallow; 9 drams each of myrrh and aloe; 6 drams of acacia; 10 drams of Armenian bole, and grind well, and mix with water or egg white, and administer it.

Autre maniere d'emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l'os, et la briseure:
Another manner of plaster for joints and bones separated from their places, and soothes the pain occurring, and the cut using the bone, and the fracture:

pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.
take new wool, and soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and put it on the place.

Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d'aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.
This plaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing hot swelling, and properly removes pains.

Autre maniere d'emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:
Another manner of plaster that restores broken bones:

pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.
take dried fig leaves, and leaves of ground poppy, and grind together, and make a plaster.

Autre maniere d'emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l'os et por amenusier lou remenant de l'aposteme.
Another manner of plaster for the restoration of bone fracture and to reduce the remainder of the swelling.

Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin,
Take root of marshmallow, chamomile, violet flowers, vetch flour, one part of each; and grind, and mix with wine,

et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d'aigue, et en use.
and if the limb is heated, mix it with water of moist coriander, or water, and use it.

Autre maniere d'emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.
Another manner of plaster stronger than the first, when hard swelling comes to the restoration of the limb.

Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;
Take roots of marshmallow, and linseed, pomegranate flower, melilot, and savory, and flowers of violet and chamomile, one part of each;

et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.
and grind, and mix with willow water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.

Ypocras dist en son livre c'on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d'oile, et nulle autre chose plus,
Hippocrates says in his book that one should put on the broken limb to restore only cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else more,

et dist qu'il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.
and says that it should be between neither too soft nor too hard.

Et il semble galien c'on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.
And it seems to Galen that one should put on the broken limb, to restore, dry things a little hot, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.

Autre maniere d'emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:
Another manner of plaster that is valuable for injury and pain:

pren mugath et chevolz d'omes decopez, ou pennes d'oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.
take musk and chopped human hair, or bird feathers, and marshmallow, and salt equally, and grind them, and make a plaster and tie it.

Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s'est meus li os de son leu;
And then untie it a little after, and take care if the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone moved from its place;

si ne lou deslie par mains jors
if not, do not untie it for many days

Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l'emplaustre maintenant;
And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, hasten, and untie it, and remove the plaster now;

et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;
and take light cloth, and moist sea sponge, and plunge in water, and wash the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is soothed;

puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d'aposteme chaut;
then let the limb rest an hour, then put dry wool on it, soaked in water or rose oil, and tie on for a night, until you are sure of hot swelling;

et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d'emplaustre, et ne l'estraindre mie si fort com devant;
and let the inflammation of the limb rest, and let the pain be removed, then begin again the fine binding, and a little plaster, and do not tighten it as strongly as before;

et subtilie tant qu'il soit sanez.
and refine until it is healed.

Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d'emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.
And if you see that hot swelling and redness and pain and swelling are already removed completely, and you need plaster and binding, then begin again, as you did first equally.

Et s'il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.;
And if none of what we have said comes to the limb, do not untie it except after 3 days or 4 or 5 or 7;

et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c'on voit, tant que li briseure s'aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;
and sometimes leave it 20 days, according to what one sees, until the fracture adheres, and the joining of the flesh approaches above;

adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j'ai dit devant;
then tighten it more than before, and thicken its food, as I have said before;

et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n'est, saiches que norrissemens n'i puet venir;
and if you see the place drying more than is necessary, know that nourishment cannot come there;

arose lou donques d'aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;
water it then with warm tepid water, every time you untie it, and this should be every third day, and loosen the binding a little;

par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:
by this work then the nourishment runs to the limb, and quickly amends what foolish doctors do, who restore the limb crookedly:

c'est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n'i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l'ovrer droitement.
this is bad, and it is fearful work, and I see nothing else but to leave it and to work directly.

des diverses manieres de brisure
Of the various manners of fracture

Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;
There are many manners of fractures, and various shapes, and the causes are distinct;

car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d'espee, et li colz oste tout l'os jusc'a syfac qui est desoz l'os, si com fait haiche ou fust;
for there are fractures that are made by sword strike, and the blow removes all the bone down to the membrane that is under the bone, as does an axe or stick;

et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».
and for this reason this manner of fracture is called "hacking".

Ou li espee cope l'os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;
Or the sword cuts the bone from above without piercing, and this manner of fracture is called "absolute";

et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.
and the wound of these two fractures is large or small.

Et s'il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d'autres semblans.
And if there is a blunt strike, or splitting or from stone blows, or from falling on stone, or from other similar things.

Et s'il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc'a la toile qui est desoz l'os, ou elle est sus l'os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.
And if there is a piercing fracture, which approaches up to the membrane that is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.

Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l'os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;
And if there is a wound hidden in the bone as fine as a hair, and the crack is small, this fracture is called "capillary";

et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l'os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.
and if the wound is made either by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by a similar thing, and causes the piece of bone to enter downward, and the place is hollowed out as coppersmiths do when they strike on cauldrons; so the stone enters inside.

Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d'enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.
And this happens more to those who have moist bones in the head, such as a child's head; and it happens to all these types of fractures that small pieces are separated like splinters; and I will speak about it in its place.

Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l'inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.
And we recognize all types of fractures by the examination of them, and the investigation with probes, and by the corrupted flesh that is on top.

Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l'os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.
The capillary-like appearance is known by this: when the bone is uncovered, and ink is rubbed on it, the fracture appears black.

En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d'entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.
In the treatment of the fracture, be aware of the patient's symptoms, and if you see any bad symptoms, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, tension, fainting, acute fever, the eyes bulging out and reddening, and other similar conditions in various states, it cannot heal without doubt.

Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.
And if you don't see any frightening symptoms, and you hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.

Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c'est en yver, si covient oster l'os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.
And when the wounded person first comes to you, and it's in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the latest, if you can.

Et se c'est en esteit, si te haste d'oster l'os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l'os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.
And if it's in summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, before the membrane under the bone becomes corrupted, and the symptoms we have mentioned occur.

Et se li brisure de l'os vient jusc'a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l'os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l'os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu'il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l'os a oster, et c'est fait selonc .ij. manieres d'ovraige: l'une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c'est li forme:
And if the bone fracture reaches the membrane that covers the brain, it is necessary that you split the cracked part thus: take the head of the wounded patient, and uncover the bone in all the ways you can, and over the shape of the wound as gently as you can, and if bleeding occurs when uncovering the bone, or hot inflammation, help it with what is necessary, which is to fill the place with cloths soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the hot inflammation is calmed, and you are assured of the cessation of bleeding; then begin to remove around the bone, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method is that you cut with a narrow incision in front, and this is the form:

Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.
And then push in another cut larger than the first.

Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.
And the second method is that you have a number of different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of Indian iron; and work lightly, so that you do not injure the head.

Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu'il ne percent outre l'os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l'os; et t'en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l'espés de l'os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c'est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:
And if the bone is strong and hard, it is necessary that you drill around it, before you administer cuts with drills, not so deep that they pierce beyond the skull bone, and there should be a margin or a circle above the point, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you should have several, so that each comes to its place in the thickness of the bone, so that you have drills for all skulls; and this is the form of the three types of drills:

Li qualitez por percier entor l'os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l'os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l'espaice de l'os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l'os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.
The method for drilling around the broken bone is that you put a drill on the bone, and turn with your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced; then put the drill elsewhere a little after, and do this all around, then cut with incisors the space of bone that is between the holes, and do this as subtly as you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you extract the bone with your hand, or with some of the instruments you have such as tongs, pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the meninges.

Et quant tu avras l'os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l'apreteit qui est demoree de l'os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu'il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s'il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d'oignemens que nos avons dit.
And when you have pierced and extracted the bone, it is necessary that you scrape the roughness that remains of the bone with another instrument similar to an incisor, but it should be thinner and more subtle than the other incisor; and if any small bones or scales remain, remove them lightly with one of the instruments; then treat the wound with tents and ointments that we have mentioned.

Et li autre maniere d'ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c'est sa parole.
And the other method of work is that which Galen spoke of, which is safer; and he praised it very strongly, and these are his words.

Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l'os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:
It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture appears most, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will put under the head of this lenticular incisor, of which this is the form:

Et ne trenche mie d'une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l'os; puis fier d'un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l'os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s'elle est aerse a l'os, si l'oste legierement, car on l'oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.
And do not cut on one side, and the sharp part is on two sides, so that the cutting edge is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet above, so that you cut the bone lightly all around, and take good care of the membrane that is underneath; if it is adhered to the bone, remove it gently, for it can be removed without harm, and without fear.

Et se li brisure de l'os ne perce jusc'a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l'ovraige et la figure de la brisure.
And if the bone fracture does not pierce through to the membrane, and the bone is cut only on the surface, and there are small pieces, it is necessary to scrape this roughness, and remove the scales with a subtle razor of which you should have various sizes, to administer in each place the most suitable, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.

Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k'il soit bien.
So scrape first with large razors, and then with more subtle ones, and do not cease doing this until it is well done.

En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c'est chose que n'est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.
In each of the other capillary cuts and subtle fractures, it is necessary that you administer treatment according to its direction; and this is something that is not hidden from one who has put his study into this art.

Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l'estraindre mie fuer que tant k'il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d'encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n'i laissier mie l'oignement, ne n'i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s'asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.
And if the meninges are uncovered, it is necessary that you take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and put it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and put it on the first cloth; and do this as gently as you can, so as not to harm the meninges, then administer another bandage over it, and do not tighten it except just enough to hold the wound only; and leave it thus for a day or two, until the hot inflammation is calmed, then untie it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, and vetch flour, and incense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things; and make powder of these things, and put it on the wound, and always administer cleansing medicines without irritation; and ensure that the wound is always clean, that you do not leave the ointment there, nor let pus gather, for when pus gathers on the membrane of the brain, it corrupts and rots it, and great harm comes to the patient; for when one puts an irritating thing on the meninges, it blackens on top.

Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.
Take care therefore, if any bad symptoms come to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.

Et se noiror n'i vient fuers que por la medicine c'on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d'oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu'il couvient, tant qu'il soit sanez.
And if blackness comes only because of the medicine that has been put on, which has such virtue, it is necessary that you take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and glue a cloth with it, and put it on the meninges; then treat it with the types of treatments that are necessary, until it is healed.

Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k'enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.
Know that sometimes the two upper parts of the nose are broken, or one by itself only, for these are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, it only bends or twists, and then heals.

Et se l'une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.

And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you put your little finger in the hole of the nose, and set that break inside evenly with your index finger, and with the thumb on the outside, until the nose returns to its natural shape; and do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.

Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d'un rait un poc gros.

And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and the finger cannot reach the place, it is necessary that you set it evenly with the head of a somewhat thick stick.

Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.

And if the break is in two parts, do the same, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the hot swelling has subsided, then put linen cloth tents at the head of the nose, if the break is in one part.

Ou tu boutes .i. autre d'autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu'eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.

Or you put another on the other side, if the break is there; and let the tents be so thick that they fill the holes of the nose.

Et dirent aucun restorour c'on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu'elles soient moillies en confection d'aubun d'uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.

And some restorers said that one should moisten the tents in butter, and change them each day. It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that they be moistened in a mixture of egg white and mill powder; then leave the tent until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.

Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d'oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.

And sometimes one puts goose feathers in the nose instead of tents, and there is a soft cloth around it, and it holds the break, and the patient breathes through it; now do whichever you want.

Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.

And if a hot swelling comes to the nose while you are working on it, put a wax plaster or cotton moistened in rose oil, or in a little diachylon.

Et se apostemes chaus n'i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d'encens, confites avec aubun d'uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l'estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s'il n'a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu'il soit sanez.

And if a hot swelling does not come, put a plaster on the outside, of sesame flour, and incense powder, mixed with egg white, then put light tow on top, and do not tie the nose; and if the break of the nose is small, and it is broken into small pieces, extract it with instruments suitable for this, then sew the split, and treat it with things that generate flesh and weld, such as plasters and ointments suitable for this; and if there is no wound inside the nose, treat it with tents, and put lead tubes in it, until it is healed.

de la routure de la mandibule
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n'i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n'est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement. Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l'afaite a l'autre main par defuer, et met igal.

On the break of the jaw
When the jaw is broken below, and there is no wound outside, and the break is only on the outside, and is not broken in two, except for curves inside, it is easily recognized. It is necessary, if the break is on the right side, that you put your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the break is in the left jaw, put your index finger of the right hand, and push the break in gently, and adjust it with the other hand from the outside, and set it evenly.

Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu'il soit igalz.

And if the break of the jaw is separated in two, it is necessary that you administer extension from two sides, until it is even.

Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d'un fil d'or ou d'argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu'il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.

And if movement of the teeth occurs, or breakage, tie them with a gold or silver or silk thread, then put a wax plaster on the broken jaw, and put a double cloth on it; and put on the cloth a large well-made splint, or a piece of even leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it on as best you can, and command the patient to rest, and eat light foods.

Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c'est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d'uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l'emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s'aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k'il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.

And if you see that the shape changes, untie it on the third day, and then put back in place what has changed; and put a plaster on it, of mill powder with egg white or sesame flour, after you have removed the wax plaster; and put light wool on the plaster, and if the plaster sticks, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it is healed; many times it is healed in three weeks.

Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.

And if a hot swelling comes, administer what we have said many times.

Et s'il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l'os en est ostee; si subtilie de l'oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.

And if there is a break and wound together, check if any piece of the bone is removed; if so, carefully remove it with instruments suitable for this.

Et se li plaie est estroite, si l'eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.

And if the wound is narrow, widen it with a lancet according to your need.

Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n'i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s'ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu'il soit sanez.

And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, sew the wound, if it is wide, and put on one of the plasters suitable for this, to generate flesh, until it is healed.

de la forcele
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l'espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.

On the collarbone
The collarbone breaks several times in front, towards the shoulder, and the break is in three ways: either it is broken and separated in two, and there are pieces, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.

Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l'ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n'i ait ne apparance ne chevement.

And the work is when the break is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the arm that feels the broken collarbone; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then set the break evenly with your fingers, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor completion.

Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l'espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.

And if you need to extend more, put under the patient's shoulder a round ball of cloth, or wool, and let it be thick according to your need; and extend and lift the collarbone, and tighten the ball with your hand, so that you set the break evenly, as it should be.

Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu'elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l'espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l'espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.

And if you cannot draw the head of the collarbone to the outside, because it comes deep, it is necessary that the patient lie on his back on his nape, and put a medium pillow under the shoulder, and the assistant pushes the shoulder down, until the collarbone bone is raised.

Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l'un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:
et semble une cuiller, et n'est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l'os et la possance de l'uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d'aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.

And then straighten the break with your fingers, and if you find it broken, it is necessary that you cut above; and draw out the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join due to some protrusion, cut it with one of the incisors that you have; but put this instrument under the collarbone, to protect the pleura:
and it looks like a spoon, and is not hollow, and should be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and it has two heads, as you see, and one is wide, and the other narrow, as is the break of the wound that you made when you drew out the bones; and when you are assured of hot swelling, sew the wound, and if the break is small, or you fear hot swelling, fill the wound with cloths and tents, according to its quantity.

Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.

And if a hot swelling comes, moisten a cloth in rose oil and in vinegar and in wine, and put it on.

Li estrignement de l'os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l'os l'enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d'aubun d'uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l'assele, se tu en as mestier;
The treatment of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cuts, is that you put on the bone a plaster made of mill powder and egg white, and put light tow on top, and put a sphere under the armpit, if you need it;

puis pren une tres grant bende d'une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l'emplaustre;
then take a very large bandage a palm wide, then put a double cloth over the tow, and the plaster;

puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l'envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;
then take a thin splint three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the ends of the bandage are hanging;

et met l'estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l'asselle sainne, et desoz l'asselle malaide;
and put the splint on the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the healthy armpit, and under the injured armpit;

et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l'os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;
and bring it back from each side, and when you see that the binding holds the fracture properly, and you clearly see that the splint does not move above the broken bone, check it each day, and when the binding loosens, tighten it;

et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l'assele, por lever l'ajutoire en haut;
and make the patient lie on his back, and put a small pillow under his armpit when he sleeps, to raise the humerus up;

si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l'aligement de l'espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n'i vient, jusc'a .xx. jors;
this will ease the fracture of the collarbone by lifting the shoulder, or you tie his arm to his neck, and do not untie it unless bad accidents occur, for up to 20 days;

puis rencomence l'emplaustre, se tu vois qu'il en ait mestier, et l'estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu'il soit restorez;
then restart the plaster, if you see that it is needed, and tighten it and leave it like that, until it is healed;

et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.
and it is healed at most in 28 days, and in less for some men.

de la brisure de l'espaule
On the fracture of the shoulder

Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;
It rarely happens that the shoulder breaks in the wide place or in the middle, and one only knows it by touching;

si l'apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;
so prepare it according to the shape of the fracture, and bring it back to its natural form, in all the ways that you can;

puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d'uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double;
then put on the place mill powder with egg white, and light tow, and put on top a double cloth;

puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l'espaule, et se desoz l'estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l'espaule, si emple celle cheveure d'estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;
then put on top a wide and thin splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if under the splint there is a hollow in any place of the shoulder, fill that hollow with linen tow, so that the splint sits evenly;

et puis l'estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;
and then tighten it firmly with a large bandage, so that the splint does not move from its place, and check the binding each day;

et toutes les fois k'il amolist, si l'estraint, et met igal l'estele s'elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;
and every time it loosens, tighten it, and put the splint back in place if it is out of its place, and make the patient lie on his side;

et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n'est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.
and the shoulder is healed in 20 days or in 25, And when this number is completed, untie it, and be sure, because this is not a bone that easily goes out of place.

Et se une piece de l'os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l'oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d'apaisier aposteme chaut.
And if a piece of the bone sticks out, and points under the skin, then cut above it, and remove it, and do what we have said in the fracture of the collarbone to calm a hot abscess.

de la brisure dou pis
On the fracture of the chest

Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.
The chest is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it often breaks on the outside.

Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d'alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l'os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.
And when it is broken in the middle, it declines downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of breath, and coughs, and perhaps vomits blood, and the hollow in the broken bone appears, and one feels it well.

Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l'os soit si com il covient;
And the restoration is that the patient lies supine on his back, and you put a cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and bring together the ribs of the two sides with your hands, and refine putting it even in all the ways that you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be;

puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l'estele subtil de salz, ou d'autre fust legier, et l'envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l'os brisiet, si qu'elle ne se mueve;
then put on plasters and tow above the thin splint of willow, or other light wood, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it on the broken bone, so that it does not move;

et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l'estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s'elle ramolist, si l'estraint;
and turn the binding around to the back, and tighten it properly, and check the binding every hour, and if it loosens, tighten it;

et s'il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l'emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;
and if it needs to be untied, because of corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and untie it, and scrape off the plaster, and address what has come in terms of treatments;

puis ramoinne l'emplaustre, et l'estraint tant qu'il soit sanez.
then bring back the plaster, and tighten it until it is healed.

de la brisure des costes
On the fracture of the ribs

Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu'eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l'inquisition as dois.
Know that the fracture of the ribs only occurs in thick places after the back, and at the inner end, and they only bend out because they are cartilaginous; and one feels it well when examining with the fingers.

Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l'emplaustre, et l'estraint d'une estele, se tu en as mestier.
And the restoration is that you even out the fracture, as it should be. And then put the plaster, and tighten it with a splint, if you need it.

Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c'est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.
And if the fracture of the ribs is declining inwards, the patient feels very great pain, and stabbing, as if from pleurisy, because the bone pricks the membrane; and breathes with difficulty, and coughs and vomits a great quantity of blood, and it is of grave health, and the ancients have put great ingenuity into it.

Et si a de ces qui dient qu'il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.
And there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that inflate the belly, to push the fracture outwards.

Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n'i viegne, s'il n'i est venus.
We do not do this, lest hot abscesses come, if they have not already come.

Et s'il i est venus, si le saine.
And if it has come, then bleed it.

Et dirent aucun d'ous c'on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c'est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n'atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.
And some of them said that one puts cupping glasses on the place, to suck strongly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cupping glass might attract superfluities to the place due to the disposition of weakness.

Et dirent aucun d'ous c'on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.
And some of them said that one should cover the place with wool moistened in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to even out the binding around, then it should be treated with the treatment for pleurisy, with food and medicine.

Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu'il ne puet soffrir par l'os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l'os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s'elle est grans, et le curez d'emplaustres, tant qu'il soit sanez.
And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear due to the bone pricking the membrane, and there is doubt for the patient, it is necessary to cut above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put an instrument underneath to protect the peritoneum; and then one should cut the bone, and draw it out gently, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters, until it is healed.

Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu'il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu'il soit sanez.
And if hot abscesses come, put cloths moistened in rose oil on it, and put them on the place; and meanwhile treat the place with what is necessary for an abscess, and let him lie supine on the side where he should, until he is healed.

de la brisure dou col
On the fracture of the neck

Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k'il ploie; et ausi a l'espinee dou dos.
Sometimes fracture comes to the bones of the neck, and it rarely happens that it bends; and also to the spine of the back.

Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s'il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d'une aguille, si ne lou sent.
And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, observe if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and he cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it.

Saiches qu'il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s'il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l'os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s'on i met cure.
Know that he is mortal in many dispositions, and if he moves them and feels well when they are squeezed and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and that the patient will be cured, if care is given.

Et se semblans chose vient a l'espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s'il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l'a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.
And if a similar thing comes to the spine of the back, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, observe if the feet are softened, and if the accidents that are in the hands are there, and if on the back there is flatulence and excretion without will; and when he has been laid on his belly, if excretion comes without will.

Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu'il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.
And when he is laid on his back and he wants to defecate, he cannot. Know that he is mortal: so do not labor in his cure.

Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.
And if these accidents do not come to him, then the thing is lighter.

Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s'il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l'espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d'uef, tant qu'il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d'un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k'il soit sanez.
And the cure is that you look if there is a hot abscess, then put on the spine rose oil or oil of egg yolk, until it is calmed; then put on one of the comforting and drying plasters, and tie it with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and do not let him sleep on the part where he feels the pain, until he is healed.

Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l'os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s'elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d'oignement enjanrant char, tant qu'il soit sanez;
And if any bone separates, it is necessary to cut above the skin; and remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then treat it with ointment generating flesh, until it is healed;

et se li chiés de l'os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l'autre main a ton pooir, puis met l'emplaustre et l'estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l'estraint, et s'il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l'oste, et cure la plaie tant qu'elle soit sanee.
and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the tail", push your left hand's thumb, and put it even with the other hand to your ability, then put the plaster and the splint on top, if you need it; then tighten it, and if there is a separated bone, cut above it, and remove it, and treat the wound until it is healed.

de la brisure de l'os de la hainche
On the fracture of the hip bone

Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s'il avient, si n'avient fuer c'un poc d'amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.
It rarely happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it does happen, it only occurs with a slight reduction at the head; and it splits lengthwise, and bends inward, and causes pain to the patient at the site, and a stabbing sensation, and swelling where it is broken.

Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu'ele soit a figure natureil.
And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it until you are over the fracture; and know what the fracture is and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the head, then set that fracture evenly, until it is in its natural shape.

Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.
And if the fracture is lengthwise, or it bends inward, then make the patient lie on their stomach, until the restoration of that fracture is prepared for you.

Et quant tu l'avras mise igal, si met sus l'emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu'ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.
And when you have set it evenly, then put a plaster on it, then put a splint of wood or leather on it, and tighten the fracture, so that it does not move; and fill the place under the ribs, until the binding is even.

Et comande au malaide k'il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.
And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back.

Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n'i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l'estraint si com il covient, s'il n'i a nul mavais accident; et c'est li maniere.
And if a hot abscess comes, do not touch it until the hot abscess has calmed down, and put on what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and tighten it as is appropriate, if there is no bad accident; and this is the method.

de la brisure de l'ajutoire
On the fracture of the humerus

Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l'espaule, et s'il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l'une des .ij. manieres: dont l'une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:
The humerus is that which is between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of two methods: of which one is that you take a flat piece of wood of medium thickness, according to this shape:

Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu'il viegne a l'aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l'estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.
And tie two bonds to the two ends, and hang them high, and seat the patient on a chair; then throw their broken arm over the wood, until it comes to the armpit, and have a curve of wood in the middle, then hang some heavy thing or have the assistant extend it downward; then let the physician set the fracture evenly with his hands together, until the fracture returns as it should.

Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.
And the other method is that one lays the patient on their back, and ties their hand to their neck, then commands two assistants that one holds what is above the fracture with their hands, and the other holds below with a bond, and each extends to their part.

Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.
And if you want the extraction to be stronger, then tighten a bond below the fracture, and above the fracture, and have each of the assistants extend to their part.
