Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l'espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l'assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l'estraint, se apostemes chaus n'i vient.
And if the fracture is close to the head of the shoulder, it is necessary that you put a medium bond under the armpit, and another towards the elbow, below the fracture; and also if the fracture is towards the elbow, it is necessary to put a bond lightly, without effort, until the fracture is even on the site, and on the elbow; then set the fracture evenly, as is appropriate, and tighten it, if a hot abscess does not come.

Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l'estraindre mie jusc'a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l'estraint, et li maniere de l'estraindre si est que tu mettes l'emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l'ajutoire, et met ta main sus l'espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l'ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d'esteles, s'aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n'est muez.
And if a hot abscess comes, do not tighten it until seven days, and put wool soaked in vinegar and rose oil on it, until the hot abscess has calmed down; then tighten it, and the method of tightening is that you put the plaster on the fracture, then assemble the arm on the humerus, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the cloth, and tighten on the humerus, and on the arm, so that the arm is in place of splints, if nothing prevents you from doing so, or if the bone has not moved.

Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d'esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d'espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu'elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j'ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.
And if you fear that the bone might move, then use splints, and put on the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint a finger's space, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture by three fingers on each side; then tighten on the splints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on fractures, stronger and less in lengthening.

Et se tu vois l'assise des esteles, et l'estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l'oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l'aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc'a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n'i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k'il est trop estrois. Si l'adrece, si com nos avons dit.
And if you see the placement of the splints, and the tightening, as we have said, at the time when you restore the broken limb, and you fear a hot abscess, then leave it untied until the seventh day, as we have said; then check the binding every three days, so that itching or swelling does not come to the site, or that nourishment cannot come to the limb because it is too tight. Then adjust it, as we have said.

Et se nulz telz accidens n'i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l'ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l'adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.
And if no such accidents come, do not untie it except after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back, and have their hands on their stomach; and put under the humerus a cushion evenly filled with wool, and check every hour of the day or night, that the shape of the broken limb does not move, or that the binding is not loosened; then adjust it by the virtue of medicine, and give them the food that we have put before, in such a manner that the food is at first subtle; and when it begins to heal, let it be thick.

Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d'oignemens por le leu adrecier.
And it is customary that the humerus and the leg should be healed in 40 days completely; and then one should untie it and administer baths and ointment medicines to straighten the site.

Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.
And if the tightening is ugly and swollen, then delay untying it for 50 days or 2 months.

de la brisure du bras
On the breaking of the arm

Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.
The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "fosciles", of which one is small and follows the thumb; and the other is large and is below, towards the little finger; by chance the large foscile breaks alone, or the small one, and by chance both together.

Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.
When the small foscile is broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing; and when the large one is broken, the healing is difficult, and more grievous than when they are both broken together.

Se c'est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.
If it is the small foscile that is broken alone, it should be extended slightly and gently, and set evenly.

Et se c'est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l'estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus.
And if it is the large foscile, it should be tightened more strongly; and extend it on a cushion, and hold the thumb of the hand higher than the others, and the little finger lower than the other fingers, and let the patient be crossed over himself, and a cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient suffers no labor; then let the minister extend his arm to the lower part of his hand, or to a band, and another minister to another above.

Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.
And then let the physician set it evenly, according to its best form.

Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s'il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l'oste, si com nos avons dit devant.
And if there are pieces in the break, put each in its place, and if there is any separate piece that pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut above and remove it, as we have said before.

Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.
And if there is a wound with the break, I have spoken of it in a separate chapter; so take care.

Et se en l'encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d'oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.
And if at the beginning of the restoration hot swellings occur, glue a cloth of cerote made of rose oil and white wax, which should be neither too hard nor too soft; and tie a cloth over it subtly, until the hot swellings are calmed.

Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l'emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d'uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l'un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j'ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.
And then remove the cerote, and put the plaster of mill powder with egg white, then put the splints, and let the splint of the break be always stronger, and a little wider than the others; and know that there should be six splints on the arm in several arrangements: whether the break is in one of the bones or in two; and tighten more on the break than elsewhere, and always less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths that are on the break be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the thread, with which it is tightened, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.

Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.
And examine the limb and the bandage after a few days.

Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d'aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.
And if any bad accidents come to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, you should sprinkle the limb with hot water, until that itching is calmed; and let the limb rest, not tightly.

Et puis rencomence l'estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l'adresce.
And then begin the tightening again, and if the bandage is softened and the bones separated, and similar things, then straighten it.

Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu'il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l'amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l'estraint.
And take care if the nourishment cannot come to the limb, because it is too tight, so you should soften it a little, and leave it thus for a few days, until the nourishment flows there, and then tighten it.

Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc'a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.
And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, do not untie it until twenty days or thereabouts, then hang his hands on his neck, and let his neck be even, and guard against movement and throwing, and sleep on his back; and know that this break is restored in thirty days or in thirty-five, and by chance in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.

de la brisure de la main
On the breaking of the hand

Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n'i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.
Know that on the back of the hand and at the knuckles of the fingers, few breaks occur, and nothing comes but bending many times.

Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu'il soient bien joint; et met l'emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n'i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.
And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, the patient should sit crossed, and sit straight in front of him evenly; then put his hand on the extended cloth, and let the minister extend the broken bones, and let the physician set them evenly, until they are well joined; and put the plaster and the tow, if swellings do not come, then put a splint according to the quantity of the place; and let it be wrapped in a linen cloth.

Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu'il l'estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l'estrain d'un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l'estraint, si com il covient.
And if the break is on the inside around the belly of the palm, make a sphere of cloths, and command the patient to tighten it to his broken palm; and then tighten it with a long cloth, and let the splint be of soft leather as large as the palm of the hand, and tighten it, as it should be.

Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.
And if the break is on the outside, you should put a splint on top, and another below in the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it all around the hand, and stop the bandage between the fingers.

Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c'est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l'estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l'indice ou l'un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d'aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j'ai dit.
And if the break comes to any of the knuckles of the fingers, if it is the thumb, set it evenly, as it should be; and tighten it with the palm, and if you want, put a small straight splint to raise the break, and do not move it; and if the break is in the other fingers, such as in the index or one of the others, set it evenly, and tie it with the healthy finger that is next to it; or tie them all together, which is better, or put a splint on it, as on the thumb; and take care in the restoration and in the disposition of hot swelling, and help what comes there, as I have said.

de la cuixe brisie
Of the broken thigh

Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c'on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.
The thigh bone is often broken, and one can see it well when it turns front and back; and the restoration is that one ties a bandage above the break, and another below.

Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c'est quant li brisure est emmi l'os.
And the patient lies on his face, then each attendant extends his bandage to his part equally; and this is when the break is in the middle of the bone.

Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.
And if the break is close to the root of the thigh, let one of the bandages be towards the groin, and the other bandage below the break.

Et ausi s'elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l'os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu'il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l'emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n'i vient.
And also if it is close to the knee, then let the bandage be next to the knee, and let the extension be downward; then the physician puts the bone equal with his two hands, until it is according to its natural shape, and then puts the plaster, and ties it, if no hot swelling comes.

Et s'il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.
And if there is a hot swelling, let it calm down then return to your work and your treatment; the binding is done in this manner.

Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l'os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l'estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l'estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l'estraint, si qu'il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k'il n'i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n'autre semblant.
It is necessary that you wrap over the break a hard bandage doubled in two or three, and the excess remains, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the buttock, and push a long thread between the thigh and the leg, next to the knee below, and let the ends of the thread come to the top; then turn the bandage over the leg and over the thigh, then put splints on the break, and put a splint on the leg bone; then fill the empty space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to make the tightening even, then begin to tie strongly three or four turns over the break; and the further you go from the break, the less you tighten; then attend to the two ends of the thread that you have pushed between the leg and the thigh, and tie three splints that are above, then go back down to the end of the thread, until you come next to the foot; and tighten it, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, as long as no swelling or inflammation or other symptom comes.

Et s'il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l'os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s'om puet; et s'on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k'il soit sanez.
And if it happens, untie it, and address what comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, it is necessary to remove them, if one can; and if one cannot, it is necessary to split the place, and draw them out; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.

Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c'on i met esteles, si com en l'ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.
And sometimes the thigh is broken so that one puts splints, as in the shoulder and arm; however, in the restoration thus made, the patient does not limp.

Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.
And know that the thigh is restored in 50 days, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of complexions.

de la ruelle dou genoil
Of the kneecap

Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.
Know that in the kneecap, breakage happens rarely, but it bends many times.

Et s'elle brise, si n'est mais c'une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.
And if it breaks, it is but a crack, or a hole, and it happens with all wounds, and without wounds, and one feels it well.

Et li restauration si est c'on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu'il soit assemblez mues c'on puet; puis met l'emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l'estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k'il li covient, tant qu'il soit sanez.
And the restoration is that one puts equal what is round to his fingers, until it is assembled as much as one can; then put the plaster, and put a round splint, if you need it, and tighten it as it is necessary, then look at all the dispositions that we have said in other breaks, such as hot swelling and other symptoms; so put to each accident what is necessary for it, until it is healed.

de la brisure de la jambe
Of the break of the leg

Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.
Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is rightly called "mustelz" (tibia), and the other is called "foscile" (fibula); and the same break happens as it does in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is just like that of the arm equally, and the procedure is all one.

Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.
And if the two bones are broken together, the leg turns in all directions.

Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.
And if the thin bone is broken, it turns forward.

Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.
And if the thick bone is broken, one feels great pain, and one sees it well; and it turns downward.

Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l'alige selonc ta vertu.
Then administer extension, and put it equal, and tie the splints equally; but nevertheless, it is necessary if the break is ugly, and there are several pieces, that the extension be lesser and lighter; and ease it according to your strength.

Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d'une part et d'autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s'est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s'il i a aposteme chaut n'autre accident; si le cure tant qu'il soit sanez.
And when you have completed all your work, take two hollowed wooden bands that encompass the leg on one side and the other, and are the length of the leg from the knee to below; then wrap in two places a bandage above and below, and tie it in the middle also, and with this binding the leg will not be able to decline to the right or left, and thus it is good; and some administer a cradle the length of the leg, and it is of wood, and one puts the leg in it to guard against movement, and this is properly done in the break where there is a wound; and move the leg each day, to see if there is a hot swelling or other accident; treat it until it is healed.

de la brisure des os dou piet
Of the break of the bones of the foot

A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n'i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.
To the ankle comes no break, but to the bones of the foot comes sometimes a break and to the toes rarely, and there happens nothing but bruising in several dispositions.

Et s'il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l'un l'autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s'il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k'il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l'emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l'estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.
And if it happens that the bones of the foot break, and you see these bones overlapping one another, have the patient put his foot on the ground, as if he wanted to walk, and then put now your foot on his, there where the bones are raised, then press it until they return to their places; then put the plaster and tow on top, and put under the sole of the foot a small board with two flat ends, then tighten it to the foot suitably, after you have wrapped cloths around, and other things that you need.

Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.
And when three or four days have passed, untie the binding, for you will find the bones equal, whether broken or dislocated.

Et s'il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j'ai dit, et l'estrain avenanment; et s'il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu'il le teigne bien.
And if there are any of the toes broken, restore them, as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then put on the broken toe a splint according to the length of the toe, and let it be a little wider, then put under the foot that board that I have mentioned, and tighten it suitably; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, put on each toe a splint according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and tighten the board under the foot; and let it be standing on the end of the board outside the sole of the foot, so that it holds it well.

Et covient que tu n'oblier mie les autres choses que j'ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.
And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said for other breaks, of which we have spoken; and attend to each accident as is necessary.

de la brisure de l'os dou poignil
On the fracture of the wrist bone

Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l'encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;
When the bone of a woman's genitals is broken, make her sit with legs spread, then lean her back, and have her held from behind;

puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto;
then fill the patient's genital area with cotton, and insert an amount as large as a 'sto' (possibly a unit of measurement);

puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu'il vient a l'entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;
then push the woman, and raise her back little by little, and then the cotton will come out, until it reaches the entrance of the genitals, and the bone will return with the 'sto';

et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure,
and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do this for seven days or thereabouts: thus the fracture will be restored,

et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;
and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, and tie a reed to its opening, and insert the entire bladder into the genitals;

puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure;
then blow strongly into the reed, until the bladder is inflated inside: thus the fracture in the genitals will return;

puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu'il soit sanez.
then fill it with cotton, and leave it thus for some days, until it is healed.

Et quant li os dou poignil de l'ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l'os de la hainche;
And when the wrist bone of a man is broken, or of a woman, restore it as we have said for the hip bone;

et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.
and these nearby fractures are not hidden from one who applies their study and practice to it, and understands my book.

Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.
For the fracture indicates in many cases the right way of restoration: understand it then.

En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d'oie et i boute la verge;
For the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's throat and insert the penis into it;

puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.
then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for three days or thereabouts, and it will be healed quickly.

de brisure avec plaie
On fracture with wound

Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s'elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l'ajutoire ou semblant, qu'il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.
It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the thigh bone or the humerus or similar, that he be bled immediately, as the bloodlettings we have mentioned testify.

// Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n'as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n'i vient.
And if the wound heals, staunch it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then begin again to restore the fracture in that same hour, or that day, if no hot swelling comes.

Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc'a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n'i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.
And if a hot swelling comes, leave the restoration until the ninth day, until the swelling has subsided, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause bad complications.

Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.
And if the broken bone is visible on the exposed flesh, it is necessary that you set it gently with your hands, with little extension.

Et se li extensions ne t'est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;
And if the extension is not prepared to be set equally with your hands, bring it back with this iron instrument, which is seven or eight fingers long, and its width is according to the size of the wound;

et por ceu est mestier au mire qu'il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu'il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;
and for this reason it is necessary for the physician to take three or four, according to what he needs in each treatment of fracture;

et soit rons et un poc gros, k'il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:
and let it be round and a bit thick, so that it does not bend under compression on the limb during your work, and let it be sharp in front, and thick from the middle forward, like this:

Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l'os apparent;
And it is called a "lever", for which it is necessary that the curved end be placed on the head of the visible bone;

et le boute a une fois, tant k'il reviegne, et soit igalz l'un encontre l'autre.
and push it at once, until it returns, and let them be equal one against the other.

Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l'os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l'os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.
And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot well grasp the bone, it is necessary that you cut the head of the bone, until the instrument has power over it.

Et se tu ne pues ramener l'os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d'un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;
And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, cut it with a suitable instrument for this, either an incision tool or a saw, to the best of your ability;

puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l'os d'aspreteit et de menues escorces.
then scrape what remains of roughness and small fragments on the bone.

Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu'il n'est mie en son leu natureil.
And when the bone is brought back, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.

Si fai tant qu'il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c'est en esteit;
So do what is necessary for it to be in its place, then moisten a cloth in black astringent wine, especially if it is in summer;

et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu'il n'i faice venir porriture et corruption;
and do not put on the wound wax or other thing that has oil, lest it cause rot and corruption;

puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l'os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie,
then apply splints when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering all around, according to the size of the wound,

et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;
and take good care that the wound is not tightened with the fracture;

et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;
and many times foolish physicians have done this, and have caused death or sometimes corrosion to come upon the patient;

et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.
and let the tightening be softer and gentler than for other fractures.

Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n'i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n'i covient mie mettre sus esteles;
And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that bad complications may come, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, it is not necessary to put splints on it;

mais envoloupe entor, en leu d'esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.
but wrap around, instead of splints, hard cloths, and tie them.

Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.
And when you see after a day or two that pus is generated in the wound, remove what you have put on with all the wine, and apply a healing ointment for wounds, such as tetrapharmacon ointment and similar ones.

Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu'il soit soudez et sanez.
And it is necessary that you unbind the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is joined and healed.

Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.
And it is necessary that the limb be prepared in such a manner that the pus runs down easily.

Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k'il i a petites pieces d'os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.
And if many days pass, and it cannot join but still produces pus, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which it is necessary that you probe the wound with a tent, and remove all these separated pieces that cause that pain.

Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu'il dist en son chapistre ci devant.
And if a fistula comes to the place, or another manner of corruption, it is necessary that you treat it, according to what is said in its chapter above.

Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l'ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors,
And when the bone is broken, and appears on the limb, such as the thigh bone or the humerus, and other similar large bones, do not pull it, for many times death comes from it,

mais le laisse tant qu'il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.
but leave it until it rots; by chance it will fall off by itself after 20 or 30 days, then treat the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.

de brisure avec plaie
On fracture with wound

Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s'elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l'ajutoire ou semblant, qu'il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.
It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the thigh bone or the humerus or similar, that he be bled immediately, as the bloodlettings we have mentioned testify.

// Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n'as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n'i vient.
And if the wound heals, staunch it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then begin again to restore the fracture in that same hour, or that day, if no hot swelling comes.

Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc'a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n'i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.
And if a hot swelling comes, leave the restoration until the ninth day, until the swelling has subsided, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause bad complications.

Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.
And if the broken bone is visible on the exposed flesh, it is necessary that you set it gently with your hands, with little extension.

Et se li extensions ne t'est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;
And if the extension is not prepared to be set equally with your hands, bring it back with this iron instrument, which is seven or eight fingers long, and its width is according to the size of the wound;

et por ceu est mestier au mire qu'il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu'il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;
and for this reason it is necessary for the physician to take three or four, according to what he needs in each treatment of fracture;

et soit rons et un poc gros, k'il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:
and let it be round and a bit thick, so that it does not bend under compression on the limb during your work, and let it be sharp in front, and thick from the middle forward, like this:

Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l'os apparent;
And it is called a "lever", for which it is necessary that the curved end be placed on the head of the visible bone;

et le boute a une fois, tant k'il reviegne, et soit igalz l'un encontre l'autre.
and push it at once, until it returns, and let them be equal one against the other.

Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l'os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l'os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.
And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot well grasp the bone, it is necessary that you cut the head of the bone, until the instrument has power over it.

Et se tu ne pues ramener l'os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d'un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;
And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, cut it with a suitable instrument for this, either an incision tool or a saw, to the best of your ability;

puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l'os d'aspreteit et de menues escorces.
then scrape what remains of roughness and small fragments on the bone.

Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu'il n'est mie en son leu natureil.
And when the bone is brought back, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.

Si fai tant qu'il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c'est en esteit;
So do what is necessary for it to be in its place, then moisten a cloth in black astringent wine, especially if it is in summer;

et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu'il n'i faice venir porriture et corruption;
and do not put on the wound wax or other thing that has oil, lest it cause rot and corruption;

puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l'os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie,
then apply splints when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering all around, according to the size of the wound,

et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;
and take good care that the wound is not tightened with the fracture;

et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;
and many times foolish physicians have done this, and have caused death or sometimes corrosion to come upon the patient;

et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.
and let the tightening be softer and gentler than for other fractures.

Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n'i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n'i covient mie mettre sus esteles;
And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that bad complications may come, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, it is not necessary to put splints on it;

mais envoloupe entor, en leu d'esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.
but wrap around, instead of splints, hard cloths, and tie them.

Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.
And when you see after a day or two that pus is generated in the wound, remove what you have put on with all the wine, and apply a healing ointment for wounds, such as tetrapharmacon ointment and similar ones.

Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu'il soit soudez et sanez.
And it is necessary that you unbind the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is joined and healed.

Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.
And it is necessary that the limb be prepared in such a manner that the pus runs down easily.

Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k'il i a petites pieces d'os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.
And if many days pass, and it cannot join but still produces pus, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which it is necessary that you probe the wound with a tent, and remove all these separated pieces that cause that pain.

Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu'il dist en son chapistre ci devant.
And if a fistula comes to the place, or another manner of corruption, it is necessary that you treat it, according to what is said in its chapter above.

Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l'ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors,
And when the bone is broken, and appears on the limb, such as the thigh bone or the humerus, and other similar large bones, do not pull it, for many times death comes from it,

mais le laisse tant qu'il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.
but leave it until it rots; by chance it will fall off by itself after 20 or 30 days, then treat the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.

des brus qui vienent sor la sodure
On the knots that come on the joint

Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c'est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.
They often come after the healing of the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and it is an ugly thing to see the shape of the limb; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.

Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres,
Take care then if the knot is fresh: administer astringent medicines to it, such as aloe, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others,

ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d'uef ou avec aisil;
so that you take some of these things, or all together, and mix them with astringent wine or with egg white or with vinegar;

et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l'estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;
and put them on the knot in tow, and tighten it well, and do not unbind it for many days;

et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;
and then unbind it, and begin another, until the nodule is removed;

ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu'il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;
or you tighten a well-made piece of lead over it; for the property of lead is that it removes all swellings from the limbs;

et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l'oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;
and if the nodule has already turned into a hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, cut it above, and split the apparent superfluity;

ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu'ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu'ele soit sanee.
or you scrape it with a razor, until it is removed, and treat it until it is healed.

dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison
On the limb that is weak after healing

Quant li brisure de l'os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:
When the bone fracture is restored, and afterwards the limb remains weak and thin, it happens for many reasons:

de coi l'une est por ceu qu'il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;
of which one is because it was bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been;

ou por ceu qu'il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;
or because there were too many bandages, and nourishment could not come to the limb;

ou por multitude d'arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;
or because of excessive moistening; or because of too much movement, not at the right time;

ou por ceu qu'il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.
or because there is little blood in the body, so it is weak.

Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;
And the treatment is that you make the patient eat, and make the body tender, until the blood is multiplied in him;

et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;
and administer a bath to him, and give him joy and happiness;

puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l'arose sovent d'aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;
then put pitch on the limb, so that the pitch attracts great nourishment to it, and moisten it often with warm water, until the nourishment runs to the limb;

et reviegne a sa figure natureil.
and it returns to its natural shape.
